The Threefold Classification of Messengers' Attributes
Sanusi classifies the attributes of messengers into three categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational categories of attributes that apply to messengers: necessary, impossible, and permissible, and the specific attributes in each category.

Core Idea
Prophets must be truthful, trustworthy, and deliver the message; the opposite is impossible; human imperfections are permissible.

Sanusi now applies the same threefold classification that he used for Allah to the prophets. Just as we must affirm certain attributes for Allah, we must also affirm specific qualities for His messengers. This passage enumerates what is necessary, impossible, and permissible for them, establishing the doctrinal baseline for prophethood.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice how Sanusi uses the same three categories (wajib, mustahil, ja'iz) that he used for Allah's attributes.
2
Identify the three categories
The passage presents three distinct groups: necessary attributes, impossible attributes, and permissible attributes. List each category and its contents.
3
Understand the impossible attributes
Note that the impossible attributes are direct opposites of the necessary ones. Also note that treachery includes both forbidden and disliked acts, showing the high standard of prophetic protection.
This guards against the misconception that prophets could commit minor sins.
4
Reflect on the permissible attributes
The permissible category includes human experiences like illness that do not lower their rank. Consider why such attributes are allowed and what they imply about the prophets' humanity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الرُّسُلُ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : فَيَجِبُ فِي حَقِّهِمُ : الصِّدْقُ ، وَالأَمَانَةٌ ، وَتَبْلِيغُ مَا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ (۱) لِلْخَلْقِ وَيَسْتَحِيلُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : أَزْدَادُ هَذِهِ الصَّفَاتِ ; وَهِيَ : الْكَذِبُ ، وَالْخِيَانَةُ بِفِعْل شَيْءٍ مِمَّا نُهِيَ عَنْهُ نَهْيَ تَحْرِيمٍ أَوْ كَرَاهَةٍ ، وَكِتْمَانُ (۲) شَيْءٍ مِمَّا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ لِلْخَلْقِ . وَيَجُوزُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : مَا هُوَ مِنَ الأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ الَّتِي لا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ فِي مَرَاتِبِهِمُ الْعَلِيَّةِ ; كَالْمَرَضِ وَنَحْوِهِ (۱) في ( أ ، ب ، ج ) : ( بإبلاغه ) ، والمثبت من نسخ الشرح . (۲) في ( ج ) : ( أو كتمان ) .
As for the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them: the necessary [attributes] in their right are: truthfulness, trustworthiness, and delivering what they were commanded to deliver (1) to the creation. And the impossible in their right, peace and blessings be upon them, are the opposites of these attributes: lying, treachery by doing something from which they were forbidden by a prohibition of prohibition or dislike, and concealing (2) something from what they were commanded to deliver to the creation. And permissible in their right, peace and blessings be upon them, is that which is from human accidents that do not lead to a deficiency in their high ranks, like illness and the like. (1) In copies A, B, C: 'to inform him', and the confirmed is from the versions of the commentary. (2) In copy C: 'or concealing'.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage classifies the attributes of messengers into three categories: wajib (necessary), mustahil (impossible), and ja'iz (permissible). Necessary: truthfulness, trustworthiness, and delivering the message. Impossible: lying, treachery (by committing forbidden or disliked acts), and concealing any part of the message. Permissible: human accidents that do not lower their high status, such as illness. The footnotes note textual variants in the phrase 'تبليغه' and the conjunction in 'كتمان'.

Key Terms

صدق
أمانة
تبليغ
كذب
خيانة

أعراض بشرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets can commit sins, including minor sins or acts of dislike.
Correction: This passage shows that even disliked acts (makruh) are impossible for prophets, as they fall under 'treachery' (khiyana). Prophets are protected from all forms of disobedience.

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a necessary attribute of messengers?
A) Truthfulness
B) Trustworthiness
C) Delivering the message
D) Being free from illness

Key Takeaway
Prophets are protected from lying, treachery, and concealing the message, but may experience human ailments like illness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Prophet ﷺ was absolutely truthful and trustworthy. In what area of your life do you struggle most with truthfulness or trustworthiness? What one honest action can you commit to this week to align yourself with this prophetic attribute?
?
Prophets are protected from even disliked acts. Think of a 'small' sin you have come to tolerate. How can you begin to treat it with the same seriousness as a major sin, knowing that the prophets avoided even what is disliked?
?
The messengers delivered every part of the revelation without concealment. Are there aspects of Islam you have been hesitant to fully embrace or share? What would it take for you to commit to complete honesty in living and conveying the truth, as the prophets did?

Proof of the Necessity of Truthfulness for Messengers
Sanusi proves messengers must be truthful using divine endorsement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for why prophets must be truthful, based on divine endorsement through miracles.

Core Idea
If a prophet could lie, God would be endorsing a lie—impossible.

This lesson presents a short but powerful rational argument from Imam Sanusi. It shows why lying is impossible for prophets by linking their truthfulness to God's own trustworthiness. The proof uses the concept of miracles as divine confirmation.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once carefully, then read the literal translation. Notice the concise logical structure.
2
Understand the logical structure
Identify the conditional premise: if prophets were not truthful, then lying would be attributed to God. Understand why miracles are equivalent to God saying 'My servant is truthful'.
3
Grasp the conclusion
The conclusion is that prophets must be truthful because otherwise God would be endorsing a falsehood, which is impossible for God.
This is a rational necessity, not just a scriptural claim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : فَلأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ لَمْ يَصْدُقُوا لَلَوْمَ الْكَذِبُ فِي خَبَرِهِ تَعَالَى ; لِتَصْدِيقِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُمْ بِالْمُعْجِزَاتِ النَّازِلَةِ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى : صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي
As for the proof of the necessity of their truthfulness, peace and blessings be upon them: it is that if they were not truthful, then lying would be implied in the report of God, Exalted, because of God's affirming them with the miracles which serve as His statement: 'My servant is truthful in all that he conveys from Me'.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage provides a rational proof for the necessity of truthfulness in messengers. The argument is that if a prophet were to lie, then God's affirmation of him through miracles would make God complicit in the lie, since miracles are equivalent to God saying 'My servant is truthful'. Therefore, lying by a prophet is impossible.

Key Terms
صدق
معجزة
خبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles only prove the prophet's power or special status, not necessarily that they are truthful.
Correction: Miracles are not just signs of power; they are divine endorsements of the prophet's message. God does not confirm a liar, so miracles guarantee the truthfulness of the messenger.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, what would happen if a prophet lied?
A) God would punish him immediately
B) Lying would be attributed to God
C) The miracle would still confirm him
D) Nothing would change

Key Takeaway
The truthfulness of prophets is rationally necessary because God confirms them by miracles, which would make God a liar if the prophet were false.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If every miracle in the Quran is God's personal guarantee that Muhammad (ﷺ) is truthful in everything he conveys, then why do you still hesitate to fully obey a single command from the Sunnah? What area of your life are you treating as if the Prophet might have been mistaken?
?
Consider a lie you have told—even a small one. By the logic of this lesson, if a prophet’s lie would make God a liar, how does your own lie reflect on your claim to follow the truthful prophet? Are you willing to purge deceit from your speech today?
?
This proof shows that God would never endorse falsehood. Do you live as though God's word is the ultimate truth, or do you sometimes treat it as a recommendation? What would it cost you to start treating every verse as a direct command from the One who cannot lie?

Why Messengers Must Be Trustworthy
Sanusi begins a proof that messengers must be trustworthy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational conditional premise that if messengers were treacherous, it would invert the moral status of prohibited and disliked acts, thereby showing the necessity of their trustworthiness.

Core Idea
A messenger's trustworthiness is proven by the absurdity of the alternative: it would make prohibited acts permissible.

Sanusi begins a rational demonstration that divine messengers must be inherently trustworthy. The proof proceeds by a counterfactual: if they could be treacherous, the very categories of prohibited and disliked would be upended. This lesson examines the opening of that argument, setting up the logical structure that will lead to the necessity of trustworthiness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the translation. Note that the passage is cut off, but the logical direction is clear.
The proof is incomplete; the conclusion is implied by the context.
2
Identify the conditional structure
The proof is framed as a conditional: 'if they were treacherous... then...'. Identify the premise (the act of treachery) and the consequence (inversion of moral status).
3
Infer the missing conclusion
Since the passage ends abruptly, ask yourself: what would become of the prohibited or disliked act? The commentary suggests it would become permissible or commendable. Understand why that would be absurd and thus impossible.
The full proof continues beyond this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الأَمَانَةِ لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : فَلَأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ خَانُوا بِفِعْلِ مُحَرَّمِ أَوْ مَكْرُوهِ لَأَنْقَلَبَ الْمُحَرَّمُ أَوِ
As for the proof of the necessity of trustworthiness for them, peace and blessings be upon them: it is that if they were treacherous by doing a prohibited or disliked act, then the prohibited or disliked would become...
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage begins a rational proof that messengers must be trustworthy (أمانة). The argument is that if they committed a prohibited (محرم) or disliked (مكروه) act, that act's moral status would be inverted (لانقلب) – likely becoming permissible or even commendable, since God's endorsement through miracles would otherwise affirm the act. The passage is incomplete.

Key Terms
أمانة
خيانة
محرم
مكروه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets could commit minor sins but God would forgive them.
Correction: This passage shows that any prohibited or disliked act by a messenger would invert its moral status, which is impossible. Therefore, prophets are protected from all such acts.

Checkpoint
What does the proof say would happen if a messenger committed a prohibited or disliked act?
A) They would be punished immediately
B) The act's moral status would invert
C) God would reject their prophethood
D) The act would be hidden from people

Key Takeaway
The proof establishes that messengers cannot commit prohibited or disliked acts because doing so would invert the moral order, which is rationally impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The proof shows that even a disliked (makruh) act cannot come from a messenger. Think of a 'small sin' or disliked habit you tolerate in your life. If the Prophet ﷺ would not even approach it, how can you continue to excuse it? What will you do to uproot it starting today?
?
The argument hinges on the fact that a messenger's actions define moral categories. Who are you allowing to define right and wrong in your life? Are you truly taking the messenger's standard as your measure, or are you following cultural norms or your own desires?
?
If the inversion of moral order is impossible for a messenger, what does that say about your own responsibility to uphold the moral order? In what area of your life are you currently inverting God's commands by treating a prohibition as permissible? What step will you take to correct this today?

The Three Categories of Prophetic Attributes
Sanusi enumerates the three categories of prophetic attributes with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational categories of attributes for prophets as defined by Sanusi in Sunni kalam: obligatory (wajib), impossible (mustahil), and permissible (ja'iz).

Core Idea
Prophetic attributes are neatly divided into wajib, mustahil, and ja'iz.

Sanusi now turns from discussing the divine attributes to the attributes of prophets. He applies the same three-fold classification we studied earlier—obligatory, impossible, and permissible—to the messengers. This passage establishes the standard Sunni framework for prophetic infallibility and the boundaries of what can be attributed to them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Sanusi uses the same categories as for divine attributes, but applies them to prophets.
2
Identify the three categories
The passage presents three categories: obligatory, impossible, and permissible. Find the Arabic terms and the specific attributes listed under each.
3
Understand the opposites
For each obligatory attribute, there is an impossible opposite. Identify the three opposites and note that even disliked acts (makruh) are impossible for prophets.
This establishes a strong form of prophetic infallibility.
4
Reflect on permissible attributes
The permissible category includes human traits that do not lower the prophet's rank. Consider examples like illness. Why does this matter?
This shows prophets are still human, but free from defects.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام في النبوات . وَأَمَّا الرُّسُلُ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : فَيَجِبُ فِي حَقِّهِمُ : الصِّدْقُ ، وَالأَمَانَةُ ، وَتَبْلِيغُ مَا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ لِلْخَلْقِ . وَيَسْتَحِيلُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : أَضْدَادُ هَذِهِ الصَّفَاتِ ؛ وَهِيَ : الْكَذِبُ ، وَالْخِيَانَةُ بِفِعْلِ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا نُهِيَ عَنْهُ نَهْيَ تَحْرِيمٍ أَوْ كَرَاهَةٍ ، وَكِتْمَانُ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ لِلْخَلْقِ . وَيَجُوزُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : مَا هُوَ مِنَ الأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ الَّتِي لا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ فِي مَرَاتِبِهِمُ الْعَلِيَّةِ ؛ كَالْمَرَضِ وَنَحْوِهِ .
Discourse on prophethoods. As for the messengers (peace and blessings be upon them): obligatory concerning them are truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveying what they were commanded to convey to creation. And impossible concerning them (peace and blessings be upon them) are the opposites of these attributes, which are: lying, betraying by doing something prohibited or disliked, and concealing anything they were commanded to convey to creation. And permissible concerning them (peace and blessings be upon them) is what is of the human traits that do not lead to a deficiency in their lofty ranks, such as illness and the like.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage defines the three categories of attributes for prophets: wajib (obligatory), mustahil (impossible), and ja'iz (permissible). The obligatory attributes are truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amana), and conveying the message (tabligh). The impossible attributes are their opposites: lying (kadhib), betraying (khiyana) by committing prohibited or disliked acts, and concealing (kitman) any part of the message. The permissible attributes are human traits (a'rad bashariyya) that do not detract from their high station, such as illness. This categorization is standard in Sunni kalam and establishes the foundation for prophetic infallibility.

Key Terms
واجب
مستحيل
جائز
صدق
أمانة
تبليغ
كذب
خيانة
كتمان
أعراض بشرية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets can commit minor sins or make honest mistakes that involve sin.
Correction: The passage clarifies that even disliked acts (makruh) are impossible for prophets, as they fall under betrayal (khiyana). Prophets are protected from all sin, major and minor.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT an impossible attribute for prophets?
A) Lying
B) Concealing the message
C) Illness
D) Betraying by doing a prohibited act

Key Takeaway
Prophets must possess truthfulness, trustworthiness, and conveyance; they cannot have their opposites; and permissible human traits do not diminish their rank.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a hadith that seems difficult or contradicts your desires, does your heart lean towards doubting its authenticity or finding an excuse to ignore it? How does the knowledge that concealment is impossible for the Prophet ﷺ confront your reluctance to accept what he conveyed? Will you commit today to accepting every authentic teaching from him, even if it challenges you?
?
The Prophet ﷺ was entrusted with the message and delivered it fully without any omission. Think of one teaching of Islam that you know but have not fully implemented in your life. What is stopping you? Is it not a form of betrayal (khiyana) to hold back obedience when you know the truth? What step will you take this week to act on that neglected command?
?
Prophets are allowed to experience human traits like illness, but never to lie or betray. Consider your own life: in what situations are you tempted to lie or hide the truth to protect your image or avoid discomfort? How can the example of the Prophet's perfect truthfulness and trustworthiness inspire you to be more honest and reliable, even when it is costly? What will you change starting today?

Proof for the Obligation of Truthfulness in Prophets
Sanusi proves the obligation of truthfulness in prophets via a conditional argument.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that prophets must be truthful, based on Allah's confirmation through miracles.

Core Idea
Miracles are Allah's stamp of truth; if prophets could lie, Allah would be lying.

Sanusi presents a concise but powerful proof for why truthfulness is obligatory for prophets. The argument hinges on the logical link between miracles and divine confirmation. Before we examine the passage, consider this: if Allah endorses a prophet through a miracle, what would it mean if that prophet then spoke falsely? This passage answers that question.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the English translation. Notice the concise style.
The key term is 'برهان' meaning proof.
2
Identify the logical structure
Identify the conditional: if prophets were not truthful, then Allah's report would be false. Miracles are equivalent to Allah saying the prophet is truthful.
The proof is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Reflect on the impossibility
Consider why it is impossible for Allah to lie. This is a foundational theological premise. Therefore, the assumption that prophets could lie is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : فَلأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ لَمْ يَصْدُقُوا لَلَزِمَ الْكَذِبُ فِي خَبَرِهِ تَعَالَى ؛ لِتَصْدِيقِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُمْ بِالْمُعْجِزَاتِ النَّازِلَةِ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى : صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي .
As for the proof of the obligation of their truthfulness (peace and blessings be upon them): because if they were not truthful, then lying would necessarily follow in the report of Allah the Exalted, due to His confirming them by miracles that are in the position of His statement: 'My servant has spoken truthfully in all that he conveys from Me.'
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage provides the proof (burhan) for the obligation of truthfulness in prophets. The argument is: if prophets could lie, then Allah's confirmation of them through miracles would entail that Allah's own statement is false, because miracles serve as Allah's endorsement that the prophet is truthful. Since it is impossible for Allah to lie, prophets must be truthful. The miracles are like Allah saying, 'My servant has spoken truthfully.' Therefore, lying would imply lying in Allah's statement, which is impossible.

Key Terms
برهان
وجوب
صدق
معجزات

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof is circular because it assumes Allah cannot lie, which is what we are trying to prove about prophets.
Correction: The proof does not assume the conclusion; it uses a separate premise that Allah's statement cannot be false, which is a foundational theological truth, not derived from prophecy.

Checkpoint
What is the consequence if prophets were not truthful?
A) They would lose their prophethood
B) Allah's report would be false
C) Miracles would cease
D) People would not believe them

Key Takeaway
Prophets must be truthful because their miracles are divine endorsements; if they lied, Allah would be condemning Himself to falsehood, which is impossible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah's truthfulness is absolute and He cannot lie, what does that mean for your own speech? In what areas of your life do you allow small falsehoods—jokes, exaggerations, white lies—that contradict the character of a servant of the All-Truthful? This week, commit to one specific situation where you will choose truth even when a lie would be easier.
?
You now understand that when a prophet conveys a message, Allah essentially says, 'My servant has spoken truthfully.' When you convey Islamic knowledge to others—even a simple hadith or verse—do you feel the weight of that same endorsement? Are you as careful with accuracy as if Allah were saying that about you? What is one step you can take today to ensure that everything you teach or quote is verified and truthful?

Prophethood

Proof for Trustworthiness and Conveying
Sanusi proves prophets must be trustworthy and convey the message, using the command to follow them.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the kalam argument that prophets must be trustworthy and convey the message because Allah commands us to follow them.

Core Idea
Following prophets means Allah cannot command us to do wrong, so prophets are sinless.

Sanusi now proves a crucial attribute of prophets: their trustworthiness and their duty to convey the message. He uses a simple but powerful logical argument based on Allah's command to follow the prophets. This passage shows how kalam derives theological truths from the very commands of revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then read the English translation. Notice the concise logical structure.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Understand the conditional
Identify the conditional statement: 'if they were to betray by doing something forbidden or disliked, then the forbidden or disliked would turn into an act of obedience.' Why would that happen? Because Allah commanded us to follow them.
3
Grasp the contradiction
Allah does not command what is forbidden or disliked. So if following a prophet meant doing a forbidden act, that would contradict Allah's nature. Therefore, prophets cannot commit such acts.
This is the core of the proof.
4
Apply the same logic to conveying
Notice the final sentence: 'this very same is the proof for the obligation of the third.' The third attribute is conveying the message. If prophets concealed part of the message, following them would require concealing, which Allah does not command.
So the same proof establishes both attributes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الْأَمَانَةِ لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ : فَلَأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ خَانُوا بِفِعْلِ مُحَرَّمٍ أَوْ مَكْرُوهٍ لَانْقَلَبَ الْمُحَرَّمُ أَوِ الْمَكْرُوهُ طَاعَةً فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ ; لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى قَدْ أَمَرَنَا بِالِاقْتِدَاءِ بِهِمْ فِي أَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ ، وَلَا يَأْمُرُ تَعَالَى بِمُحَرَّمٍ وَلَا مَكْرُوهٍ ، وَهَذَا بِعَيْنِهِ هُوَ بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الثَّالِثِ .
As for the proof of the obligation of trustworthiness for them (peace and blessings be upon them): because if they were to betray by doing something forbidden or disliked, then the forbidden or disliked would turn into an act of obedience in their case (peace and blessings be upon them), because Allah the Exalted has commanded us to follow them in their sayings and actions, and the Exalted does not command what is forbidden or disliked. And this very same is the proof for the obligation of the third.
Source pages p. 95

Commentary
This passage presents the proof for the obligation of trustworthiness (amana) and, by extension, conveying the message (tabligh). The argument: if prophets were to commit forbidden or disliked acts, those acts would become acts of obedience for them, because Allah commands us to follow the prophets in all their sayings and actions. But it is impossible for Allah to command something forbidden or disliked. Therefore, prophets cannot commit such acts. The same reasoning applies to the third attribute (tabligh): if they concealed any part of the message, following them would entail concealing, which is not commanded.

اقتداء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets are not infallible and can commit sins.
Correction: Prophets are protected from sin and error in conveying revelation. The argument shows that if they committed sins, following them would be impossible because Allah commands only good.

Checkpoint
What would happen if a prophet committed a forbidden act?
A) It would remain forbidden
B) It would become an act of obedience for him
C) He would be punished
D) His prophethood would end

Key Takeaway
Prophets are trustworthy and convey the message because if they did otherwise, following them would require disobedience, which Allah cannot command.

Proof for the Permissibility of Human Traits in Prophets
Sanusi provides the proof and four wisdoms for human traits in prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof and the divine wisdoms behind prophets experiencing human traits despite their high status.

Core Idea
Prophets' human traits are not flaws but serve higher purposes.

Sanusi now explains why it is entirely permissible for prophets to experience human traits like illness, poverty, or sadness. The proof is simple: we observe these traits happening to them. But there is a deeper wisdom behind each occurrence. This lesson unpacks the four purposes that transform what might look like a deficiency into a sign of divine care.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the literal translation. Notice the structure: a proof followed by four possible wisdoms.
The passage is a single sentence in Arabic, so read carefully.
2
Identify the proof
Sanusi states that the proof is observation (mushahada) of these traits occurring to prophets. This is an empirical argument from history.
Observation is a valid proof in kalam for contingent matters.
3
List the four wisdoms
Find the four purposes introduced by 'إِمَّا' (either): (1) to magnify reward, (2) for legislation, (3) to console from the world, (4) to alert to the lowliness of this world.
These wisdoms show that human traits are not pointless or degrading.
4
Reflect on the common misunderstanding
Some might think prophets should be free from all hardship. But Sanusi shows that these experiences are meaningful and even beneficial.
This connects to the core idea that human traits serve higher purposes.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا دَلِيلُ جَوَازِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ - صَلَوَاتُ اللهِ وَسَلَامُهُ عَلَيْهِمْ - : فَمُشَاهَدَةُ وُقُوعِهَا بِهِمْ ، إِمَّا لِتَعْظِيمِ أَجْرِهِمْ ، أَوْ لِلتَّشْرِيعِ ، أَوْ لِلتَّسَلِّي عَنِ الدُّنْيَا ، وَالتَّنَتُهِ لِخِسَّةِ قَدْرِهَا عِنْدَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى ، وَعَدَمِ رِضَاهُ تَعَالَى بِهَا دَارَ جَزَاءٍ لِأَوْلِيَائِهِ ; بِاعْتِبَارِ أَحْوَالِهِمْ فِيهَا عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ .
As for the proof of the permissibility of human traits upon them—peace and blessings of Allah be upon them—it is the observation of their occurring to them, either to magnify their reward, or for legislation, or to console from the world, and the alerting to the lowliness of its status with Allah the Exalted, and His not being pleased with it as an abode of recompense for His friends, considering their states in it, peace and blessings be upon them.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage provides the proof (dalil) for the permissibility of human traits (a'rad bashariyya) in prophets. The proof is direct observation (mushahada) that prophets indeed experienced such traits. The text then lists four wisdoms (hikam) behind this permission: (1) to increase their reward, (2) to legislate rulings related to those states, (3) to console them about worldly life, (4) to alert to the lowliness of this world and that Allah is not pleased with it as an abode for His friends. These traits are not deficiencies but serve higher purposes.

Correction: Sanusi shows that such traits are permissible and even beneficial, serving higher purposes like increased reward and legislation.

?

Proof for Human Accidents on Prophets
Sanusi gives the proof for human accidents befalling prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for the permissibility of human accidents (a'rad bashariyya) befalling prophets and the three divine purposes behind such occurrences.

Core Idea
Human hardships of prophets are observed and serve divine wisdom.

Sanusi now turns to a crucial question: If prophets are protected, can they still experience ordinary human trials like illness or poverty? The answer is yes, and the proof is simply that we have observed it in history. But this observation is not random — it points to deeper purposes. In this passage, he lays out the evidence and its threefold rationale.

Guided Path
1
Read and locate the proof
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that Sanusi begins with 'wa amma dalilu...' — this signals he is now giving the evidence for a claim already stated.
The proof is not a theoretical argument but an empirical observation (mushahada).
2
Identify the three reasons
The passage lists three purposes for why human accidents occur on prophets. Try to spot them in the Arabic: li-ta'zim ajrihim, li-tashri', li-tasalli 'an al-dunya wa al-tanattuh...
These are not exhaustive but represent key wisdoms.
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Consider why Sanusi includes the disparagement of the world as a reason. How does this reinforce the idea that prophets' hardships are not punishments?
This connects to the broader theme of prophethood and divine justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا دَلِيلُ جَوَازِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ - صَلَوَاتُ اللهِ وَسَلامُهُ عَلَيْهِمْ - : فَمُشَاهَدَةُ وُقُوعِهَا بِهِمْ ، إِمَّا لِتَعْظِيمِ أَجْرِهِمْ ، أَوْ لِلتَّشْرِيع ، أَوْ لِلتَسَلِّي عَنِ الدُّنْيَا ، وَالتَّنَتُهِ (۱) لِخِسَةِ قَدْرِهَا عِنْدَ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى ، وَعَدَمِ رِضَاهُ تَعَالَى بِهَا دَارَ جَزَاءِ لِأَوْلِيَائِهِ ؛ بِأَعْتِبَارِ أَحْوَالِهِمْ فِيهَا عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ .
As for the proof of the permissibility of human accidents upon them (peace and blessings of Allah be upon them): it is the observation of their occurrence upon them, either for the magnification of their reward, or for legislation, or for consolation regarding the world, and for disparagement (1) of its lowly status with Allah Most High, and His Most High not being pleased with it as an abode of recompense for His friends, considering their states therein, upon them be prayer and peace.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is a proof for the permissibility (jawaz) of human accidents (a'rad bashariyya) occurring on prophets. The author states that the proof is observation (mushahada) of such occurrences happening to them. He then lists three reasons for these occurrences: (1) to magnify their reward (ta'zim ajrihim) – implying that through hardships their ranks are elevated; (2) for legislation (tashri') – meaning that their experiences serve as legal precedents for the community; (3) for consolation regarding the world (tasalli 'an al-dunya) and to show the lowly status of the world in Allah's sight, indicating that the world is not the abode of recompense for the righteous. The passage ends by noting that these considerations are based on their states (ahwal) in the world. The footnote variant 'التنبه' (tanabbuh) suggests an alternative reading meaning 'admonition' or 'alertness'.

Implications of the Second Shahada: Prophethood and Messengers
Sanusi derives prophetic attributes and implications from the second Shahada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the second part of the Shahada entails belief in all prophets and their essential attributes of truthfulness, sinlessness, and human nature.

Core Idea
Believing Muhammad is Allah's messenger means affirming all prophets and their infallibility.

This passage unpacks the phrase 'Muhammadun Rasul Allah' to show its far-reaching implications. Sanusi demonstrates that affirming Muhammad's messengerhood necessarily includes belief in all previous prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day. Moreover, it establishes three non-negotiable attributes of prophets: their truthfulness, their protection from sin, and their shared humanity. Understanding these implications deepens one's faith and guards against common misconceptions about prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and its translation
Read the Arabic text slowly, then the literal translation. Notice how Sanusi begins by expanding the scope of the second Shahada.
The passage ends abruptly; the doctrine is still complete.
2
Identify the three derived doctrines
List the three key points: (1) necessity of truthfulness, impossibility of lying; (2) impossibility of any forbidden acts; (3) permissibility of human attributes.
These are the core theological consequences.
3
Reflect on why these attributes are essential
Consider why truthfulness and sinlessness are necessary for their role as teachers and messengers of revelation.
This connects to the concept of 'isma (protection) in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما قولنا: (محمد رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم) فيدخل فيه الإيمان بسائر الأنبياء والملائكة عليهم الصلاة والسلام والكتب السماوية واليوم الآخر؛ لأنه عليه الصلاة والسلام جاء بتصديق جميع ذلك. ويؤخذ منه: وجوب صدق الرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام واستحالة الكذب عليهم؛ وإلا لم يكونوا رسلاً أمناء لمولانا العالم بالخفيات جل وعز، واستحالة فعل المنهيات كلها؛ لأنهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام أرسلوا ليعلموا الخلق بأقوالهم وأفعالهم وسكوتهم، فيلزم ألا يكون في جميعها مخالفة لأمر مولانا جل وعز الذي اختارهم على جميع الخلق وأمنهم على سر وحيه. ويؤخذ منه أيضاً: جواز الأعراض البشرية التي
And as for our statement: (Muhammad is the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace) — it includes belief in all the prophets and angels, peace be upon them, and the heavenly books, and the Last Day; because he, peace be upon him, came confirming all of that. And from it is taken: the necessity of the truthfulness of the messengers, peace be upon them, and the impossibility of lying upon them; otherwise they would not be trusted messengers of our Master, the Knower of hidden things, mighty and majestic; and the impossibility of [them] doing all forbidden acts; because they, peace be upon them, were sent to teach creation by their words, actions, and silences, so it is necessary that there be no opposition in all of them to the command of our Master, mighty and majestic, who chose them over all creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. And from it is also taken: the permissibility of human attributes that...
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage explains the theological implications of the second part of the Shahada, 'Muhammadun Rasul Allah'. Sanusi begins by noting that belief in Muhammad as God's messenger entails belief in all other prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day, because Muhammad confirmed them. He then derives three key doctrines regarding prophets. First, the necessity of their truthfulness (ṣidq) and the impossibility of lying (kidhb) upon them; otherwise they would not be trustworthy (umanāʾ). Second, the impossibility of their committing any prohibited acts (manhiyyāt), because they were sent to teach by example, so their actions must align with God's commands. Third, the permissibility (jawāz) of human attributes (aʿrāḍ bashariyya) for them, consistent with their human nature. The passage ends mid-sentence, but the gist is that prophets share common human characteristics while being protected from sin and falsehood.

Key Takeaway
The second Shahada implies belief in all prophets and their essential attributes of truthfulness, sinlessness, and human nature.

Implications of the Second Shahada: Belief and Prophetic Attributes
Sanusi derives belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, Last Day, and necessary prophetic attributes from the second shahada.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the second shahada implies belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day, and that it also necessitates the prophets being truthful and sinless.

Core Idea
The second shahada is the key to all prophetic belief and attributes.

Sanusi teaches us that the declaration 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' is not just about Muhammad—it opens the door to believing in all messengers, angels, books, and the Last Day. More importantly, it reveals the essential qualities a prophet must have: absolute truthfulness and freedom from sin. Let's explore how he proves this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Notice how Sanusi structures his argument from the shahada to its implications.
The passage is a single continuous argument.
2
Identify the two implications
First, the shahada implies belief in other prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day. Second, it implies necessary prophetic attributes: truthfulness and impossibility of sin.
These are derived from the fact that Muhammad confirmed all previous revelations and that prophets are teachers.
3
Understand the proof for truthfulness
Sanusi argues that if prophets could lie, they would not be trustworthy (أمناء) for God, who knows all hidden things.
Truthfulness is obligatory (واجب), lying is impossible (مستحيل).
4
Understand the proof for sinlessness
Prophets were sent to teach by words, deeds, and silences; therefore none of these can contradict God's command. This makes it impossible for them to commit forbidden acts.
Sinlessness (عصمة) is derived from their role as teachers.
5
Reflect on the overall lesson
Consider how the second shahada encompasses both belief and moral attributes. This shows the depth of the testimony of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا قَوْلُنَا : ( مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ ( صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ : فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالْمَلائِكَةِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ ، وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ ، وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ . وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ : وُجُوبُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ ، وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الْكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِمْ ، وَإِلا لَمْ يَكُونُوا رُسُلاً أمَنَاءَ لِمَوْلانَا الْعَالِم بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ ، وَاسْتِحَالَهُ فِعل الْمَنْهِيَّاتِ كُلْهَا ؛ لأَنَّهُمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ أُرْسِلُوا ليُعَلِّمُوا الْخَلْقَ بأَفْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَسُكُوتِهِمْ ، فَيَلْزَمُ أَلا يَكُونَ فِي جَمِيعِهَا مُخَالَفَةٌ لِأَمْرِ مَوْلانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي اخْتَارَهُمْ عَلَى جَمِيعِ الْخَلْقِ ، وَأَمِنَهُمْ عَلَى سِرْ وَحْيِهِ
As for our statement: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of God (may God bless him and grant him peace)', it includes belief in all the [other] prophets and the angels, upon them be prayers and peace, and the heavenly scriptures, and the Last Day; because he, upon him be prayer and peace, came confirming all of that. And from it is derived: the obligation of truthfulness of the messengers, upon them be prayers and peace, and the impossibility of lying upon them, and if not they would not be trustworthy messengers to our Lord, the Knower of hidden things, may He be glorified and exalted, and the impossibility of committing all forbidden acts; because they, upon them be prayers and peace, were sent to teach creation by their words, deeds, and silences, so it is necessary that there be in all of them no opposition to the command of our Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, who chose them above all creation, and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation.
Source pages p. 99

Commentary
This passage is both an implication and a proof. Sanusi explains that the second shahada, 'Muhammadun Rasul Allah', implies belief in all other prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day because the Prophet Muhammad confirmed all of these. Then he derives two necessary attributes of prophets from the fact that they are messengers: first, truthfulness (sidq) is obligatory for them and lying is impossible; otherwise they would not be trustworthy. Second, it is impossible for them to commit any forbidden act (ma'asi), because they are sent to teach by their words, deeds, and even silences, so none of these can contradict God's command. The proof is that if they could sin, they would not be reliable teachers. The final phrase emphasizes that God chose them and entrusted them with revelation.

Key Terms
الإيمان بسائر الأنبياء
وجوب صدق الرسل
استحالة الكذب
استحالة فعل المنهيات
أمناء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the second shahada only affirms Muhammad's prophethood.
Correction: Sanusi shows it includes belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, Last Day, and necessary prophetic attributes.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, what does the second shahada necessarily imply about the prophets?
A) They are infallible only in delivering the message
B) They must be truthful and cannot commit forbidden acts

Key Takeaway
The second shahada is not only about Muhammad but implies belief in all prophethood fundamentals and the essential attributes of truthfulness and sinlessness.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Prophets taught by their actions no less than their words. Is your own life a consistent teaching of the message of Islam? If a non-Muslim observed your behavior for a day, would they see the truthfulness and sinlessness that your shahada requires you to emulate? What are you willing to change to align your actions with the prophetic example?

Permissible Human Attributes for Prophets
Sanusi derives the permissibility of human attributes for prophets and explains their benefit.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets may have permissible human traits that neither diminish nor harm their prophethood, and that such traits can actually elevate their status.

Core Idea
Prophetic humanity is a virtue, not a flaw.

Sanusi has already established the necessary and impossible attributes for prophets. Now he draws a corollary: prophets may have permissible human traits—like eating, sleeping, marriage—as long as they do not reduce their high rank. This passage explains why such traits are not only allowed but can even increase the prophets' standing with Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the full Arabic passage once, then its literal translation. Notice the structure: a derivation from a previous proof, the ruling of permissibility, and the reasoning.
The passage is a single sentence with multiple clauses.
2
Identify the ruling and its condition
Find the phrase that states the permissibility (جَوَازُ) and the condition that it does not lead to deficiency (لا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ).
The condition is crucial to distinguish permissible from impermissible traits.
3
Reflect on why permissible attributes can increase the prophets' rank
Consider how the prophets' complete humanity makes them relatable role models. Why would that increase their rank with Allah? Write a brief reflection.
Think about the wisdom in prophets experiencing human trials.

Commentary
This passage is a corollary to the previous proof. Sanusi adds that besides the necessary and impossible attributes, prophets may have permissible (ja'iz) human attributes—such as eating, sleeping, marriage, illness—provided these do not detract from their exalted rank. Such attributes are not only harmless, but can actually increase their status because they demonstrate the prophets' complete humanity and make them relatable as role models. The key point is that these attributes do not conflict with prophethood or imply any imperfection in their character.

Moses' Experience Proves Divine Speech's Sublimity
Sanusi relates how Moses blocked his ears after hearing God's speech to avoid the ugliness of human speech.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the reported experience of Moses demonstrates the radical uniqueness of divine speech and its qualitative difference from all created speech.

Core Idea
Divine speech is so sublime that human speech becomes unbearable by comparison.

Sanusi presents a powerful narrative proof from the life of Moses (peace be upon him). After Moses heard Allah's speech directly, he found human speech so ugly and desolate that he had to block his ears to survive. This extraordinary reaction underscores that divine speech is not merely a superior version of human speech but belongs to an entirely different order of reality.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the narrative flow through you before interpreting.
Notice the emotional intensity: words like 'ugliness' (قبح) and 'desolation' (وَحشة).
2
Identify the key elements
Find Moses' action (plugging ears), the reason (fear of death from human speech's ugliness), and the duration (long period until forgetting).
3
Reflect on the theological implication
Ask yourself: why does Sanusi use this story? It shows divine speech is 'without example' (عديم المثال) and that created speech is incomparably inferior.
This connects to the doctrine of the uncreatedness and transcendence of divine speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ورد عن موسى عليه الصلاة والسلامُ أَنَّهُ كَانَ يَسدُّ أذنيه بعد رجوعِهِ مِنَ المناجاة وسماع كلامِ اللهِ تعالى مدَّةً ؛ لئلا يسمع كلام الناس فيموتَ مِنْ شدَّةِ قبحِهِ ووَحشة حقيقته بالنسبة إلى كلام الله تعالى العديم المثالِ ، ولا يستطيع أن يسمع كلامَ الخَلْقِ حتى تطولَ بهِ المدَّةُ ، وينسيَهُ الله تعالى ما ذاقَ مِنْ لذَّةِ ذلكَ الاستماع لكلامِهِ
And it has been reported from Moses, peace and prayer be upon him, that he used to plug his ears after returning from the intimate conversation and hearing the speech of Allah the Exalted for a period, lest he hear the speech of people and die from the intensity of its ugliness and the desolation of its reality relative to the speech of Allah the Exalted, which has no example. And he could not hear the speech of people until a long period passed, and Allah the Exalted made him forget what he had tasted of the pleasure of that listening to His speech.
Source pages p. 200

Commentary
This passage provides a historical proof of the transcendence of divine speech. It recounts that after Moses (peace be upon him) heard God's speech directly, he would block his ears for a period to avoid hearing human speech. The reason is that human speech, compared to God's speech, was so ugly and desolate in its reality that it could cause death. Moses could only bear to hear human speech again after a long time, once God had made him forget the pleasure of hearing His speech. This story underscores the qualitative gap between divine and human speech: divine speech is utterly unique (عديم المثال) and its beauty is such that all created speech becomes repulsive by comparison. The report is used to counter any attempt to liken God's speech to human speech.

Correction: This passage shows that divine speech is so qualitatively different that human speech becomes unbearably ugly and desolate by comparison. It is 'without example' (عديم المثال), meaning it belongs to a completely different category.

Necessary, Impossible, and Permissible Attributes of the Messengers
Sanusi enumerates the necessary, impossible, and permissible attributes of messengers and defines a messenger.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three rational judgments applied to the messengers: their necessary, impossible, and permissible attributes, as well as the definition of a messenger and the types of messengers.

Core Idea
Messengers must be truthful, trustworthy, and deliver the message; the opposite is impossible; human traits that don't diminish their rank are permissible.

In this passage, Sanusi applies the framework of necessary, impossible, and permissible to the messengers (rusul). He first lists the essential attributes that every messenger must possess, then their logical opposites that cannot be attributed to them, and finally the human traits that are permissible. He also provides a concise definition of a messenger, clarifying that messengers may have a book, a law, or abrogate previous laws.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic once, then the translation. Notice the structure: three categories, then a definition.
Pay attention to the flow from necessary to impossible to permissible.
2
Identify the three categories
Find the necessary, impossible, and permissible attributes. Note how each is defined and the examples given.
The impossible attributes are the opposites of the necessary ones.
3
Understand the definition of a messenger
Read the definition and the note about 'or'. Consider the distinction between having a book, a law, or abrogation.
The footnote clarifies that the second and third types overlap.
4
Reflect on the implications
Think about why these attributes are essential for prophethood. What does this tell us about the role of a messenger?
Permissible human traits show that messengers are not superhuman but chosen humans.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الكلام على الرسل فيها يجب لهم ويستحيل عليهم ويجوز في حقهم
وَأَمَّا الرُّسُلُ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ : فَيَجِبُ فِي حَقِّهِمُ الصِّدْقُ ، وَالأَمَانَهُ ، وَتَبْلِيغُ مَا أُمِرُوا بِتَبْلِيغِهِ لِلْخَلْقِ وَيَسْتَحِيلُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : [أَزْدَادُ؟] هَذِهِ الصِّفَاتِ ؛ وَهِيَ : الْكَذِبُ ، وَالْخِيَانَةُ بِفِعْلِ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا نُهِيَ عَنْهُ نَهْيَ تَحْرِيم أَوْ كَرَاهَةٍ ، وَكِتْمَانُ شَيْءٍ مِمَّا أُمِرُوا بتَبْلِيغِهِ لِلْخَلْقِ .
وَيَجُوزُ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : مَا هُوَ مِنَ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ الَّتِي لا تُؤَدِّي إِلَى نَقْصٍ فِي مَرَاتِبِهِمُ الْعَلِيَّةِ ؛ كَالْمَرَضِ وَنَحْوِهِ .
اعلم : أنَّ الرسول : هو إنسان بعثَهُ الله تعالى للخلْقِ ليبلِّغَهم ما أوحي إليه ، وقد يختص بمَنْ له كتاب ، أو شريعة ، أو نسخ لبعض أحكام الشريعة السابقة (١).
(١) ظاهر العطف بـ ( أو ) يقتضي المغايرة ، فهي ثلاثة أقوال ، لكن يشكل في الثاني والثالث ؛ إذ بينهما عموم وخصوص مطلق ؛ فكل من له نسخ له =
Discussion of the messengers, concerning what is necessary for them, impossible for them, and permissible with respect to them. As for the messengers, upon them be prayers and peace: necessary with respect to them are truthfulness, trustworthiness, and the delivery of what they were commanded to deliver to creation. And impossible with respect to them, upon them be prayers and peace, are the opposites of these attributes, namely: falsehood, betrayal by doing something that they were forbidden by a prohibition of prohibition or dislike, and concealment of something that they were commanded to deliver to creation. And permissible with respect to them, upon them be prayers and peace, is that which is from human accidents that do not lead to deficiency in their exalted ranks, such as illness and the like. Know that the messenger is a human being sent by Allah Almighty to creation to deliver to them what was revealed to him. And he may be specified as one who has a book, or a law, or an abrogation of some rulings of the previous law. (1) The apparent conjunction with 'or' requires differentiation, thus there are three statements, but the second and third are problematic because between them there is absolute generality and specificity, for everyone who has abrogation has a law, etc.
Source pages p. 232

Commentary
This passage is a classification of the attributes of the messengers (rusul) according to the three rational judgments: necessary (wajib), impossible (mustahil), and permissible (ja'iz). The author begins by stating the discussion topic. First, he lists the necessary attributes: truthfulness (sidq), trustworthiness (amanah), and delivery (tabligh) of what they were commanded to convey. Second, he states that the opposites of these attributes are impossible: falsehood (kadhib), betrayal (khiyanah) by committing a prohibited or disliked act, and concealment (kitman) of what they must deliver. Third, he states that human accidental traits that do not diminish their high station, such as illness, are permissible. The author then defines a messenger (rasul) as a human sent by Allah to deliver revelation. He adds that a messenger may be distinguished by having a book, a law, or abrogation of some previous rulings. The footnote clarifies that the wording 'or' in the definition implies a disjunction between three types, but notes that the second and third overlap, as every abrogator has a law.

صدق (sidq)
أمانة (amanah)
تبليغ (tabligh)
كذب (kadhib)
خيانة (khiyanah)
كتمان (kitman)
رسول (rasul)
شريعة (shari'ah)
نسخ (naskh)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think messengers must be free from all human limitations, like illness.
Correction: The passage clarifies that permissible human traits like illness do not detract from their rank.

Key Takeaway

Sending Messengers: Possible, Not Obligatory
Sanusi states the Ahl al-Sunna position and gives a proof refuting Mu'tazila and Barahima.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Ahl al-Sunna consider sending messengers to be possible (jāʾiz) rather than obligatory or impossible, and how this refutes the opposing views of the Mu'tazila and Barahima.

Core Idea
God is never obligated, so sending messengers is possible, not necessary.

In this lesson, Sanusi presents a concise but powerful argument on the nature of prophethood. He positions Ahl al-Sunna between two extremes: the Mu'tazila, who consider sending messengers obligatory for God, and the Barahima, who deem it impossible. Sanusi cuts through both errors with a fundamental principle of Islamic theology: God is not subject to any obligation. Let's walk through the text and unpack this proof.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice how Sanusi first states Ahl al-Sunna's position, then contrasts it with two opposing views, and finally provides a proof.
2
Identify the three positions
Find where Sanusi mentions the positions of Ahl al-Sunna, Mu'tazila, and Barahima. What does each group say about sending messengers?
Ahl al-Sunna say jāʾiz (possible), Mu'tazila say wājib (obligatory), Barahima say muḥāl (impossible).
3
Understand the proof
The proof is simple: sending is an act of God, and God is not obligated to do any act (lā yajibu ʿalayhi fiʿl). This principle refutes both obligation and impossibility.
The proof rests on an earlier established principle: God is free from any obligation.
4
Reflect on the implications
Why is it important that sending messengers is possible but not obligatory? How does this protect God's sovereignty?
It affirms God's absolute freedom and wisdom; He may send messengers or not as He wills.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا البعثُ مِنَ الجائزاتِ عند أهل السنة ، وأوجبَتْهُ المعتزلة على أصلهم الفاسد في وجوب مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح ، وأحالته البراهمة لذلك أيضاً ، ولا خفاء في هوسهم وكفرهم. والدليل لأهل السنَّةِ على أنَّ بعثَ الله تعالى للرُّسُلِ جائز لا واجبٌ : أنَّ البعثَ فعلُ مِنْ أفعالِ اللهِ تعالى ، وقد علمْتَ أَنَّهُ جَلَّ وعزَّ لا يجب عليه فعل وإنْ كانَ صلاحاً أو أصلح ، ولا يتحتم عليه ترك ، وكلامنا في أصل العقيدة واضحٌ لا يحتاجُ إلى شرح.
And this sending is among the possible things according to Ahl al-Sunna, while the Mu'tazila made it obligatory based on their corrupt principle of the obligation of observing benefit and the most beneficial, and the Barahima deemed it impossible for that reason as well, and there is no concealment of their folly and disbelief. And the proof for Ahl al-Sunna that sending messengers by God Most High is possible, not obligatory, is that sending is an act from the acts of God Most High, and you have known that He, exalted and majestic, is not obligated to do an act even if it be beneficial or most beneficial, nor is He compelled to refrain, and our speech regarding the foundation of creed is clear and does not need explanation.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a proof and refutation. Sanusi begins by stating the position of Ahl al-Sunna: that sending messengers (baʿth al-rusul) is among the possible things (jāʾizāt) for God—meaning it is within His power to do or not to do. He contrasts this with the Mu'tazila, who made it obligatory (awjabat-hu) based on their corrupt principle (aṣluhum al-fāsid) that God must observe what is beneficial and most beneficial (ṣalāḥ wa aṣlaḥ) for creation. On the other extreme, the Barahima (Brahmins) deemed it impossible (aḥālat-hu) for God to send messengers, also due to their flawed reasoning. Sanusi dismisses both as folly and disbelief. He then provides the proof (dalīl): sending is an act of God, and it has been established that God is not obligated to do any act, even if it brings benefit, nor is He compelled to refrain from anything. The matter is clear in the foundation of creed and needs no further elaboration. The argument is simple: since God is not subject to obligation, sending messengers is not necessary but remains a possibility that God may or may not actualize according to His wisdom.

جائز
واجب
أهل السنة
معتزلة
براهمة
صلاح
أصلح
فعل
لا يجب عليه

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God must do what is most beneficial for creation (Mu'tazila view).
Correction: God is not obligated to do any act, even if it is beneficial. He does as He wills.

Checkpoint
Why do Ahl al-Sunna consider sending messengers possible and not obligatory?
A) Because God has no power over it
B) Because it is an act of God and God is not obligated to do anything
C) Because the Mu'tazila proved it is impossible
D) Because messengers are not needed

Key Takeaway
For Ahl al-Sunna, sending messengers is a possible act of God that He may or may not do according to His wisdom.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you feel that God 'must' grant you something or guide you in a certain way, are you unconsciously adopting the Mu'tazila mindset? How will you train yourself to see every blessing as pure grace, not obligation?
?
The Barahima denied that God could send messengers. In what subtle ways might you be doubting God's ability to speak into your life through revelation or circumstances? Will you repent of that limit you have placed on Him?
?
If God owes you nothing—not even a prophet—yet He sent them out of His will, how does that change the way you receive His guidance today? Will you approach His commands with the gratitude of one who received an unearned gift?

The Ruling on Sending Messengers
Sanusi defines the ruling on sending messengers and gives proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to Ahl al-Sunna, sending messengers is permissible (ja'iz) for Allah, not obligatory, and why this conclusion follows from Allah's absolute freedom from obligation.

Core Idea
Allah sends messengers by His free will, not because He must.

Sanusi begins by clarifying a fundamental point of creed: is Allah obligated to send messengers? The Mu'tazila said yes, the Brahmins said impossible, but Ahl al-Sunna take the middle path of permissibility. This passage presents the concise proof that anchors this position in the principle of divine transcendence.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the Arabic once, then the literal translation. Notice the clear contrast between the three groups.
The passage uses very precise theological terms.
2
Identify the three positions
Find the three groups mentioned: Ahl al-Sunna, Mu'tazila, and Brahmins. What does each say about sending messengers?
Brahmins are a non-Islamic group that rejects prophethood entirely.
3
Understand the proof
Read the proof carefully: sending is an act of Allah, and Allah is not obligated to do any act—even beneficial ones. Hence sending is permissible, not obligatory.
This proof rests on the principle that Allah's actions are not subject to external obligations.
4
Reflect on the key principle
The passage concludes that this point of creed is clear. Ask yourself: why is it important that Allah's actions are free from obligation?
This protects divine transcendence and avoids making Allah subject to created standards.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا البعثُ مِنَ الجائزاتِ عند أهل السنة، وأوجبَتْهُ المعتزلة على أصلهم الفاسد في وجوب مراعاة الصلاح والأصلح، وأحالته البراهمة لذلك أيضاً، ولا خفاء في هوسهم وكفرهم. والدليل لأهل السنَّةِ على أنَّ بعثَ الله تعالى للرُّسُلِ جائز لا واجبٌ : أنَّ البعثَ فعلُ مِنْ أفعالِ اللهِ تعالى، وقد علمْتَ أَنَّهُ جَلَّ وعزَّ لا يجب عليه فعل وإنْ كانَ صلاحاً أو أصلح، ولا يتحتم عليه ترك، وكلامنا في أصل العقيدة واضحٌ لا يحتاجُ إلى شرح
This sending (of messengers) is among the permissible things according to Ahl al-Sunna. The Mu'tazila made it obligatory according to their corrupt principle of observing what is beneficial and most beneficial. The Brahmins deemed it impossible for that same reason as well. There is no hiding in their foolishness and disbelief. The proof for Ahl al-Sunna that Allah's sending of messengers is permissible, not obligatory: that sending is an act among the acts of Allah, and you have known that He, Majestic and Mighty, is not obligated to do an act even if it is beneficial or most beneficial, nor is He compelled to abandon (any act). And our speech concerning the foundation of creed is clear and does not need explanation.
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage defines the ruling on sending messengers (ba'th) according to Ahl al-Sunna. It begins by stating that the sending of messengers is among the permissible things (al-ja'izat) according to Ahl al-Sunna, meaning that Allah is free to send messengers or not; He is not obligated to do so. Then it contrasts this with the Mu'tazila who made it obligatory upon Allah based on their corrupt principle of observing what is beneficial and most beneficial (al-salah wa al-aslah). The Brahmins (a group that denies prophethood entirely) deemed it impossible (ahaluhu) for the same reason. The author dismisses their views as foolishness and disbelief. Then he presents the proof for Ahl al-Sunna: the act of sending messengers is an act of Allah. Since Allah is not obligated to perform any act, whether beneficial or most beneficial, nor is He compelled to refrain from any act, therefore sending messengers is permissible, not obligatory. The author concludes that this foundational point of creed is clear and needs no further elaboration.

Misconception: Some mistakenly think that sending messengers is obligatory upon Allah because it brings great benefit to humanity.
Correction: Allah is not obligated by any benefit; His actions are free. Sending messengers is a favour, not a duty.

Key Takeaway
Allāh's actions, including sending messengers, are free from any external obligation; hence they are permissible, not obligatory.

?
If you truly internalise that Allah is under no obligation to guide anyone, what responsibility does that place on you to cherish and act upon the guidance you have been given? Write one concrete change you will make today because you have received this undeserved favour.

Conditions of Prophethood: Rational, Legal, and Customary
A note explaining the rational, legal, and customary conditions of prophethood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of conditions of prophethood: rational, legal, and customary, and why Sanusi focused only on the rational conditions.

Core Idea
Prophethood has rational, legal, and customary conditions, each serving a different purpose.

This lesson explores a clarifying note from the commentators. A question arises: why did Sanusi omit conditions like intelligence in his main text? The answer reveals a crucial classification—conditions of prophethood are not all of the same type. Rational conditions are the core, but legal and customary conditions ensure the messenger's effectiveness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the question
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice that it begins with a potential question: why didn't Sanusi mention certain conditions like intelligence?
The passage is a note (tanbih) addressing this objection.
2
Understand the classification of conditions
Yaseen's answer distinguishes three types: rational, legal (shar'i), and customary (adiyya). Sanusi covered the rational ones; the others are additional.
This classification is key to understanding the completeness of Sanusi's text.
3
Review the list of legal/customary conditions
Al-Sa'd lists conditions such as masculinity, intelligence, safety from repulsive defects, and matters preserving manliness. Reflect on why each is necessary for the prophetic mission.
These conditions ensure the messenger is credible and effective in conveying the message.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تنبيه : قد يُقال : ثُمَّ شروط يذكرها المتكلمون فيما يجب للرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام؛ كالفطانة مثلاً، فلم لم يتعرّض لها الإمام المصنف ؟ والجواب : قال العلامة ياسين في ( حاشيته ) ( ق٢٣٦ ) : ( واعلم : أن ما ذكره شروط عقلية للرسل عليهم الصلاة والسلام، وأما الشروط الشرعية، والعادية : فقال السعد : من شروط النبوة : الذكورة، وكمال العقل والذكاء، والفطنة، وقوة الرأي ولو في الصبا؛ كيحيى وعيسى عليهما الصلاة والسلام، والسلامة عن كل ما ينفّر عن الاتباع؛ كزنا الآباء الأمهات والغلظة والفظاظة، والعيوب المنفرة؛ كالبرص والجذام، والأمور المخلة بالمروءة؛ كالأكل على الطريق، والحرف الدنيئة؛ كالحجامة، وكل ما يخلُّ بحكمة البعثة من أداء الشرائع وقبول الأمة. انتهى )
A note: It may be said: Then there are conditions that the mutakallimun mention among what is obligatory for the messengers, peace be upon them, such as intelligence, for example. So why did the author (al-Musannif) not address them? The answer: The scholar Yaseen said in his gloss: 'Know that what he (al-Sanusi) mentioned are rational conditions for the messengers, peace be upon them. As for the legal (shar'i) and customary conditions, al-Sa'd said: Among the conditions of prophethood are: masculinity, perfection of intellect and intelligence, acumen, strength of opinion even in childhood, like Yahya and 'Isa, peace be upon them; and safety from everything that repels from following, like fornication of parents, harshness and roughness, and repulsive defects like leprosy and elephantiasis; and matters that detract from manliness (muru'a) like eating on the road, and base professions like cupping; and everything that negates the wisdom of sending (messengers) of conveying the divine laws and acceptance by the community. End.'
Source pages p. 234

Commentary
This passage is a note (tanbih) addressing a potential question: Why did the author (al-Musannif, i.e., Sanusi) not mention conditions of prophethood like intelligence in his main text? The answer, quoting Yaseen, distinguishes between rational conditions (which Sanusi did mention) and legal (shar'i) and customary (adiyya) conditions. The passage then lists the latter as given by al-Sa'd al-Taftazani. The conditions include: masculinity (dhukura), perfection of intellect, intelligence, acumen, strength of opinion even in childhood (citing Yahya and 'Isa), safety from anything that repels followers such as parental fornication, harshness, repulsive defects like leprosy, and matters that detract from manliness (muru'a) such as eating on the road and base professions like cupping. All of these are necessary to fulfill the wisdom of the prophetic mission: conveying the laws and gaining acceptance by the community. This clarifies that the author's omission was intentional because he focused on rational conditions, while the legal and customary conditions are additional and mentioned by later scholars.

Key Terms
شروط العقلية
شروط الشرعية
شروط العادية
النبوة
الفطانة
المروءة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think all conditions of prophethood are purely rational and that Sanusi's omission of conditions like intelligence was a mistake.
Correction: The passage shows that Sanusi only covered rational conditions; there are also legal and customary conditions that he did not need to address in his main text.

Checkpoint

A) Rational conditions
B) Legal conditions
C) Customary conditions
D) All of the above

Key Takeaway
The conditions of prophethood are not only rational; legal and customary conditions ensure the messenger's credibility and effectiveness.

The Proof of the Prophets' Truthfulness: Miracles as Divine Attestation
Sanusi presents the proof that prophets must be truthful, based on miracles.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi proves the necessity of prophets' truthfulness through the concept of miracles as God's direct affirmation.

Core Idea
Miracles are God's stamp of approval on a prophet's message.

Sanusi now turns to proving that every prophet must be truthful in everything they convey from God. The argument is elegant: if God confirms a prophet's claim through miracles, then the prophet cannot lie—because that would make God a liar. This lesson unpacks that proof and the definition of miracles that supports it.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: a conditional statement (if...then) followed by explanation.
2
Understand the conditional argument
The proof is: if prophets were not truthful (i.e., they lied), then God would be lying because He confirmed them with miracles. Understand why confirming a liar is a lie.
3
Grasp the role of miracles
Miracles are not just wonders; they are positioned as God's explicit statement of truthfulness. Note the definition: khariq li'l-ada, accompanied by challenge, no opposition.
4
Connect to the conclusion
Since lying is impossible for God, prophets must be truthful. This applies to both their initial claim and subsequent teachings.
5
Reflect on the significance
This proof establishes sidq as a necessary attribute of prophets, foundational for trusting their message.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ : فَلَأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ لَمْ يَصْدُقُوا لَلَزِمَ الْكَذِبُ فِي خَبَرِهِ تَعَالَى ؛ لِتَصْدِيقِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُمْ بِالْمُعْجِزَاتِ النَّازِلَةِ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى : صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي . هَذَا بُرْهَانُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ فِي دَعْوَاهُمُ الرِّسَالَةَ، وَفِيمَا يُبَلِّغُونَهُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ إِلَى الْخَلْقِ. وَحَاصِلُ هَذَا الْبُرْهَانِ: أَنَّ الْمُعْجِزَاتِ الَّتِي خَلَقَهَا اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَلَى أَيْدِي الرُّسُلِ - وَهِيَ أَمْرٌ خَارِقٌ لِلْعَادَةِ، مَقْرُونٌ بِالتَّحَدِّي، مَعَ عَدَمِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ - تَتَنَزَّلُ مِنْ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ: صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي. فَلَوْ جَازَ الْكَذِبُ عَلَى الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ لَجَازَ الْكَذِبُ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى؛ إِذْ تَصْدِيقُ الْكَاذِبِ كَذِبٌ.
As for the proof of the necessity of their truthfulness (upon them prayers and peace): it is that if they were not truthful, then lying would be necessary in the report of Him, Most High, because He, Most High, has affirmed their truthfulness by means of the miracles (al-mu'jizat) that take the place of His statement: 'My servant has spoken truthfully in everything he conveys from Me.' This is the proof of the truthfulness of the messengers (upon them prayers and peace) in their claim of prophethood and in what they convey after that to creation. The summary of this proof is that the miracles which Allah Most High creates at the hands of the messengers—and they are a matter that breaks the norm, accompanied by challenge, with no possibility of opposition—are placed by our Lord, Majestic and Mighty, in the position of His statement: 'My servant has spoken truthfully in everything he conveys from Me.' So if lying were possible for the messengers, then lying would be possible for Him, Most High; because confirming a liar is a lie.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage presents the proof (burhan) that prophets must be truthful. It begins by stating the necessity (wujub) of their truthfulness. The argument: if they were not truthful (i.e., if they lied), then lying would be necessary in God's report, i.e., God would be a liar, because God affirms their truthfulness through miracles. Miracles are extraordinary events that indicate divine confirmation, analogous to God saying 'My servant has spoken truthfully.' This proof applies to both their initial claim of prophethood and subsequent teachings. The passage then summarizes: miracles (defined as: 1) breaking the natural norm, 2) accompanied by challenge, 3) with no opposition) serve as God's attestation. If it were possible for a prophet to lie, then it would be possible for God to lie, because confirming a liar is itself a lie. But lying is impossible for God, so prophets must be truthful. This establishes the attribute of truthfulness (sidq) as necessary for prophets.

Key Terms
برهان
الصدق
المعجزة
التصديق
الكذب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Miracles are merely displays of power or signs of divine favor, not directly tied to truthfulness.
Correction: The passage clearly states that miracles function as God's direct statement, 'My servant has spoken truthfully,' so they are specifically an attestation of the prophet's truthfulness.

Checkpoint
What is the key function of miracles in the proof of the prophets' truthfulness?
A) They prove the prophets are powerful
B) They serve as God's declaration that the prophet is truthful
C) They prove the existence of God
D) They are meant to defeat opponents

Key Takeaway
Miracles serve as God's declaration that a prophet is truthful, making it impossible for the prophet to lie, as that would entail lying by God.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear a command from the Prophet ﷺ that contradicts your desires or convenience, does your heart immediately submit, knowing that he cannot lie? If not, what does that reveal about your certainty in this proof?
?
If you truly believed that every miracle of the Prophet ﷺ is God’s personal declaration of his truthfulness, how would that change the way you read the Quran or listen to hadith? What would you do differently starting today?
?
The proof shows that doubting a prophet’s truthfulness ultimately leads to doubting God’s truthfulness. Have you ever allowed small doubts about the Prophet’s teachings to linger in your heart? What would it cost you to fully eradicate them?
