The Proof of the Truthfulness of the Messengers
Sanusi proves the necessary truthfulness of the messengers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Sanusi's rational proof for the necessary truthfulness of the messengers and why lying is impossible for Allah.

Core Idea
Miracles are Allah's endorsement; if a messenger could lie, Allah would be endorsing a lie.

Sanusi presents a concise proof for why messengers must be truthful. He argues that miracles, which are extraordinary events created by Allah at their hands, serve as divine endorsements. If a messenger could lie, Allah would be confirming a liar, which is impossible because Allah's speech is necessarily true.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let Sanusi's own logic come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the core argument
The proof is structured: if messengers could lie, then Allah would be lying because miracles are His testimony. Find the phrase 'لو لم يصدقوا لزم الكذب في خبره تعالى'.
This is a conditional proof (al-qiyās al-sharṭī).
3
Understand the role of miracles
Sanusi explains that miracles are like Allah saying 'My servant has spoken the truth'. They are not just events but divine statements of truthfulness.
The phrase 'تنزل منزلة قوله' is key.
4
Draw the conclusion
Since affirming a liar is a lie, and lying is impossible for Allah, the messengers must be truthful. Note the final statement: 'فخبره تعالى لا يكون إلا صدقا'.
This completes the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ : فَلَأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ لَمْ يَصْدُقُوا لَلَزِمَ الْكَذِبُ فِي خَبَرِهِ تَعَالَى ؛ لِتَصْدِيقِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُمْ بِالْمُعْجِزَاتِ النَّازِلَةِ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى : صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي. هَذَا بُرْهَانُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ فِي دَعْوَاهُمُ الرِّسَالَةَ ، وَفِيمَا يُبَلِّغُونَهُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ إِلَى الْخَلْقِ. وَحَاصِلُ هَذَا الْبُرْهَانِ : أَنَّ الْمُعْجِزَاتِ الَّتِي خَلَقَهَا اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَلَى أَيْدِي الرُّسُلِ - وَهِيَ أَمْرٌ خَارِقٌ لِلْعَادَةِ ، مَقْرُونٌ بِالتَّحَدِّي ، مَعَ عَدَمِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ - تَتَنَزَّلُ مِنْ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ : صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي ، فَلَوْ جَازَ الْكَذِبُ عَلَى الرُّسُلِ لَجَازَ الْكَذِبُ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى ؛ إِذْ تَصْدِيقُ الْكَاذِبِ كَذِبٌ ، وَالْكَذِبُ عَلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى مُحَالٌ ؛ إِذْ خَبَرُهُ تَعَالَى عَلَى وَفْقِ عِلْمِهِ ، وَالْخَبَرُ عَلَى وَفْقِ الْعِلْمِ لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا صِدْقاً ، فَخَبَرُهُ تَعَالَى لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا صِدْقاً . وَقَوْلُنَا فِي تَعْرِيفِ الْمُعْجِزَةِ : ( أَمْرٌ ) أَحْسَنُ مِنْ قَوْلِ بَعْضِهِمْ : ( فِعْلٌ ) ؛ لِأَنَّ الْأَمْرَ يَتَنَاوَلُ الْفِعْلَ ؛ كَانْفِجَارِ الْمَاءِ مَثَلاً مِنْ بَيْنِ الْأَصَابِعِ ، وَعَدَمَ الْفِعْلِ ؛ كَعَدَمِ إِحْرَاقِ النَّارِ مَثَلاً لِإِبْرَاهِيمَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ . وَاحْتَرَزْنَا بِقَيْدِ ( الْمُقَارَنَةِ لِلتَّحَدِّي ) عَنْ كَرَامَاتِ الْأَوْلِيَاءِ ، وَالْعَلَامَاتِ الْإِرْهَاصِيَّةِ الَّتِي تَتَقَدَّمُ بِعْثَةَ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ تَأْسِيساً لَهَا ، وَعَنْ أَنْ يَتَّخِذَ الْكَاذِبُ مُعْجِزَةَ مَنْ مَضَى حُجَّةً لِنَفْسِهِ . وَاحْتَرَزْنَا بِقَيْدِ ( عَدَمِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ ) عَنِ السِّحْرِ وَالشَّعْوَدَةِ .
As for the proof of the obligation of their truthfulness, peace and blessings be upon them: because if they were not truthful, then lying would be necessary in His report, may He be exalted, due to His, may He be exalted, affirming them through the miracles that take the place of His, may He be exalted, saying: 'My servant has spoken the truth in everything he conveys from Me.' This is the proof of the truthfulness of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, in their claim of prophethood and in what they convey thereafter to creation. The summary of this proof is that the miracles which Allah, may He be exalted, creates at the hands of the messengers — and they are a matter that breaks custom, accompanied by a challenge, with absence of opposition — take the place, from our Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, of His, may He be glorified and exalted, saying: 'My servant has spoken the truth in everything he conveys from Me.' So if lying were possible for the messengers, then lying would be possible for Him, may He be exalted; because affirming a liar is a lie. And lying against Allah, may He be exalted, is impossible; because His report, may He be exalted, conforms to His knowledge, and a report that conforms to knowledge is nothing but truth. So His report, may He be exalted, is nothing but truth. And our saying in the definition of miracle: (a matter) is better than the saying of some: (an act); because 'matter' includes the act, such as the bursting forth of water from between the fingers, for example, and the non-act, such as the non-burning of fire for Abraham, peace be upon him, for example. And we guarded by the condition of (accompanying the challenge) against the miracles of saints and the preparatory signs that precede the mission of the prophets, as a foundation for them, and against a liar taking the miracle of a past prophet as an argument for himself. And we guarded by the condition of (absence of opposition) against sorcery and jugglery.
Source pages p. 235

Commentary
This passage is a proof and a definition. Sanusi begins by providing the proof (burhān) for the necessary truthfulness (wujūb ṣidq) of the messengers. The argument is: if the messengers could lie, then God would be lying because He confirms them through miracles. Miracles are placed in the position of God saying 'My servant has spoken the truth', so if the messenger is false, God would be affirming a liar, which is impossible. God's speech is necessarily truthful. Sanusi then explains that miracles are extraordinary events (khāriq li-l-ʿāda) accompanied by a challenge (taḥaddī) and without opposition (ʿadam al-muʿāraḍa). He then refines the definition: using 'matter' (amr) instead of 'act' (fiʿl) to include non-acts like protection from fire. The conditions exclude saintly miracles (karāmāt), preparatory signs (irhāṣ), and any use of past miracles by impostors, as well as sorcery and jugglery which can be opposed.

Key Terms
برهان
صدق
معجزة

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi's proof, what would be the consequence if a messenger could lie?
A) The messenger would lose his miracle.
B) God would be lying because He affirms the messenger.
C) The miracle would be invalidated.
D) The messenger would be a sinner.

Key Takeaway
Miracles are divine endorsements that make messengers' truthfulness necessary; otherwise, Allah would be endorsing a lie.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Definition and Conditions of a Miracle
Sanusi defines miracle and states its conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the precise definition of a miracle (muʿjiza) and the conditions that distinguish it from similar phenomena.

Core Idea
A miracle is an extraordinary event with a challenge and no opposition.

After establishing the proof, Sanusi turns to the definition of a miracle. He refines the term, explains why 'matter' is preferred over 'act,' and then lists two key conditions: the miracle must be accompanied by a challenge (taḥaddī) and must face no opposition (ʿadam al-muʿāraḍa). These conditions distinguish true miracles from saintly miracles, preparatory signs, and sorcery.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on definition
Read the Arabic and translation for the definition of miracle and its conditions. Notice the technical terms.
2
Understand the choice of 'amr' over 'fiʿl'
Sanusi says 'amr' (matter) is better because it includes both acts and non-acts. Find the examples: water from fingers and fire not burning.
This is a refinement in terminology.
3
Learn the condition of challenge
The miracle must be accompanied by a challenge (taḥaddī). This excludes saintly miracles and preparatory signs, and prevents liars from using past miracles.
The phrase 'المقارنة للتحدي' is key.
4
Learn the condition of no opposition
The miracle must have no opposition. This distinguishes it from sorcery and jugglery, which can be countered.
The phrase 'عدم المعارضة' excludes these.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ صِدْقِهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ : فَلَأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ لَمْ يَصْدُقُوا لَلَزِمَ الْكَذِبُ فِي خَبَرِهِ تَعَالَى ؛ لِتَصْدِيقِهِ تَعَالَى لَهُمْ بِالْمُعْجِزَاتِ النَّازِلَةِ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى : صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي. هَذَا بُرْهَانُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ فِي دَعْوَاهُمُ الرِّسَالَةَ ، وَفِيمَا يُبَلِّغُونَهُ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ إِلَى الْخَلْقِ. وَحَاصِلُ هَذَا الْبُرْهَانِ : أَنَّ الْمُعْجِزَاتِ الَّتِي خَلَقَهَا اللَّهُ تَعَالَى عَلَى أَيْدِي الرُّسُلِ - وَهِيَ أَمْرٌ خَارِقٌ لِلْعَادَةِ ، مَقْرُونٌ بِالتَّحَدِّي ، مَعَ عَدَمِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ - تَتَنَزَّلُ مِنْ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ مَنْزِلَةَ قَوْلِهِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ : صَدَقَ عَبْدِي فِي كُلِّ مَا يُبَلِّغُ عَنِّي ، فَلَوْ جَازَ الْكَذِبُ عَلَى الرُّسُلِ لَجَازَ الْكَذِبُ عَلَيْهِ تَعَالَى ؛ إِذْ تَصْدِيقُ الْكَاذِبِ كَذِبٌ ، وَالْكَذِبُ عَلَى اللَّهِ تَعَالَى مُحَالٌ ؛ إِذْ خَبَرُهُ تَعَالَى عَلَى وَفْقِ عِلْمِهِ ، وَالْخَبَرُ عَلَى وَفْقِ الْعِلْمِ لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا صِدْقاً ، فَخَبَرُهُ تَعَالَى لَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا صِدْقاً . وَقَوْلُنَا فِي تَعْرِيفِ الْمُعْجِزَةِ : ( أَمْرٌ ) أَحْسَنُ مِنْ قَوْلِ بَعْضِهِمْ : ( فِعْلٌ ) ؛ لِأَنَّ الْأَمْرَ يَتَنَاوَلُ الْفِعْلَ ؛ كَانْفِجَارِ الْمَاءِ مَثَلاً مِنْ بَيْنِ الْأَصَابِعِ ، وَعَدَمَ الْفِعْلِ ؛ كَعَدَمِ إِحْرَاقِ النَّارِ مَثَلاً لِإِبْرَاهِيمَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ . وَاحْتَرَزْنَا بِقَيْدِ ( الْمُقَارَنَةِ لِلتَّحَدِّي ) عَنْ كَرَامَاتِ الْأَوْلِيَاءِ ، وَالْعَلَامَاتِ الْإِرْهَاصِيَّةِ الَّتِي تَتَقَدَّمُ بِعْثَةَ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ تَأْسِيساً لَهَا ، وَعَنْ أَنْ يَتَّخِذَ الْكَاذِبُ مُعْجِزَةَ مَنْ مَضَى حُجَّةً لِنَفْسِهِ . وَاحْتَرَزْنَا بِقَيْدِ ( عَدَمِ الْمُعَارَضَةِ ) عَنِ السِّحْرِ وَالشَّعْوَدَةِ .
As for the proof of the obligation of their truthfulness, peace and blessings be upon them: because if they were not truthful, then lying would be necessary in His report, may He be exalted, due to His, may He be exalted, affirming them through the miracles that take the place of His, may He be exalted, saying: 'My servant has spoken the truth in everything he conveys from Me.' This is the proof of the truthfulness of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, in their claim of prophethood and in what they convey thereafter to creation. The summary of this proof is that the miracles which Allah, may He be exalted, creates at the hands of the messengers — and they are a matter that breaks custom, accompanied by a challenge, with absence of opposition — take the place, from our Lord, may He be glorified and exalted, of His, may He be glorified and exalted, saying: 'My servant has spoken the truth in everything he conveys from Me.' So if lying were possible for the messengers, then lying would be possible for Him, may He be exalted; because affirming a liar is a lie. And lying against Allah, may He be exalted, is impossible; because His report, may He be exalted, conforms to His knowledge, and a report that conforms to knowledge is nothing but truth. So His report, may He be exalted, is nothing but truth. And our saying in the definition of miracle: (a matter) is better than the saying of some: (an act); because 'matter' includes the act, such as the bursting forth of water from between the fingers, for example, and the non-act, such as the non-burning of fire for Abraham, peace be upon him, for example. And we guarded by the condition of (accompanying the challenge) against the miracles of saints and the preparatory signs that precede the mission of the prophets, as a foundation for them, and against a liar taking the miracle of a past prophet as an argument for himself. And we guarded by the condition of (absence of opposition) against sorcery and jugglery.

This passage is a proof and a definition. Sanusi begins by providing the proof (burhān) for the necessary truthfulness (wujūb ṣidq) of the messengers. The argument is: if the messengers could lie, then God would be lying because He confirms them through miracles. ?

?

Repent if you have ever used your talents to compete with Allah's signs.

Excluding Karamat and Irhasat from Miracles
Sanusi excludes karamat, irhasat, and false claims from miracles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two conditions that distinguish a true miracle from saintly wonders, preparatory signs, and sorcery.

Core Idea
Not every supernatural event is a miracle; it must accompany a challenge and be unopposable.

Sanusi clarifies the precise definition of a miracle by excluding three types of extraordinary events that might be confused with it. The two conditions—'accompanying the challenge' and 'lack of opposition'—act as filters. This passage shows how careful theological reasoning distinguishes prophetic miracles from other phenomena.

Guided Path
1
Understand the two safeguards
The passage introduces two conditions that protect the definition of a miracle: accompanying the challenge and lack of opposition. Notice that each condition excludes specific phenomena.
2
First safeguard: accompanying the challenge
This condition excludes three things: wonders of saints (karamat), preparatory signs (irhasat), and a false claimant using a past miracle as his proof. Reflect on why each is excluded.
These lack a prophetic challenge (tahaddi) from the person performing them.
3
Second safeguard: lack of opposition
This condition excludes sorcery (sihr) and jugglery (shu'badha), because they can be opposed or replicated by others.
True miracles are inimitable and cannot be opposed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واحترزنا بقيد ( المقارنة للتحدّي ) عن كرامات الأولياء ، والعلامات الإرهاصيَّةِ التي تتقدَّمُ بعثة الأنبياء عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ تأسيساً لها ، وعن أنْ يَتَّخذ الكاذب معجزةَ مَنْ مضى حجَّةً لنفسِهِ . واحترزنا بقيد ( عدمِ المعارضة ) عن السحر والشعوذة .
We guarded by the condition of 'accompanying the challenge' against the wonders of the saints (karamat al-awliya') and the signs of foretelling (al-'alamat al-irhasiyya) that precede the mission of the prophets, peace and blessings be upon them, as a foundation for it, and against the false claimant taking the miracle of a past (prophet) as a proof for himself. And we guarded by the condition of 'lack of opposition' against sorcery and jugglery.
Source pages p. 236

Commentary
This passage is an explanation of the conditions that distinguish a miracle from other extraordinary events. The author lists two safeguards (ihtirazat). The first condition 'accompanying the challenge' (muqarana li-t-tahaddi) excludes three things: 1) karamat (wonders of saints) which are not accompanied by a claim of prophethood, 2) irhasat (preparatory signs) that occur before a prophet's mission, and 3) a false claimant using a previous prophet's miracle as his proof. The second condition 'lack of opposition' ('adam al-mu'arada) excludes sorcery (sihr) and jugglery (shu'badha), which are natural acts that can be opposed or replicated.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any supernatural event is a miracle.
Correction: Miracles require two conditions: accompanying a prophetic challenge and being unopposable. Saintly wonders (karamat) and preparatory signs (irhasat) lack the challenge, while sorcery can be opposed.

Key Takeaway

Meaning of Tahaddi and the King-Messenger Analogy
Sanusi defines tahaddi and illustrates with an analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of tahaddi and how the king-messenger analogy demonstrates that a miracle yields necessary knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
A miracle is like a king breaking habit to confirm his messenger.

Sanusi begins by defining tahaddi—the miraculous challenge—as a claim of a supernatural event as proof of truthfulness. He then presents a vivid analogy from the scholars: a man claims to be a king's messenger, and the king's unprecedented action confirms him. This analogy clarifies how miracles produce certain knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of tahaddi
Start by reading the opening sentence where Sanusi defines tahaddi. Notice that it involves a claim of a miraculous event as evidence for truthfulness, expressed either by the state (action) or by speech.
The term 'tahaddi' is central to discussions of prophethood.
2
Study the king-messenger analogy
Read the analogy carefully. A man stands before a king and claims to be his messenger. When asked for proof, he requests the king to break his habit (e.g., stand and sit three times). The king complies. Understand why this action confirms the messenger's truthfulness.
The analogy is designed to demonstrate how a miracle functions as proof.
3
Understand the role of tawatur
Sanusi emphasizes that necessary knowledge of truthfulness is not limited to eyewitnesses; those who receive the report through tawatur (mass transmission) also attain certainty. Reflect on why this is important for the preservation of prophetic miracles.
Tawatur ensures that later generations can be certain without direct observation.
4
Connect the analogy to prophethood
The passage concludes that this example perfectly matches the situation of the prophets. Consider how the miracle serves as a divine confirmation of the prophet's message, just as the king's action confirmed the messenger.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعنى التحدّي : دعوى الخارقِ دليلاً على الصدق ; إما بلسان الحالِ ، وإما بلسان المقال . وقد ضربَ العلماء لدعوى الرسولِ الرسالة وطلبه للمعجزة مِنَ اللهِ تعالى دليلاً على صدقِهِ . . مثالاً لتتضح بهِ دَلالتها على صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ ، ويُعلَمَ ذلك على الضرورة ; فقالوا : مثال ذلكَ : ما إذا قام رجلٌ في مجلس ملكِ بمرأى منه ومسمع بحضورِ جماعةٍ مِنَ الناسِ ، وادَّعى أنَّهُ رسولُ هذا الملكِ إليهم فطالبوه بالحُجَّةِ ، فقال : هي أن يخالف الملكُ عادته ويقوم عن سريرِهِ ويقعد ثلاثَ  َمرَّاتٍ مثلاً (۱) ، ففعلَ ، فلا شكَ أنَّ هذا الفعلَ مِنَ الملكِ على سبيل الإجابة للرسولِ تصديق له ، ومفيد للعلم الضروري بصدقِهِ بلا ارتياب ، ونازل منزلة قولِهِ : صدق هذا الإنسانُ في كلّ ما يبلِّغُ عنِّي . ولا فرق في حصولِ العلم الضروري بصدْقِ ذلكَ الرسولِ بينَ مَنْ شاهدَ ذلكَ الفعلَ مِنَ الملكِ ، ومَنْ لم يشاهدُهُ إِلا أَنَّهُ بلَغَهُ بالتواتر خبر ذلك الفعل ، ولا شك في مطابقة هذا المثالِ لحالِ الرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام .
The meaning of challenge (tahaddi) is the claim of the miraculous as evidence for truthfulness, either by the tongue of the state or by the tongue of speech. The scholars have set for the claim of the messenger of the message and his request for a miracle from Allah as evidence for his truthfulness... an example to clarify its indication of the truthfulness of the messengers, and that it is known necessarily. They said: An example of that is the case of a man standing in the court of a king in his sight and hearing, in the presence of a group of people, and he claims that he is the messenger of this king to them. They demand a proof from him, so he says: 'It is that the king should violate his habit and stand up from his throne and sit down three times, for example.' He does so. There is no doubt that this action from the king, in response to the messenger, is a confirmation of him, and it yields necessary knowledge of his truthfulness without any doubt. It takes the place of his saying: 'This man is truthful in everything he conveys from me.' And there is no difference in the attainment of necessary knowledge of the truthfulness of that messenger between one who witnessed that action from the king and one who did not witness it but only received the report of that action through tawatur (mass transmission). And there is no doubt that this example matches the condition of the messengers, peace and blessings be upon them.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage first defines tahaddi (challenge) as the claim of a miraculous event as proof of truthfulness. Then it presents a famous analogy from the scholars to demonstrate how a miracle necessitates knowledge of the prophet's truthfulness. The analogy: a man claims to be a king's messenger; his requested proof is that the king breaks his habit (a small action). The king's compliance leaves no doubt that the man is truthful. The author emphasizes that this yields 'necessary knowledge' ('ilm daruri). Importantly, this necessary knowledge is not limited to direct witnesses; those who receive the report via tawatur (mass transmission) also attain certainty. The analogy perfectly fits the situation of prophets.

Key Terms
تحدّي
خارق
علم ضروري
تواتر
تصديق

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only eyewitnesses can be certain of a prophet's truthfulness.
Correction: The passage states that those who receive the report through tawatur also attain necessary knowledge of the messenger's truthfulness.

Checkpoint
According to the analogy, what does the king's action in response to the messenger demonstrate?
A) The king's power.
B) The messenger's cleverness.
C) The truthfulness of the messenger.
D) The habit of the king.

Key Takeaway
The king-messenger analogy shows that a miracle (khariq) confirms a prophet's truthfulness just as the king's action confirms the messenger, and this certainty is conveyed to all who hear the report through tawatur.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about a miracle in the Quran or Sunnah, do you feel the same level of certainty as if you had witnessed it yourself? What prevents you from having that certainty, and what would it take for you to attain it?
?
If you were to claim something on behalf of Allah, would you dare to ask for a sign to confirm your truthfulness? What does that say about your own certainty and awareness of divine accountability?
?
How does the king-messenger analogy affect your view of the Prophet's miracles? Do you accept them as necessary knowledge that leaves no room for doubt, or do you hesitate? Reflect on the consequences of that hesitation.

Jugglery and Sorcery: Natural, Not Miraculous
Sanusi defines jugglery and sorcery as natural phenomena

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why jugglery and sorcery are not considered miracles, as they rely on learnable natural causes.

Core Idea
Only the unopposable is miraculous; what can be learned is not.

In this passage, Sanusi clarifies the boundaries of miracles by defining two phenomena often mistaken for them: jugglery and sorcery. Both involve surprising transformations, but they are rooted in natural causes that can be taught and opposed. Understanding this distinction is essential for recognizing the true nature of prophetic miracles.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once without analysing. Let the definitions sink in.
2
Identify the two phenomena
Notice that Sanusi gives separate definitions for shu'badha and sihr. How are they similar? How do they differ?
Both are based on natural causes that can be learned.
3
Understand the exclusion from miracles
The key point: because these phenomena can be learned and opposed, they do not qualify as miracles. Reflect on why this matters for proving prophethood.
This connects back to the condition that miracles cannot be opposed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم الشعوذة - ويقال : الشعبذة - : خفة في اليد تُري الشيء على خلاف ما هو عليه ، وأما السحر فإنه وإن وقع فيه قلب للصورة ، وأثبتنا له حقيقةً ; إلا أنه يكون كما سبق بسبب عادي يمكن تعلمه
Then shu'badha (juggling) - it is also said: shu'badha - is lightness of hand that shows a thing contrary to what it is. As for sorcery (sihr), although it involves transformation of form and we affirm a reality for it, it occurs as previously mentioned by natural causes that can be learned.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage defines two phenomena that are excluded from miracles by the condition of lack of opposition. Shu'badha (juggling) is simply sleight of hand. Sihr (sorcery) is more serious: the author affirms that it involves actual transformation of forms and has a real existence. However, both are ultimately based on natural causes that can be learned and thus can be opposed or replicated. This distinguishes them from true miracles, which are unopposable.

Key Terms
شعوذة
سحر
عادة
تعلم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think sorcery is a miracle because it involves supernatural transformation of forms.
Correction: Although sorcery produces real changes, it is based on natural causes that can be learned, and therefore it can be opposed. Miracles are unopposable and come only from Allah through prophets.

Checkpoint
What distinguishes sorcery from a miracle according to Sanusi?
A) Sorcery is not real.
B) Sorcery cannot be learned.
C) Sorcery occurs by natural causes that can be learned and opposed.
D) Sorcery is a form of jugglery.

Key Takeaway
Jugglery and sorcery, though surprising, are based on learnable natural causes and thus are not miracles.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you witness something extraordinary, do you first seek a natural explanation, or are you quick to call it a miracle? How might this lesson correct your instinct?
?
Have you ever been impressed by someone's 'spiritual gifts' without examining whether they could be learned or natural? Will you now test such claims against the criterion of opposition?
?
If sorcery is real but natural, does that make it less dangerous? How does this knowledge affect your reliance on Allah versus your fear of evil?

Tahaddi: How Miracles Prove Prophethood
Defines tahaddi and provides a royal court analogy.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the meaning of tahaddi and how the example of a king's act illustrates that miracles provide necessary knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness.

Core Idea
Miracles are divine endorsements that produce certainty in the prophet's message.

This passage from Sanusi's work introduces the concept of tahaddi (challenge) and uses a powerful analogy to clarify how miracles function as definitive proofs of prophethood. Before reading the source, consider how a public demonstration of extraordinary acts can establish credibility beyond doubt.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of tahaddi
The passage opens by defining tahaddi as the claim of a miraculous act as evidence of truthfulness. Note the two forms: by language of state or speech.
2
Study the king's court analogy
Read the example carefully: a man claims to be a king's messenger and requests the king to break his habit by rising and sitting three times. The king's compliance serves as confirmation.
The three times is to avoid the suspicion of coincidence; even once would suffice.
3
Understand necessary knowledge and tawatur
The author asserts that the king's act yields necessary knowledge (al-ilm al-daruri) of the man's truthfulness. This knowledge is available both to witnesses and to those who receive the report via tawatur (mass transmission).
Tawatur ensures certainty even without direct observation.
4
Reflect on the theological conclusion
The example mirrors the situation of the prophets. Those who doubt them are described as having hearts sealed by Allah. Consider why this analogy is so compelling.
This shows that miracles are a universal proof for all people.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومعنى التحدّي : دعوى الخارقِ دليلاً على الصدق ؛ إما بلسان الحالِ ، وإما بلسان المقال وقد ضربَ العلماء لدعوى الرسولِ الرسالة وطلبه للمعجزة مِنَ اللهِ تعالى دليلاً على صدقِهِ . . مثالاً لتتضح بهِ دَلالتها على صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ ، ويُعلَمَ ذلك على الضرورة ؛ فقالوا : مثال ذلكَ : ما إذا قام رجلٌ في مجلس ملكِ بمرأى منه ومسمع بحضورِ جماعةٍ مِنَ الناسِ ، وادَّعى أنَّهُ رسولُ هذا الملكِ إليهم فطالبوه بالحُجَّةِ ، فقال : هي أن يخالف الملكُ عادته ويقوم عن سريرِهِ ويقعد ثلاثَ  َمرَّاتٍ مثلاً (۱) ، ففعلَ ، فلا شكَ أنَّ هذا الفعلَ مِنَ الملكِ على سبيل الإجابة للرسولِ تصديق له ، ومفيد للعلم الضروري بصدقِهِ بلا ارتياب ، ونازل منزلة قولِهِ : صدق هذا الإنسانُ في كلّ ما يبلِّغُ عنِّي ولا فرق في حصولِ العلم الضروري بصدْقِ ذلكَ الرسولِ بينَ مَنْ شاهدَ ذلكَ الفعلَ مِنَ الملكِ ، ومَنْ لم يشاهدُهُ إِلا أَنَّهُ بلَغَهُ بالتواتر خبر ذلك الفعل ، ولا شك في مطابقة هذا المثالِ لحالِ الرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، فلا يرتابُ في صدقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام إلا مَنْ طبع الله على قلبه والعياذ بالله تعالى (۱) قيد الثلاث لدفع شبهة القيام لعارض ، وإلا فهي متحققة بالمرة
The meaning of tahaddi (challenge) is: the claim of the miraculous act as proof of truthfulness; either by the language of the state or by the language of speech. And the scholars have set for the claim of the messenger of the message and his request for a miracle from Allah Almighty as proof of his truthfulness... an example to clarify its evidence for the truthfulness of the messengers, and so that it be known necessarily. They said: An example of that is: when a man stands in the assembly of a king within his sight and hearing, in the presence of a group of people, and claims that he is the messenger of this king to them, and they demand from him proof, so he says: 'It is that the king go against his habit and rise from his throne and sit three times, for example' (1), and he does so. Then there is no doubt that this action of the king in response to the messenger is a confirmation of him, and it yields necessary knowledge of his truthfulness without any hesitation, and it is in the position of him saying: 'This man is truthful in everything he conveys from me.' And there is no difference in the attainment of necessary knowledge of the truthfulness of that messenger between one who witnessed that action of the king and one who did not witness it except that it reached him via tawatur (mass transmission) the report of that action. And there is no doubt about the correspondence of this example to the situation of the messengers, peace be upon them, so none doubts their truthfulness except one whose heart Allah has sealed, and we seek refuge in Allah. (1) The qualifier 'three times' is to repel the suspicion that the standing was for an incidental reason; otherwise it is actualized even with one time.
Source pages p. 237

Commentary
This passage defines tahaddi (challenge) and provides a vivid analogy to explain how miracles function as proofs of prophethood. The author begins by stating that tahaddi is the claim of a miraculous act as evidence of truthfulness, either implicitly (bi-lisan al-hal) or explicitly (bi-lisan al-maqal). Then he presents an example crafted by scholars: a man claims to be a king's messenger in the king's presence and asks for a sign—the king breaking his habit by rising and sitting three times. When the king does so, it is a direct confirmation of the man's claim, yielding necessary knowledge (al-ilm al-daruri) of his truthfulness without doubt. The author emphasizes that this necessary knowledge is attained not only by those who witness the act but also by those who receive it via tawatur (mass transmission). He then declares that this example perfectly mirrors the situation of the prophets, and no one doubts them except those whose hearts are sealed. A footnote explains that the specification of three times is to avoid the suspicion that the king stood for a random reason; even one time would suffice. The passage establishes that miracles are a definitive proof for prophethood, accessible through direct observation or reliable report.

Key Terms
التحدّي
الخارق
العلم الضروري
التواتر
الرسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only those who directly witness a miracle can be certain of a prophet's truthfulness.
Correction: The author explains that necessary knowledge is also attained through tawatur (mass transmission) of the miracle report.

Checkpoint
According to the example, what does the king's act of rising and sitting three times demonstrate?
A) The king's power over his subjects.
B) The truthfulness of the man's claim to be a messenger.
C) The king's habit of changing his routine.
D) The man's skill in persuading the king.

Key Takeaway
Miracles, like a king's extraordinary act confirming a messenger, provide certain knowledge of a prophet's truthfulness, accessible through observation or reliable report.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you have that 'necessary knowledge' about the Prophet Muhammad's miracles, or do you only give intellectual assent without conviction? If the latter, what concrete step will you take today to seek that certainty?
?
The king's act was a direct visible response. Are you looking for the direct responses of Allah to His messengers in your own life—through the Quran, the sunna, or the state of the believers? How will you respond when you see His signs?
?
The passage says only sealed hearts doubt the prophets. Search your heart: is there any lingering doubt about the truthfulness of the Prophet that you have not confronted? What will you do this week to remove that doubt through study, du'a, or sincere reflection?

The Proof of Prophetic Trustworthiness
Sanusi proves the obligation of trustworthiness and delivery for prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof for why prophets must be completely trustworthy in conveying the message.

Core Idea
Prophets cannot betray trust, else following them would command sin.

This lesson examines a concise yet powerful proof from Imam Sanusi showing that prophets are necessarily trustworthy. The argument hinges on the divine command to follow prophets in all their words and deeds. If prophets could commit forbidden acts, then those acts would become required – an impossibility for a just God.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage once
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get the overall flow. Notice the conditional structure and the Quranic citations.
The passage starts with 'As for the proof...'
2
Understand the conditional argument
Identify the 'if-then' logic: if prophets betrayed, then their forbidden acts would become obedience because Allah commands us to follow them.
3
Explore the scriptural evidence
Look at the cited verses that command following the Prophet. Note that the command is general, except for matters unique to him.
The verses support the premise that we are commanded to follow.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Understand that this proof establishes both trustworthiness and 'the third' (likely delivery). Ask yourself why this is convincing.
The conclusion is that prophets cannot commit forbidden or disliked acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الْأَمَانَةِ لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : فَلَأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ خَانُوا بِفِعْلِ مُحَرَّمِ أَوْ مَكْرُوهِ لَانْقَلَبَ الْمُحَرَّمُ أَوِ الْمَكْرُوهُ طَاعَةٌ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ ؛ لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى قَدْ أَمَرَنَا بِالِاقْتِدَاءِ بِهِمْ فِي أَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ ، وَلا يَأْمُرُ تَعَالَى بِمُحَرَّمٍ وَلَا مَكْرُوهِ ، وَهَذَا بِعَيْنِهِ هُوَ بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الثَّالِثِ .
لا شَكَّ أَنَّ الرُّسُلَ عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ أُمرنا بالاقتداء بهم في أقوالهم وأفعالهم ، إلا ما ثبت اختصاصهم بهِ عن أممِهم ، قالَ الله تعالى في حق نبينا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ﴿ قُلْ إِن كُنتُم تُحِبُّونَ اللَّهَ فَاتَّبِعُونِي يُحْبِبْكُمُ اللَّهُ ﴾ [آل عمران : ٣١] ، وقال تعالى : ﴿ وَاتَّبِعُوهُ ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٥٨] ، وقال تعالى : ﴿ وَرَحْمَتِي وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَسَأَكْتُبُهَا لِلَّذِينَ يَتَّقُونَ وَيُؤْتُونَ الزَّكَاةَ وَالَّذِينَ هُمْ بِآيَاتِنَا يُؤْمِنُونَ * الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الْأُمِّيَّ ﴾ [الأعراف : ١٥٦ - ١٥٧]، إلى غير ذلكَ ممَّا يطولُ تتبعه . وقد عُلِمَ مِنْ دِينِ الصَّحَابَةِ ضَرُورَةَ اتِّبَاعِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ
As for the proof of the obligation of trustworthiness (al-amānah) for them, upon them be prayers and peace: it is that if they were to betray by doing something forbidden (muḥarram) or disliked (makrūh), then the forbidden or disliked would become an act of obedience (ṭā‘ah) in their case, upon them be prayers and peace; because Allah the Exalted has commanded us to follow them in their words and deeds, and the Exalted does not command what is forbidden or disliked. And this very same is the proof of the obligation of the third. There is no doubt that the messengers, upon them be prayers and peace, we have been commanded to follow them in their words and deeds, except what is established as specific to them as opposed to their communities. Allah the Exalted said concerning our Prophet and master Muḥammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: “Say, if you love Allah, then follow me, Allah will love you” (Āl ‘Imrān 31); and He said: “And follow him” (al-A‘rāf 158); and He said: “And My mercy encompasses all things, and I will prescribe it for those who are righteous and give zakāh and those who believe in Our signs – those who follow the Messenger, the unlettered Prophet” (al-A‘rāf 156-157); and other verses too numerous to trace. And it is known from the religion of the Companions, by necessity, the obligation of following him, upon him be prayers and peace.
Source pages p. 238

Commentary
This passage presents a proof (burhān) for the obligation of trustworthiness (amānah) and delivery (tablīgh) upon prophets. The proof is structured as a conditional argument: if prophets were to betray by committing a forbidden or disliked act, then that forbidden or disliked act would, in their case, become an act of obedience. Why? Because Allah has commanded us to follow them in all their words and deeds. Since Allah never commands what is forbidden or disliked, it follows that prophets cannot commit such acts—otherwise, we would be commanded to commit them through following the prophets, which is impossible. The same argument is said to prove the 'third' (likely the obligation of delivery or another attribute). The author then reinforces this by citing Quranic verses commanding obedience to the Prophet, noting that this command is general except for matters unique to him. The proof concludes by stating that the Companions' practice of following the Prophet was a matter of necessary knowledge (ḍarūrah) in their religion.

Key Terms
برهان
أمانة
تبليغ
اقتداء
محرم
مكروه
طاعة
رسل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the logical consequence if a prophet were to commit a forbidden act?
A) The act remains forbidden for everyone.
B) The act would become obedience because Allah commands us to follow them.
C) The prophet would lose prophethood.
D) The act would be forgiven automatically.

Key Takeaway
Prophets cannot commit forbidden or disliked acts because Allah commands us to follow them, and commanding forbidden acts is impossible for Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This proof shows that following the Prophet perfectly leads only to good. When you choose to follow your own desires over his example, what does that imply about your trust in Allah’s command to follow him? Will you this week identify one habit where you prefer your own way over his and replace it?
?
If you truly believe the Prophet never did anything disliked, then every action of his is a model. Think of the last time you said, 'That's just his culture' or 'That's not required.' How would viewing his every action as a model change your daily choices? Commit to one small sunnah you have been ignoring for the next seven days.
?
The proof is simple: a prophet cannot sin because obeying him would then be sinning. Does your obedience to the Prophet reflect that conviction, or is it selective? What area of your life do you keep outside his guidance, and what would it cost you to bring it under his sunnah today?

The Logical Proof for Prophetic Trustworthiness
Sanusi proves prophetic trustworthiness via logical reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical proof that prophets must be trustworthy (sinless) because if they sinned, their sin would become an obligatory act of obedience for us, which is impossible since Allah does not command sin.

Core Idea
A prophet's sin would make sin obligatory – impossible.

Sanusi presents a crisp reductio ad absurdum argument to prove that prophets cannot commit sins. The argument hinges entirely on the command to follow them: if they did something forbidden, we would have to follow it, turning sin into obedience. This would contradict Allah's nature, so prophets must be sinless. This same reasoning also proves they must deliver the message faithfully.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Let the logical structure become apparent.
2
Identify the logical steps
Identify the assumption (prophet sins), the consequence (we follow), and the contradiction (Allah commands sin).
3
Reflect on the third obligation
Notice that Sanusi says the same proof applies to the third obligation (delivering the message). Ask yourself why.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الْأَمَانَةِ لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : فَلَأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ خَانُوا بِفِعْلِ مُحَرَّمِ أَوْ مَكْرُوهِ لَانْقَلَبَ الْمُحَرَّمُ أَوِ الْمَكْرُوهُ طَاعَةٌ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ ؛ لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى قَدْ أَمَرَنَا بِالِاقْتِدَاءِ بِهِمْ فِي أَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ ، وَلا يَأْمُرُ تَعَالَى بِمُحَرَّمٍ وَلَا مَكْرُوهِ ، وَهَذَا بِعَيْنِهِ هُوَ بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الثَّالِثِ .

لا شَكَّ أَنَّ الرُّسُلَ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ أُمِرْنَا بِالِاقْتِدَاءِ بِهِمْ فِي أَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ، إِلَّا مَا ثَبَتَ اخْتِصَاصُهُمْ بِهِ عَنْ أُمَمِهِمْ، قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى فِي حَقِّ نَبِيِّنَا وَمَوْلَانَا مُحَمَّدٍ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: ﴿ قُلْ إِنْ كُنْتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ اللَّهَ فَاتَّبِعُونِي يُحْبِبْكُمُ اللَّهُ ﴾ [آل عمران: 31]، وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿ وَاتَّبِعُوهُ ﴾ [الأعراف: 158]، وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿ وَرَحْمَتِي وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَسَأَكْتُبُهَا لِلَّذِينَ يَتَّقُونَ وَيُؤْتُونَ الزَّكَاةَ وَالَّذِينَ هُمْ بِآيَاتِنَا يُؤْمِنُونَ * الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الْأُمِّيَّ ﴾ [الأعراف: 156-157]، إِلَى غَيْرِ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا يَطُولُ تَتَبُّعُهُ. وَقَدْ عُلِمَ مِنْ دِينِ الصَّحَابَةِ ضَرُورَةَ اتِّبَاعِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ مِنْ غَيْرِ تَوَقُّفٍ وَلَا نَظَرٍ أَصْلًا فِي جَمِيعِ أَقْوَالِهِ وَأَفْعَالِهِ، إِلَّا مَا قَامَ فِيهِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى اخْتِصَاصِهِ بِهِ؛ فَقَدْ خَلَعُوا نِعَالَهُمْ لَمَّا خَلَعَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ نَعْلَهُ، وَنَزَعُوا خَوَاتِمَهُمْ لَمَّا نَزَعَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ خَاتَمَهُ، وَحَسَرَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرُ رَضِيَ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُمَا عَنْ رُكْبَتَيْهِمَا فِي قِصَّةِ جُلُوسِهِمْ عَلَى الْبِئْرِ كَمَا فَعَلَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ، وَكَادَ يَقْتُلُ بَعْضُهُمْ بَعْضًا مِنْ شِدَّةِ الِازْدِحَامِ عَلَى الْحِلَاقِ عِنْدَمَا رَأَوْهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ يَحْلِقُ رَأْسَهُ وَحَلَّ مِنْ عُمْرَتِهِ فِي قَضِيَّةِ الْحُدَيْبِيَةِ، وَكَانُوا يَبْحَثُونَ الْبَحْثَ الْعَظِيمَ عَنْ هَيْئَةِ جُلُوسِهِ وَنَوْمِهِ وَكَيْفِيَّةِ أَكْلِهِ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ؛ لِيَقْتَدُوا بِهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، حَتَّى أَنْزَلُوا أَنْفُسَهُمْ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمْ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْأَطْفَالِ فِي حَجْرِ أَبِيهِمْ؛ هُوَ يَرْعَاهُمْ وَيَكْلَؤُهُمْ، وَهُمْ يَتَعَلَّمُونَ مِنْهُ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ.
As for the proof of the obligation of trustworthiness for them, upon them be prayer and peace: it is that if they betrayed by committing something forbidden or disliked, then the forbidden or disliked would turn into an act of obedience in their regard, upon them be prayer and peace; because Allah the Exalted has commanded us to follow them in their sayings and actions, and the Exalted does not command the forbidden nor the disliked. And this itself is the proof of the obligation of the third.

There is no doubt that the messengers, upon them be prayer and peace, were given the command that we follow them in their sayings and actions, except what is established of their exclusivity from their nations. Allah the Exalted said concerning our Prophet and master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: 'Say: If you love Allah, follow me, Allah will love you' [Aal 'Imran 3:31]. And the Exalted said: 'And follow him' [al-A'raf 7:158]. And the Exalted said: 'And My mercy encompasses all things, so I will prescribe it for those who are righteous and give zakah and those who believe in Our signs, who follow the unlettered prophet' [al-A'raf 7:156-157], and other verses too numerous to trace. And it is known from the religion of the Companions, by necessity, the following of him, upon him be prayer and peace, without hesitation and without any consideration at all, in all of his sayings and actions, except what there was evidence for his exclusivity in it. For they removed their sandals when he, upon him be prayer and peace, removed his sandal; and they took off their rings when he, upon him be prayer and peace, took off his ring; and Abu Bakr and 'Umar, may Allah the Exalted be pleased with them, uncovered their knees in the story of their sitting at the well as he, upon him be prayer and peace, did; and some of them almost killed others due to the intensity of the crowding for shaving when they saw him, upon him be prayer and peace, shave his head and he had completed his 'umrah in the matter of al-Hudaybiyyah; and they would make great inquiries about the manner of his sitting, his sleeping, how he ate, and other things, in order to follow him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace; until they placed themselves, may Allah be pleased with them, in the position of children in the lap of their father; he cares for them and protects them, and they learn everything from him.
Source pages p. 239

Commentary
This passage is a proof (burhan) for the obligation of trustworthiness (al-amanah) in prophets, and by extension the obligation of delivering the message (al-tabligh, referred to as 'the third'). The argument follows a reductio ad absurdum: if a prophet were to commit a sin (forbidden or disliked), then that action, because we are commanded to follow the prophet in all his sayings and actions, would become an act of obedience for us. But Allah, the Exalted, does not command what is forbidden or disliked. Therefore, a prophet cannot sin. The same reasoning applies to the third obligation, likely the delivery of the message.

The author then provides extensive scriptural and historical evidence that the command to follow the prophets is universal. He cites Qur'anic verses commanding the following of the Prophet Muhammad, such as 'Say: If you love Allah, follow me' (3:31) and 'And follow him' (7:158), and the description of believers as those who follow the unlettered prophet (7:156-157). He then points to the practice of the Companions, which demonstrates a necessary, unhesitating following of the Prophet in all his actions, except where evidence indicated exclusivity. Specific examples include: removing their sandals when he removed his, taking off their rings when he did, Abu Bakr and 'Umar uncovering their knees when he did, and crowding to be shaved when he shaved his head during the 'umrah of al-Hudaybiyyah. The Companions even investigated the details of his sitting, sleeping, and eating to imitate him. This shows that they considered following him in all matters obligatory, placing themselves like children learning from their father.

Key Terms
الأمانة
الاقتداء
الثالث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The proof for trustworthiness is different from the proof for delivering the message.
Correction: Sanusi states that the very same proof establishes the obligation of the third (tabligh) as well.

Checkpoint
What would happen if a prophet committed a forbidden or disliked act according to the proof?
A) He would be forgiven.
B) The act would become an act of obedience for us.
C) We would not follow him.
D) Allah would command it.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of prophetic trustworthiness is proven by the impossibility of Allah commanding sin through the command to follow the prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you identify a moment today when you followed someone's opinion over a clear command of Allah? What does this lesson's logic reveal about the danger of following anyone other than the sinless prophets?
?
The proof shows that if a prophet could sin, following them would make sin obligatory. How does this challenge your assumption that you can follow religious leaders without verifying their sinlessness? What will you do to ensure your allegiance is only to those who are infallible in conveying Allah's message?
?
This proof forces you to confront: if you claim to follow the Prophet (saw), but your actions include things he would never do, are you truly following? What specific action will you repent from today to align your following with the logical conclusion of this argument?

Prophethood
intermediate
5 min
The Obligation to Follow the Prophet in All Matters
Sanusi provides scriptural and historical evidence for the comprehensive obligation to follow the prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand from Qur'anic verses and the practice of the Companions that following the Prophet is obligatory in all sayings and actions, except where exclusivity is proven.

Core Idea
The Companions imitated the Prophet in every detail.

After proving that prophets must be trustworthy, Sanusi now turns to the evidence that we are commanded to follow them in everything. He cites key Qur'anic verses and then describes the remarkable behavior of the Companions, who literally imitated the Prophet in actions like removing sandals, taking off rings, and even how he sat. This shows that the command to follow is comprehensive, covering all aspects of life.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the translation. Notice the structure: statement, verses, examples.
2
Identify the Qur'anic verses
List the three verses cited and what they command regarding following the Prophet.
3
Examine the Companion examples
Look at each example: sandals, rings, knees, shaving, inquiries about sitting/sleeping/eating. What do they show?
4
Reflect on the principle of exclusivity
Note the exception: matters exclusive to the prophet. How does that nuance the obligation?

وَأَمَّا بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الْأَمَانَةِ لَهُمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ : فَلَأَنَّهُمْ لَوْ خَانُوا بِفِعْلِ مُحَرَّمِ أَوْ مَكْرُوهِ لَانْقَلَبَ الْمُحَرَّمُ أَوِ الْمَكْرُوهُ طَاعَةٌ فِي حَقِّهِمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ ؛ لِأَنَّ اللهَ تَعَالَى قَدْ أَمَرَنَا بِالِاقْتِدَاءِ بِهِمْ فِي أَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ ، وَلا يَأْمُرُ تَعَالَى بِمُحَرَّمٍ وَلَا مَكْرُوهِ ، وَهَذَا بِعَيْنِهِ هُوَ بُرْهَانُ وُجُوبِ الثَّالِثِ .

لا شَكَّ أَنَّ الرُّسُلَ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ أُمِرْنَا بِالِاقْتِدَاءِ بِهِمْ فِي أَقْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ، إِلَّا مَا ثَبَتَ اخْتِصَاصُهُمْ بِهِ عَنْ أُمَمِهِمْ، قَالَ اللهُ تَعَالَى فِي حَقِّ نَبِيِّنَا وَمَوْلَانَا مُحَمَّدٍ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ: ﴿ قُلْ إِنْ كُنْتُمْ تُحِبُّونَ اللَّهَ فَاتَّبِعُونِي يُحْبِبْكُمُ اللَّهُ ﴾ [آل عمران: 31]، وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿ وَاتَّبِعُوهُ ﴾ [الأعراف: 158]، وَقَالَ تَعَالَى: ﴿ وَرَحْمَتِي وَسِعَتْ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ فَسَأَكْتُبُهَا لِلَّذِينَ يَتَّقُونَ وَيُؤْتُونَ الزَّكَاةَ وَالَّذِينَ هُمْ بِآيَاتِنَا يُؤْمِنُونَ * الَّذِينَ يَتَّبِعُونَ الرَّسُولَ النَّبِيَّ الْأُمِّيَّ ﴾ [الأعراف: 156-157]، إِلَى غَيْرِ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا يَطُولُ تَتَبُّعُهُ. وَقَدْ عُلِمَ مِنْ دِينِ الصَّحَابَةِ ضَرُورَةَ اتِّبَاعِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ مِنْ غَيْرِ تَوَقُّفٍ وَلَا نَظَرٍ أَصْلًا فِي جَمِيعِ أَقْوَالِهِ وَأَفْعَالِهِ، إِلَّا مَا قَامَ فِيهِ دَلِيلٌ عَلَى اخْتِصَاصِهِ بِهِ؛ فَقَدْ خَلَعُوا نِعَالَهُمْ لَمَّا خَلَعَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ نَعْلَهُ، وَنَزَعُوا خَوَاتِمَهُمْ لَمَّا نَزَعَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ خَاتَمَهُ، وَحَسَرَ أَبُو بَكْرٍ وَعُمَرُ رَضِيَ اللهُ تَعَالَى عَنْهُمَا عَنْ رُكْبَتَيْهِمَا فِي قِصَّةِ جُلُوسِهِمْ عَلَى الْبِئْرِ كَمَا فَعَلَ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ، وَكَادَ يَقْتُلُ بَعْضُهُمْ بَعْضًا مِنْ شِدَّةِ الِازْدِحَامِ عَلَى الْحِلَاقِ عِنْدَمَا رَأَوْهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ يَحْلِقُ رَأْسَهُ وَحَلَّ مِنْ عُمْرَتِهِ فِي قَضِيَّةِ الْحُدَيْبِيَةِ، وَكَانُوا يَبْحَثُونَ الْبَحْثَ الْعَظِيمَ عَنْ هَيْئَةِ جُلُوسِهِ وَنَوْمِهِ وَكَيْفِيَّةِ أَكْلِهِ وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ؛ لِيَقْتَدُوا بِهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ، حَتَّى أَنْزَلُوا أَنْفُسَهُمْ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمْ بِمَنْزِلَةِ الْأَطْفَالِ فِي حَجْرِ أَبِيهِمْ؛ هُوَ يَرْعَاهُمْ وَيَكْلَؤُهُمْ، وَهُمْ يَتَعَلَّمُونَ مِنْهُ كُلَّ شَيْءٍ.
As for the proof of the obligation of trustworthiness for them, upon them be prayer and peace: it is that if they betrayed by committing something forbidden or disliked, then the forbidden or disliked would turn into an act of obedience in their regard, upon them be prayer and peace; because Allah the Exalted has commanded us to follow them in their sayings and actions, and the Exalted does not command the forbidden nor the disliked. And this itself is the proof of the obligation of the third.

There is no doubt that the messengers, upon them be prayer and peace, were given the command that we follow them in their sayings and actions, except what is established of their exclusivity from their nations. Allah the Exalted said concerning our Prophet and master Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace: 'Say: If you love Allah, follow me, Allah will love you' [Aal 'Imran 3:31]. And the Exalted said: 'And follow him' [al-A'raf 7:158]. And the Exalted said: 'And My mercy encompasses all things, so I will prescribe it for those who are righteous and give zakah and those who believe in Our signs, who follow the unlettered prophet' [al-A'raf 7:156-157], and other verses too numerous to trace. And it is known from the religion of the Companions, by necessity, the following of him, upon him be prayer and peace, without hesitation and without any consideration at all, in all of his sayings and actions, except what there was evidence for his exclusivity in it. For they removed their sandals when he, upon him be prayer and peace, removed his sandal; and they took off their rings when he, upon him be prayer and peace, took off his ring; and Abu Bakr and 'Umar, may Allah the Exalted be pleased with them, uncovered their knees in the story of their sitting at the well as he, upon him be prayer and peace, did; and some of them almost killed others due to the intensity of the crowding for shaving when they saw him, upon him be prayer and peace, shave his head and he had completed his 'umrah in the matter of al-Hudaybiyyah; and they would make great inquiries about the manner of his sitting, his sleeping, how he ate, and other things, in order to follow him, may Allah bless him and grant him peace; until they placed themselves, may Allah be pleased with them, in the position of children in the lap of their father; he cares for them and protects them, and they learn everything from him.

Commentary
This passage is a proof (burhan) for the obligation of trustworthiness (al-amanah) in prophets, and by extension the obligation of delivering the message (al-tabligh, referred to as 'the third'). The argument follows a reductio ad absurdum: if a prophet were to commit a sin (forbidden or disliked), then that action, because we are commanded to follow the prophet in all his sayings and actions, would become an act of obedience for us. But Allah, the Exalted, does not command what is forbidden or disliked. Therefore, a prophet cannot sin. The same reasoning applies to the third obligation, likely the delivery of the message.

The author then provides extensive scriptural and historical evidence that the command to follow the prophets is universal. He cites Qur'anic verses commanding the following of the Prophet Muhammad, such as 'Say: If you love Allah, follow me' (3:31) and 'And follow him' (7:158), and the description of believers as those who follow the unlettered prophet (7:156-157). He then points to the practice of the Companions, which demonstrates a necessary, unhesitating following of the Prophet in all his actions, except where evidence indicated exclusivity. Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The command to follow applies only to religious matters, not personal actions.
Correction: The Comapnions followed him in personal actions like removing sandals and sleeping, showing the command is comprehensive.

Checkpoint
What did the Companions do when the Prophet removed his sandals?
A) They asked why.
B) They also removed their sandals.
C) They ignored it.
D) They prayed.

Key Takeaway
The command to follow the Prophet is all-encompassing, covering every aspect of life, as shown by the Qur'an and the Companions' practice.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The Companions removed their sandals when the Prophet did, without asking 'why'. When have you hesitated to follow a sunnah because it seemed small or inconvenient? What does that hesitation show about your love for the Prophet?
?
If you were as eager to learn from the Prophet as the Companions were—searching for how he sat, slept, and ate—what is one specific habit you would change starting today?
?
The Companions nearly killed each other in their rush to be shaved in imitation of the Prophet. Is there any action of the Prophet that you would be willing to inconvenience yourself for in that way? If not, what might be holding you back?

Prophethood
intermediate
8 min
The Companions' Complete Emulation of the Prophet's Actions
The author cites multiple examples of Companions imitating the Prophet's actions in detail.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Companions followed the Prophet's actions without hesitation, and why his actions (sunnah fi'liyyah) are a binding source of Islamic law.

Core Idea
The Companions copied every detail of the Prophet's life, making his actions a model for all Muslims.

This passage from the classical text demonstrates the Companions' extraordinary devotion to following the Prophet in every action, from removing sandals to eating habits. It establishes that the Prophet's actions, not just his commands, are normative for Muslims, unless proven specific to him. The author uses vivid historical examples to drive home this principle.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the translation. Notice the flow from principle to examples to a concluding remark.
The passage is long but coherent.
2
Identify the three sets of examples
Group the examples: (1) removing sandals/rings, uncovering knees; (2) crowding for shaving, researching his daily habits; (3) the incident with Ibn Umar and Umar's statement about the Black Stone.
3
Reflect on the underlying principle
The opening sentence states they followed 'without hesitation or consideration except where evidence shows specificity.' This is the key theological point: the Prophet's actions are generally binding.
This principle is reinforced by the examples.
4
Consider the implications for Islamic law
Think about how this passage shows that the Sunnah (actions) are a primary source of legislation, not just sayings. The Companions' behavior sets the precedent.

أو كلاماً يقربُ مِنْ هذا - ، فَمَنْ رَغِبَ عَنْ سُنَّتِي فَلَيْسَ مِنّي ( (۱) ، فانظر كيف ردَّهم بفعلِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ الذي لا معدل الاقتداء به.  عن  .  عما قصدوه ، معَ أَنَّهُ يظهرُ قبلَ التأمُّلِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ أكبر الطاعاتِ وجهاد النفس وقد ثبت أنَّ ابنَ عمر رضي الله عنهما لمَّا سألَهُ السائلُ عن صبغِهِ بالصفرة ، ولبسه النعالَ السِّبتيَّةَ ، وكونِهِ لا يُحرِمُ إِذا أَهل هلالُ ذي الحِجَّةِ ، وإِنَّما يُحرِمُ يوم التروية ، وكونه إنَّما يلمس الركنين اليمانيين .. فأجابَ بأَنَّهُ استندَ في ذلكَ كَلِّهِ لفعلِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّم (۲)  وقد أدارَ رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه راحلته في موضع ، واعتل لذلك بأنَّهُ كذلك رأى النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ يفعل (۳)  وانظر قول عمر رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه للحجر الأسود : ( لقد علمتُ أنَّكَ حجرٌ لا تضرُّ ولا تنفع ، ولولا أني رأيتُ رسولَ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ بيمينه ، أو يستقبل القبلة . . . الحديث (۱) رواه البخاري ( ٥٠٦٣ ) ، ومسلم ( ١٤٠١ ) من حديث سيدنا أنس بن مالك رضي الله عنه (۲) رواه البخاري ( ١٦٦ ) ، ومسلم ( ۱۱۸۷ ) ، والسائل له : هو عبيد بن جريج التيمي . (۳) انظر ( خلاصة الوفا » للسمهودي (٤٧٧/٢ ) ، وفي هامش ( أ ) عند قوله : ( واعتل ) : ( أي : استند )  .  ٢٤١
Without any hesitation or consideration whatsoever in all his words and actions, except where evidence established that it was specific to him: they removed their sandals when he (peace and blessings be upon him) removed his sandal (1), and they removed their rings when he (peace and blessings be upon him) removed his ring (2), and Abu Bakr and Umar (may Allah be pleased with them) uncovered their knees in the story of their sitting on the well just as he (peace and blessings be upon him) did (3), and they almost killed each other from the intensity of crowding for the shaving when they saw him (peace and blessings be upon him) shave his head and exit from his Umrah in the incident of Hudaybiyyah (4), and they researched extensively about the manner of his sitting, his sleep, his eating, and other things in order to imitate him (peace and blessings be upon him) (5) . . . until they regarded themselves, may Allah be pleased with them, like children in their father's lap; he cares for them and protects them, and they learn everything from him, even to the point that they learned from him (peace and blessings be upon him) the manner of relieving oneself; Muslim (262) narrated from Salman (may Allah be pleased with him) that he said: The polytheists said to us: I see your companion teaching you even how to relieve yourselves, and he said: Yes, he forbade us from using the right hand in cleaning after using the toilet . . . And he (peace and blessings be upon him) said to them when they wanted to devote themselves exclusively to worship night and day: 'As for me, I eat, sleep, and marry women' – or words close to this – 'Whoever turns away from my sunnah is not of me' (1). So see how he turned them away from what they intended by his action (peace and blessings be upon him) from which there is no alternative but to follow, even though before reflection it appears to be one of the greatest acts of obedience and jihad of the soul. And it is established that Ibn Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) when a questioner asked him about his dyeing with saffron, his wearing of sandals without hair, his not entering ihram when the crescent of Dhu al-Hijjah appeared but rather entering ihram on the day of Tarwiyah, and his only touching the two Yemeni corners – he answered that he relied in all of that on the action of the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) (2). And he (may Allah be pleased with him) once turned his mount around in a certain place and gave as reason that he had seen the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) doing likewise (3). And consider the saying of Umar (may Allah be pleased with him) concerning the Black Stone: 'I know that you are a stone that neither harms nor benefits, and were it not that I saw the Messenger of Allah (peace and blessings be upon him) kissing you, I would not have kissed you' (narration continues).
Source pages p. 240

Commentary
This passage is a historical-argumentative passage demonstrating the Companions' complete and unconditional adherence to the Prophet's actions (sunnah fi'liyyah). The author begins by stating a principle: they did not hesitate or reflect at all in following all of the Prophet's words and deeds, unless clear evidence existed that the act was specific to him. He then provides multiple examples: (1) when the Prophet removed his sandal, they removed theirs; (2) when he removed his ring, they removed theirs; (3) Abu Bakr and Umar uncovered their knees when the Prophet did so while sitting on a well; (4) they nearly killed each other in eagerness to be shaved when he shaved his head after Umrah in Hudaybiyyah; (5) they researched every detail of his sitting, sleep, eating, etc., to imitate him. The author then generalizes: they placed themselves like children in a father's care, learning even the etiquette of relieving oneself, as narrated by Salman. He then recounts the Prophet's rebuke to those who wanted to devote themselves entirely to worship night and day: 'As for me, I eat, sleep, and marry women... whoever turns away from my sunnah is not of me.' This shows that the Prophet's actions, even those that might seem merely natural, are normative. The author notes that before reflection, extreme devotional acts might appear to be great obedience, but the Prophet's own practice sets the standard. He then gives two more examples from Ibn Umar: he based his dyeing, sandals, ihram timing, and touching of Yemeni corners solely on what he saw the Prophet do; and he turned his mount in a specific spot simply because he saw the Prophet do that. Finally, he quotes Umar's famous statement to the Black Stone: 'I know you are a stone that neither harms nor benefits, but if I had not seen the Messenger of Allah kiss you, I would not have kissed you.' This reinforces that even ritual acts are based purely on following the Prophet, not on rational assessment. The passage thus establishes the binding nature of the Prophet's actions as a source of Islamic law and the Companions' exemplary compliance.

Key Terms
سنة
اقتداء
فعل النبي
اتباع
الأسوة الحسنة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only the Prophet's commands (sayings) are binding, not his actions.
Correction: The passage demonstrates that the Companions followed the Prophet's actions unconditionally, and the author uses this to establish that his actions (sunnah fi'liyyah) are a source of law unless proven specific to him.

Checkpoint
Why did the Companions remove their sandals when the Prophet removed his?
A) Because they felt forced by him.
B) Because he commanded them to.
C) Because they followed his actions without hesitation.
D) Because it was a specific order for that occasion.

Key Takeaway
The Companions' unconditional imitation of the Prophet's actions establishes that his sunnah fi'liyyah is a binding source of Islamic law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you do an ordinary act like eating, sleeping, or sitting, do you consciously try to do it as the Prophet (saw) did, or do you follow your own habit? What one change can you make this week to better align a daily action with his sunnah?
?
The Companions researched every detail of the Prophet's manner. When did you last actively seek out a sunnah of the Prophet in a practical matter (e.g., his way of sleeping, eating, or entering a house)? What stops you from doing that today?
?
Umar kissed the Black Stone purely because he saw the Prophet do it, even though he knew it had no power in itself. In your worship, do you sometimes omit or shorten prophetic practices because you don't understand their wisdom? How can you strengthen your submission to his example, especially in actions that seem illogical to you?

The Prophet's Rebuke of Extreme Asceticism
Narrates the Prophet's response to extreme asceticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Prophet's balanced practice, which includes normal human activities, is the authoritative standard for worship and how it rebukes extreme asceticism.

Core Idea
The Prophet's sunnah is the middle path in worship.

This passage presents a hadith in which the Prophet corrects companions who sought extreme asceticism, emphasizing his own balanced way. The commentary highlights that his action itself is an authoritative rebuke, leaving no room for deviation from his sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to understand the Prophet's exact words and the context.
Notice the key phrase 'so whoever turns away from my sunnah is not from me.'
2
Understand the context
The companions wanted to devote themselves entirely to worship night and day. The Prophet's response corrects their intention.
3
Identify the key message
The Prophet explicitly includes eating, sleeping, and marrying in his own practice, showing that these are part of the sunnah, not obstacles to worship.
4
Reflect on the commentary
The author notes that the Prophet's action itself is a rebuke, emphasizing that there is no alternative but to follow his example.

Source Text

(1) So see how he rebuked them by his action, may God bless him and grant him peace, which has no alternative but to follow.

Commentary
This passage presents a hadith in which the Prophet rebukes those who sought extreme asceticism, emphasizing his own balanced practice. It then comments that his action itself is an authoritative rebuke, leaving no room for deviation from his way.

Misconception: Extreme asceticism is superior to the Prophet's balanced way.
Correction: The Prophet explicitly stated his own practice as the sunnah and warned against turning away from it, showing that his balanced way is the correct standard.

Checkpoint

B) I eat, sleep, and marry, so whoever turns away from my sunnah is not from me

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's balanced lifestyle is the authoritative sunnah, and extreme asceticism is not from his way.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
In which area of your life are you most tempted to go to extremes—either in religious practice or in worldly indulgence—rather than following the balanced sunnah of the Prophet? What specific, practical step will you take today to bring that area closer to his example?
?
The Prophet said, 'Whoever turns away from my sunnah is not from me.' Does this warning make you uncomfortable about any of your current practices or attitudes? Be honest: where might you be subtly rejecting his way while thinking you are being more pious? What will you do about it starting now?

Ibn Umar's Meticulous Following of the Prophet's Actions
Ibn Umar's reliance on the Prophet's actions for his practices

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the Companion Ibn Umar exemplified meticulous following of the Prophet's actions, even in minor details.

Core Idea
Ibn Umar's religion was copying the Prophet in everything.

This lesson presents a vivid example from the life of Abdullah ibn Umar, a Companion known for his scrupulous imitation of the Prophet. When asked about his personal practices, from dyeing his beard to turning his mount, Ibn Umar's answer was consistent: he did it because he saw the Prophet do it. This shows us that following the Sunnah extends to all aspects of life.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noticing the specific actions mentioned. Note that the opening phrase has unclear OCR.
2
Identify the details
List the specific actions Ibn Umar was asked about: dyeing with saffron, wearing sandals, timing of ihram, touching the Yemeni corners, and turning his mount.
3
Understand Ibn Umar's reasoning
He repeatedly says he 'relied on the action of the Prophet.' This is his sole justification.
The key term 'استند' means 'relied upon'.
4
Reflect on the lesson
Consider what this teaches about the importance of following the Sunnah in both major and minor matters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
عن [؟] عما قصدوه [؟] معَ أَنَّهُ يظهرُ قبلَ التأمُّلِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ أكبر الطاعاتِ وجهاد النفس وقد ثبت أنَّ ابنَ عمر رضي الله عنهما لمَّا سألَهُ السائلُ عن صبغِهِ بالصفرة، ولبسه النعالَ السِّبتيَّةَ، وكونِهِ لا يُحرِمُ إِذا أَهل هلالُ ذي الحِجَّةِ، وإِنَّما يُحرِمُ يوم التروية، وكونه إنَّما يلمس الركنين اليمانيين .. فأجابَ بأَنَّهُ استندَ في ذلكَ كَلِّهِ لفعلِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّم. وقد أدارَ رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه راحلته في موضع، واعتل لذلك بأنَّهُ كذلك رأى النبيَّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ يفعل
Concerning [؟] what they intended [؟], although it appears before reflection that it is among the greatest acts of obedience and self-striving, and it is established that Ibn Umar, may God be pleased with him, when the questioner asked him about his dyeing with saffron, his wearing of sandals of tanned leather, his not entering ihram until the night of the eighth of Dhul-Hijjah, and his only touching the two Yemeni corners... he answered that he relied in all of that on the action of the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace. And he turned his mount around in a certain place, and gave as his excuse that he had seen the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, doing likewise.
Source pages p. 241

Commentary
This passage provides a concrete example of a Companion (Ibn Umar) who answered questions about his specific practices by directly citing the Prophet's actions, even for details like the direction of his mount. This illustrates the principle of following the Prophet in all matters, not just major ones.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That it is unnecessary to follow the Prophet in trivial matters like dyeing or turning a mount.
Correction: This example shows that Ibn Umar considered even minor actions of the Prophet as binding precedents, demonstrating that the Sunnah encompasses all aspects of life.

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Ibn Umar's practice teaches that the Prophet's actions are the ultimate guide for a believer, even in seemingly small matters.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Imagine that you were asked to justify every decision and habit of your day by pointing to the Prophet's way. How many of your actions would you have to change? What is one change you can commit to starting today, not because it is convenient but because it is the sunnah?

Following the Prophet: Umar and the Black Stone
Relates Umar's statement to the Black Stone, emphasizing following the Prophet

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Muslims follow the actions of the Prophet even when reason might suggest otherwise.

Core Idea
Following the Prophet supersedes rational evaluation.

Umar's statement to the Black Stone is a classic illustration that obedience to the Prophet's actions takes precedence over personal reasoning. This passage teaches that the Prophet's example is sufficient grounds for action, even when the object seems neutral. Umar openly admits the stone has no power, yet he kisses it solely because he saw the Prophet do so.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage in Arabic and English
Read Umar's statement carefully. Notice the contrast between his rational knowledge ('you are a stone that neither harms nor benefits') and his action (kissing it) motivated purely by following the Prophet.
The phrase 'were it not that I saw the Messenger of God... kissing you' is the key.
2
Analyze Umar's reasoning
Umar explicitly denies any inherent power in the Black Stone. His action is based solely on emulation of the Prophet (taqlid). Reflect on how this illustrates the principle that the Prophet's actions are a binding source of guidance.
This is not blind following; it is informed obedience to the Prophet.
3
Connect to the broader lesson
Consider how this principle applies to other acts of worship or religious practices. The lesson is that when the Prophet does something, it becomes a sunnah to be followed, even if we do not fully understand the wisdom behind it.
Umar's humility in setting aside his own reasoning is a model for believers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وانظر قول عمر رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه للحجر الأسود : ( لقد علمتُ أنَّكَ حجرٌ لا تضرُّ ولا تنفع ، ولولا أني رأيتُ رسولَ اللهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ قِبْلَكَ . . ما قبلْتُكَ
And consider the saying of Umar, may God be pleased with him, to the Black Stone: 'I know that you are a stone that neither harms nor benefits, and were it not that I saw the Messenger of God, may God bless him and grant him peace, kissing you... I would not kiss you.'
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage shows Umar acknowledging that the Black Stone has no intrinsic power, but he kisses it solely because he saw the Prophet do so. This exemplifies the principle of following the Prophet's actions without rationalizing them.

Key Terms
حجر أسود
تقبيل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Black Stone itself deserves reverence or has inherent power.
Correction: Umar explicitly states that the stone neither harms nor benefits. The reverence is for the act of following the Prophet, not for the stone itself.

Checkpoint
Why did Umar kiss the Black Stone?
A) Because he believed it could harm or benefit
B) Because he thought it was an idol
C) Because he saw the Prophet do it
D) Because it was a tradition of the Quraysh

Key Takeaway
The Prophet's actions are the ultimate guide for a believer, regardless of apparent rational considerations.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When was the last time you chose to follow the Prophet's way even though you could not see a rational benefit? What held you back from doing it sooner? Will you commit this week to one sunnah that you have been neglecting solely because it is from him?
?
Umar could have easily rationalized not kissing the stone, yet he did it because he saw the Prophet. What is one prophetic teaching in your life that you have been avoiding because it seems 'irrational' or inconvenient? What would it take for you to say, 'Were it not that I saw the Prophet... I would not do it'?
?
Imagine you are standing before the Black Stone. Can you honestly say you would kiss it just because the Prophet did, even if you felt no emotional or spiritual benefit? What does your answer reveal about the condition of your heart toward following him without reservation?
