Prophethood
beginner
4 min
Imam Ahmad's Reluctance to Eat Watermelon
Reports Ahmad ibn Hanbal's reluctance to eat watermelon due to lack of Sunnah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the depth of the Salaf's commitment to following the Prophet's example, even in everyday actions like eating.

Core Idea
Following the Prophet requires knowledge, not guesswork.

This short anecdote about Imam Ahmad ibn Hanbal illustrates a profound principle: that every action of a believer should be rooted in knowledge of the Sunnah. Even a simple act like eating watermelon becomes a matter of religious caution when the Prophet's example is unknown. Let's explore how this reflects the Salaf's meticulousness.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the directness of Imam Ahmad's statement.
The Arabic phrase 'لم يثبت عندي' emphasizes personal certainty.
2
Understand the context
Imam Ahmad was asked why he didn't eat watermelon. He didn't claim it was haram, but lacked knowledge of the Prophet's specific manner.
This shows that permissible acts can be avoided out of caution when Sunnah is unknown.
3
Reflect on the implications
If a great imam refrains from a permissible food due to lack of knowledge, it highlights the importance of seeking knowledge for all actions.
4
Address the misconception
Some might see this as extreme. But it demonstrates that following the Prophet is not limited to rituals; it encompasses lifestyle.
The Salaf understood that every act can be an act of worship if done in accordance with Sunnah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد ثبت عن بعض السلف ـ وأظنُّهُ أحمد بن حنبل رضيَ اللهُ تعالى عنه ـ أَنَّهُ كانَ لا يأكلُ البِطَّيخَ ، فقيل له في ذلكَ ، فقال : يمنعني مِنْ أكلِهِ أنَّهُ لم يثبت عندي كيف أكلَهُ النبيُّ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ
And it is established from some of the Salaf – and I think it is Ahmad ibn Hanbal, may God be pleased with him – that he would not eat watermelon. He was asked about that, and he said: 'What prevents me from eating it is that it has not been established how the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, ate it.'
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage recounts that Imam Ahmad refrained from eating a permissible food (watermelon) because he did not know the specific manner in which the Prophet ate it. This demonstrates the extreme caution in following the Prophet's example even in trivial matters.

Key Terms
بطيخ
اتباع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: It is extreme to refrain from permissible acts without knowing the Prophet's specific practice.
Correction: This anecdote shows that the Salaf considered following the Prophet's example as encompassing all aspects of life, not just religious rituals. Their caution was a reflection of their deep devotion and desire to emulate the Prophet in every possible way.

Checkpoint
Why did Ahmad ibn Hanbal not eat watermelon?
A) He disliked the taste
B) He was allergic
C) He did not know how the Prophet ate it
D) It was forbidden

Key Takeaway
Imam Ahmad's caution in eating watermelon exemplifies the Salaf's meticulous adherence to the Sunnah in all matters, even the seemingly trivial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there permissible actions in your daily life that you do without knowing how the Prophet (peace be upon him) performed them? What would it cost you to seek that knowledge and align your practice accordingly?
?
When you do not know the specific Sunnah for an action, do you feel the same sense of caution as Imam Ahmad, or do you proceed without knowledge? Reflect on a recent example and what it reveals about your relationship with the Sunnah.
?
Imam Ahmad refrained from watermelon simply because he did not know. How would that kind of mindfulness change your daily routine? What is one step you can take today to learn the Sunnah of a common act?

Doctrinal Conclusion: Ittiba' and Prophetic Infallibility
Summarizes the doctrine of following the Prophet and its proof of infallibility

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the practice of following the Prophet (ittiba') serves as a definitive proof of prophetic infallibility and how prophetic actions are categorized by essence.

Core Idea
Following the Prophet is itself a proof of his infallibility.

This passage wraps up the discussion by stating that the very practice of following the Prophet in all his sayings and actions—except those exclusive to him—is a core tenet of the righteous ancestors. This practice, accepted by consensus, becomes a decisive proof that the prophets are protected from sin and disliked actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the strong claim that ittiba' is 'known from the religion of the righteous ancestors by necessity.'
2
Identify the main claim
The passage states that ittiba' is a definitive proof of the Prophet's infallibility. Ask yourself: How does following someone prove that they are infallible?
This connects to the consensus (ijma') of the Salaf.
3
Understand the categorization of actions
The passage classifies prophetic actions into obligatory, commendable, and permissible when considered by essence. Consider what this implies about the nature of prophetic acts.
This distinction is important for later discussions on the Prophet's actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالجملة : فالاتباع له صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في جميعِ وأفعالِهِ إلا ما اختُصَّ بهِ ، ورؤية الكمال فيها جملةً وتفصيلاً بلا تردُّدِ ولا توقف أصلاً .. ممَّا عُلِمَ مِنْ دين السلف الصالح ضرورة ، ولا شكّ أنَّ هذا دليل قطعي إجماعي على عصمتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وفي معناه عصمةُ سائرِ الرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ مِنْ جميع المعاصي والمكروهات ، وأنَّ أفعالهم صلواتُ اللهِ وسلامه على دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب والمباح ، وهذا بحسب النظرِ إلى الفعلِ مِنْ حيثُ ذاتُهُ ، وأمَّا إذا نُظِرَ إِلَيْهِ بحَسَبِ عوارضهِ فالحقُّ أَنَّ
In summary: following him, may God bless him and grant him peace, in all his sayings and actions except what is specific to him, and seeing perfection in them collectively and individually without hesitation or pause at all... is something known from the religion of the righteous ancestors by necessity. And there is no doubt that this is a definitive, consensus-based proof of his infallibility, may God bless him and grant him peace, and in its meaning is the infallibility of all the messengers, peace be upon them, from all sins and disliked acts, and that their actions, God's blessings and peace be upon them all, are divided among the obligatory, commendable, and permissible. This is according to looking at the action in terms of its essence. As for considering it according to its accidental attributes, the truth is that...
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage summarizes the entire discussion into a doctrinal point: that following the Prophet in every aspect (except his exclusive prerogatives) is a central tenet of the Salaf, and this itself constitutes a definitive proof of the prophets' infallibility from sin and disliked actions. It also clarifies that their actions, by essence, fall into the categories of obligatory, commendable, or permissible.

Key Terms
اتباع
عصمة
واجب
مندوب
مباح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the Prophet's infallibility is based on rational proof rather than consensus-based ittiba'.
Correction: The passage explicitly grounds the proof of infallibility in the consensus-based practice of following the Prophet (ittiba'), not in rational arguments alone.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the practice of ittiba' prove?
A) The prophethood of Muhammad
B) The infallibility of the Prophet and all messengers
C) The permissibility of eating watermelon
D) The importance of the Black Stone

Key Takeaway
The practice of following the Prophet is a definitive consensus-based proof of the infallibility of all messengers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly follow the Prophet in all his sayings and actions, without exception (except those specific to him), or do you pick and choose based on your own desires? What would it take for you to reach a state where you see perfection in every aspect of his life without hesitation?
?
The Salaf knew the Prophet's perfection by necessity. Have you ever paused to question whether your hesitations about some of the Prophet's actions stem from your own shortcomings rather than from the actions themselves? Are you willing to submit to the consensus of the Salaf and accept that every action of the Prophet is perfect and worthy of emulation?
?
If you truly believed that following the Prophet in every detail is a definitive proof of his infallibility, how would that change the way you approach the sunnah today? Name one specific area of your life where you have not fully followed the Prophet and commit to changing it starting today.

Prophets' Actions Are Only Obligatory or Recommended
Sanusi proves prophets' actions are limited to wajib and mandub.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets' actions are never merely permissible and how intention transforms them into acts of worship.

Core Idea
Prophets' actions are always worship, never driven by mere desire.

This passage refines an earlier statement about prophets' actions. At first glance, their actions seem to include the permissible, but a deeper look reveals that even seemingly permissible acts are accompanied by intentions that make them acts of worship. This lesson unpacks that argument and shows how it reinforces prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice the flow from general principle to refined conclusion.
The passage uses a rhetorical question to emphasize the high rank of prophets.
2
Identify the two perspectives on actions
Sanusi distinguishes between considering actions by their essence (ذات) and by their accidental circumstances (عوارض). Find where he makes this distinction.
In essence, actions are wajib, mandub, or mubah. In accidents, only wajib and mandub.
3
Understand why mubah is excluded
The key reason is that prophets never act out of desire. Their actions always accompany an intention (نية) that makes them an act of worship (قربة), such as teaching.
The least intention is to legislate for others by teaching.
4
Consider the analogy with saints
Sanusi uses an a fortiori argument: if even the lowest saint can turn all permissible acts into worship through good intention, how much more so for prophets?
This strengthens the point about prophets' exceptional rank.
5
Reflect on the creedal implication
The conclusion is that in the creed (أصل العقيدة), we describe prophets' actions as 'obedience' (طاعة) to highlight their restriction to wajib and mandub.
Sanusi added 'in their case' to allow that the action itself might be called permissible in essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالجملة : فالاتباع له صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في جميعِ وأفعالِهِ إلا ما اختُصَّ بهِ ، ورؤية الكمال فيها جملةً وتفصيلاً بلا تردُّدِ ولا توقف أصلاً .. ممَّا عُلِمَ مِنْ دين السلف الصالح ضرورة ، ولا شكّ أنَّ هذا دليل قطعي إجماعي على عصمتِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وفي معناه عصمةُ سائرِ الرُّسُلِ عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ مِنْ جميع المعاصي والمكروهات ، وأنَّ أفعالهم صلواتُ اللهِ وسلامه على دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب والمباح ، وهذا بحسب النظرِ إلى الفعلِ مِنْ حيثُ ذاتُهُ ، وأمَّا إذا نُظِرَ إِلَيْهِ بحَسَبِ عوارضهِ فالحقُّ أَنَّ أفعالهم دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب لا غيرُ ؛ لأنَّ المباحَ لا يقعُ منهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام بمقتضى الشهوة ونحوها كما يقعُ مِنْ غيرِهم ، بل لا يقعُ منهم إلا مصاحِباً لنيَّةٍ يصيرُ بها قُربةً ، وأقلُّ ذلكَ أنْ يقصدوا به التشريع للغيرِ ، وذلكَ مِنْ بابِ التعليم ، وناهيك بمنزلة قُربة التعليم وعظيم فضلها. وإذا كان أدنى الأولياء يصلُ إلى رتبة تصيرُ معَها مباحاته كلُّها طاعات بحسن النية في تناولها .. فما بالكَ بِخيرةِ اللهِ تعالى مِنْ خَلقِهِ ؛ وهم أنبياؤُهُ ورُسُلُهُ عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؟! لا سيما أفضل الخلق وأشرفِ العالمين جملةً وتفصيلاً بإجماع مَنْ يُعتدُّ بإجماعِهِ ؛ سيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ . ولأجل انحصار أفعالهم في الواجب والمندوب على هذا الوجه الذي ذكرناه . . اقتصرنا في أصل العقيدة على ما يقتضي الاختصاص بهما ؛ وهو الطاعةُ ، وزدنا التقييد بقولنا : ( في حقهم ) إشارةً إلى أنَّ بعض أفعالهم وإنْ كانَ يُطلَقُ عليها الإباحةُ بالنظر إلى الفعل في نفسِهِ،
In summary: following him (peace be upon him) in all his actions except what is specific to him, and seeing perfection in them in general and in detail without hesitation or pause at all — that is known from the religion of the righteous predecessors necessarily, and there is no doubt that this is a definitive, consensus-based proof of his infallibility (peace be upon him), and in its meaning is the infallibility of the rest of the messengers (peace and blessings be upon them) from all sins and detestable things, and that their actions (blessings and peace of God be upon them) revolve between the obligatory, the recommended, and the permissible — this is according to considering the action from the perspective of its essence. But when it is considered according to its accidental circumstances, the truth is that their actions revolve between the obligatory and the recommended only; because the permissible does not occur from them (peace and blessings be upon them) out of desire and the like as it occurs from others, rather it does not occur from them except accompanied by an intention by which it becomes an act of worship. The least of that is that they intend by it legislation for others, and that is from the category of teaching. And how great is the station of the act of worship of teaching and its immense virtue! If the lowest of the saints reaches a rank by which all his permissible acts become acts of obedience through good intention in undertaking them, then what about the chosen ones of God from His creation — they are His prophets and messengers (peace and blessings be upon them)?! Especially the best of creation and the most noble of the worlds generally and specifically by consensus of those whose consensus is counted: our master and lord Muhammad (peace be upon him). And because their actions are confined to the obligatory and the recommended in this manner we have mentioned, we restricted in the foundation of the creed to what necessitates being specific to them both, which is obedience, and we added the restriction by saying 'in their case' as an indication that some of their actions, even if they are called permissible with regard to the action itself...
Source pages p. 242

Commentary
This passage is an explanation and proof that the actions of prophets, especially the Prophet Muhammad, are confined to the obligatory (wajib) and recommended (mandub), and never to the merely permissible (mubah) in the sense of being driven by desire. The author begins by stating that following the Prophet in all his actions (except those specific to him) and seeing perfection in them is a necessary part of the religion of the righteous predecessors. This is a definitive proof of his infallibility ('isma) and, by extension, the infallibility of all messengers from sins and detestable things. The actions of prophets, considered in their essence, can be obligatory, recommended, or permissible. However, when considered according to their accidental circumstances (like intention and context), the truth is that their actions are only obligatory or recommended. The reason is that a permissible act never occurs from them out of desire as it does from others; rather, it always accompanies an intention that makes it an act of worship (qurba). The least such intention is to legislate for others by way of teaching. The author then emphasizes the great virtue of teaching. He argues by analogy: if the lowest saint can transform all his permissible acts into acts of obedience through good intention, then how much more so for the prophets, especially the best of creation, Muhammad (peace be upon him). Finally, the author states that for this reason, in his creedal summary, he restricted the description of prophets' actions to obedience (i.e., wajib and mandub) and added the qualification 'in their case' to indicate that even if an action is called permissible in itself, it is not really so for them because of their high station.

Key Terms
الاتباع
العصمة
الواجب
المندوب
المباح
القربة
التشريع
التعليم
الأنبياء
الرسل
السلف الصالح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets can perform merely permissible (mubah) acts like ordinary people, out of personal desire.
Correction: Prophets never act out of desire; even seemingly permissible acts are accompanied by a worshipful intention, making them either wajib or mandub.

Checkpoint
According to Sanusi, when considering actions by their accidental circumstances (عوارض), what are the categories of prophets' actions?
A) Wajib, mandub, and mubah
B) Only wajib
C) Wajib and mandub only
D) Only mandub

Key Takeaway
Prophets' actions are never merely permissible; they are always obligatory or recommended because they are accompanied by an intention of worship.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you ever perform acts of worship out of habit or desire, without conscious intention? How does the example of the prophets, who never act without a worshipful intention, challenge you to examine your own actions today?
?
If even the lowest saint can transform permissible acts into worship through good intention, what is stopping you from turning your daily tasks—eating, sleeping, working—into acts of devotion? What specific change will you make by tomorrow?
?
The Prophet's every action was teaching. When you go about your day, do you consider that your actions might be seen as lessons by others? Are you content with what they might learn from you?

Prophethood
intermediate
10 min
Prophets' Actions Restricted to Obligatory and Recommended
Sanusi explains why prophets' actions are only obligatory or recommended

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets' actions are always acts of worship, even when they appear permissible, due to their perfect intentions and infallibility.

Core Idea
Even permissible acts of prophets become worship through their intentions.

Sanusi presents a profound argument about the nature of prophetic actions. He explains that due to their high station and perfect intentions, even acts that would be permissible for ordinary people become acts of worship for prophets. This passage clarifies a key aspect of prophetic infallibility and why their actions are always morally positive.

Guided Path
1
Read the Full Passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully to grasp the overall claim and argument structure.
Notice the strong assertion at the beginning: 'أفعالهم دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب لا غير'. This sets up the entire discussion.
2
Identify the Three Categories
Identify the categories of actions: wajib (obligatory), mandub (recommended), and mubah (permissible). Understand why mubah is excluded from prophets' actions in the ordinary sense.
The category mubah is not denied entirely, but its nature changes for prophets.
3
Understand the Reason
Sanusi gives the reason: permissible acts occur from prophets only with an intention that makes them acts of nearness (qurba). The least such intention is to legislate for others, which is an act of teaching.
Teaching is highlighted as a great virtue.
4
Reflect on the Analogy
Consider the analogy: if even the lowest saints can turn all their permissible acts into worship through good intention, how much more so for prophets? This reinforces the point.
The analogy uses a 'lesser-to-greater' argument (qiyas al-awlawi).
5
Connect to the Creed
Understand why in creed we restrict prophets' actions to 'obedience in their case' (ṭāʿa fī ḥaqqihim). The passage explains the reasoning behind this technical phrasing.
The phrase 'fī ḥaqqihim' indicates a special ruling for prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أفعالهم دائرة بين الواجب والمندوب لا غيرُ ؛ لأنَّ المباحَ لا يقعُ منهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام بمقتضى الشهوة ونحوها كما يقعُ مِنْ غيرِهم ، بل لا يقعُ منهم إلا مصاحِباً لنيَّةٍ يصيرُ بها قُربةً ، وأقلُّ ذلكَ أنْ يقصدوا به التشريع للغيرِ ، وذلكَ مِنْ بابِ التعليم ، وناهيك بمنزلة قُربة التعليم وعظيم فضلها. وإذا كان أدنى الأولياء يصلُ إلى رتبة تصيرُ معَها مباحاته كلُّها طاعات بحسن النية في تناولها .. فما بالكَ بِخيرةِ اللهِ تعالى مِنْ خَلقِهِ ؛ وهم أنبياؤُهُ ورُسُلُهُ عليهم الصلاة والسلام ؟! لا سيما أفضل الخلق وأشرفِ العالمين جملةً وتفصيلاً بإجماع مَنْ يُعتدُّ بإجماعِهِ؛ سيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ. ولأجل انحصار أفعالهم في الواجب والمندوب على هذا الوجه الذي ذكرناه .. اقتصرنا في أصل العقيدة على ما يقتضي الاختصاص بهما؛ وهو الطاعةُ، وزدنا التقييد بقولنا : ( في حقهم ) إشارةً إلى أنَّ بعض أفعالهم وإنْ كانَ يُطلَقُ عليها الإباحةُ بالنظر إلى الفعل في نفسِهِ، وبالنظر إلى وجودِهِ مِنْ عامَّةِ المؤمنينَ .. فهو في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ـ لكمال معرفتهم بالله تعالى، وسلامتهم مِنْ دواعي النفس والهوى، وأمنهم مِنْ طوارقِ الفَتَراتِ والمَلَلِ يقظة ونوماً، وتأييدهم بعصمة الله تعالى في كلِّ حالٍ - لا يقعُ منهم إلا طاعةً يثابونَ عليها.
Their actions are confined to the obligatory and the recommended, no other; because the permissible does not occur from them, peace and blessings be upon them, following desire and the like, as it occurs from others. Rather, it occurs from them only accompanied by an intention by which it becomes a means of nearness. The least of that is that they intend thereby legislation for others, and that is from the category of teaching. How great is the rank of the nearness of teaching and its immense virtue! If the lowest of the saints attains a rank by which all his permissible actions become acts of obedience by good intention in undertaking them, then what of the chosen ones of God Almighty from His creation? They are His prophets and messengers, peace and blessings be upon them, and especially the best of creation and the most honorable of the worlds in general and in detail by consensus of those whose consensus is considered: our master and lord Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace. Because of the confinement of their actions to the obligatory and the recommended in this manner we have mentioned, we limited [the discussion] in the foundation of creed to what pertains to what is specific to them both, which is obedience. And we added the restriction in our statement: 'in their case' as an indication that, although some of their acts may be called permissible in view of the act in itself, and in view of its occurrence from the generality of believers, yet in their case, peace and blessings be upon them—due to their perfection of knowledge of God Almighty, their safety from the motives of the soul and desire, their security from the vicissitudes of lapses and weariness in wakefulness and sleep, and their support by God's infallibility in every state—nothing occurs from them except an act of obedience for which they are rewarded.
Source pages p. 243

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof regarding the actions of prophets. It states that the actions of prophets are confined to the obligatory (wajib) and the recommended (mandub), and that the permissible (mubah) does not occur from them in the same way as from ordinary people. The reason given is that their permissible actions are always accompanied by an intention that transforms them into acts of nearness (qurba); at the very least, they intend to legislate for others, which is an act of teaching (ta'līm). The author highlights the great virtue of teaching. The argument then proceeds by analogy: if even the lowest of saints can turn all their permissible actions into acts of obedience through good intention, then how much more so for God's chosen ones—the prophets. The best of creation is Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him). Finally, the author explains why in the creed they restrict the actions of prophets to 'obedience in their case' (ṭāʿa fī ḥaqqihim): although an act may be considered permissible in itself and when done by ordinary believers, due to the prophets' perfect knowledge, safety from passions, security from lapses, and God's infallibility, it never occurs from them except as an act of obedience for which they receive reward.

Key Terms
الواجب
المندوب
المباح
الطاعة
القربة
العصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophets can commit permissible acts just like ordinary people, without any special religious merit.
Correction: This passage clarifies that even permissible acts by prophets are always accompanied by intentions that transform them into acts of worship, making them acts of obedience for which they are rewarded.

Checkpoint
Why does the author state that prophets' actions are only obligatory or recommended?
A) Because prophets are forced by God to only do those actions.
B) Because even their permissible acts are accompanied by intention for nearness, making them acts of worship.
C) Because prophets have no free will.
D) Because the permissible is not possible for prophets.

Key Takeaway
Prophets' actions are always acts of worship due to their perfect intentions and divine infallibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The text says that even the lowest saint can transform all their permissible actions into acts of obedience through good intention. What is one 'permissible' action in your daily life that you have never thought to turn into worship by changing your intention? Will you commit to doing that tomorrow with the intention of drawing closer to Allah?
?
Prophets are described as being 'safe from the motives of the soul and desire.' Think of a recent situation where your action was driven by personal desire rather than the pleasure of Allah. What concrete change can you make to align that area of your life with the prophetic model of pure intention?
?
If the Prophet Muhammad's every action, even eating and sleeping, was an act of worship, what does that say about your own view of ordinary moments? Will you start your next meal or routine activity with the explicit intention of obeying Allah and following the sunnah, and hold yourself to that today?

Sanusi warns believers to guard faith by rejecting false stories about prophets

By the end of this lesson, you will understand why listening to false stories about prophets can endanger your faith and how to guard against it.

Core Idea
False stories about prophets can strip your faith; cling only to the truth.

Having established the truth about the prophets, Sanusi now turns to a practical warning. He addresses the believer directly, urging caution against false narratives that circulate even among historians and commentators. This lesson explains why such tales are dangerous and how to protect your faith.

Proof of Prophets' Infallibility in Conveying
Sanusi presents a logical proof for prophets' infallibility in conveying revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Sanusi uses a reductio ad absurdum argument to prove that prophets are infallible in conveying divine revelation.

Core Idea
If a prophet could conceal revelation, we would be commanded to follow him in concealing—an impossibility.

Sanusi presents a tight logical argument for the prophetic attribute of infallibility in conveying the message. The proof relies on the principle of following the prophet (iqtidā'). By showing the absurd consequence of a prophet failing to convey, Sanusi demonstrates that such a failure is rationally impossible. This passage is a classic example of kalam reasoning: starting from an agreed premise and deducing a necessary conclusion.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing it. Then read the literal English translation. Get a sense of the argument's flow.
2
Identify the structure of the proof
Notice that Sanusi begins by stating 'This itself is the proof of the necessity of the third.' Understand that the 'third' refers to the prophets' duty to convey the message. Then follow the conditional reasoning: if a prophet did something contrary, what would follow?
3
Follow the logical chain to the conclusion
The consequence of a prophet concealing is that believers would be commanded to follow his example and also conceal. This leads to the absurdity of God commanding both conveyance and concealment of the same message. Therefore, such an act cannot occur. This proves infallibility.
This is a reductio ad absurdum: assuming the opposite leads to contradiction.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وهذا بعينِهِ هو برهان وجوب الثالث ( مراده بالثالث : تبليغهم عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ ما أمروا بتبليغه ، ولا شك أنَّهم لو وقع منهم عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ خلافُ ذلكَ لكُنَّا مأمورينَ بأن نقتدي بهم في ذلك ، فنكتم نحنُ أيضاً بعض ما أوجبَ الله تعالى علينا تبليغَهُ مِنَ
His saying: 'And this itself is the proof of the necessity of the third.' He means by 'the third': their conveying, peace and blessings be upon them, what they were commanded to convey. And there is no doubt that if something contrary to that had occurred from them, peace and blessings be upon them, we would be commanded to follow them in that, and thus we would also conceal some of what God Almighty obligated upon us to convey from...
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage explains a proof concerning the third obligation, which is the prophets' duty to convey what they were commanded. The proof is a logical reductio ad absurdum: if a prophet had committed an act contrary to conveying (e.g., hiding part of the revelation), then believers would be obligated to follow the prophet's example (al-iqtidā'). Consequently, believers would also be commanded to conceal part of what God required them to convey. This leads to a contradiction, as God would be commanding both the conveyance and the concealment of the same message. Therefore, such an act cannot possibly occur from a prophet. Thus, prophets are infallible ('isma) in the act of conveying the message.

Key Terms
برهان
تبليغ
ثالث
اقتداء
عصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophets could make mistakes in conveying revelation, but this proof shows it is logically impossible.
Correction: If a prophet could fail to convey, then believers would be commanded to follow that failure, leading to a contradiction in God's commands. Thus, infallibility in conveyance is a necessary rational conclusion.

Checkpoint
What is the logical consequence if a prophet were to conceal part of the message he was commanded to convey?
A) Believers would be commanded to follow his example and also conceal that part.
B) Believers would be commanded to reject that part.
C) The prophet would no longer be a prophet.
D) The message would be automatically corrected.

Key Takeaway
Prophets are infallible in conveying revelation because any contrary act would lead to an absurd command to follow them in error.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the prophet himself could err in conveying the message, how would that affect your trust in every single word of the Quran and Sunnah? Can you truly follow without doubt?
?
The proof shows that God cannot command both concealment and conveyance. Are there areas in your own practice where you are selective in conveying Islam, hiding parts you find uncomfortable? What would it mean to follow the prophet's complete example in that?
?
Would you follow the prophet even if he commanded something that seemed wrong to you? This lesson proves that is impossible. Now ask yourself: are you following the prophet fully, or only when it aligns with your desires?

Prophets' Infallibility and Warning Against False Narratives
Sanusi describes prophets' infallibility and warns against false stories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that prophets are divinely protected from sin and that believers must guard their faith by rejecting false narratives about them.

Core Idea
Prophets only do good; believers must reject any false stories about them.

This lesson presents Sanusi's affirmation of prophetic infallibility ('iṣma) and his urgent warning to believers. After establishing the spiritual state of the prophets, Sanusi directly addresses the reader, cautioning against listening to fabricated tales that contradict this truth.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the flow from the description of the prophets' state to the warning.
Notice the shift from theological affirmation to direct exhortation.
2
Understand the basis of infallibility
Identify the reasons Sanusi gives for why prophets only commit acts of obedience: perfect knowledge of Allah, immunity from desires, security from lapses, and divine support.
These reasons collectively establish their 'iṣma.
3
Recognize the warning
Note the sources of false narratives: liars, historians, and ignorant exegetes. Understand that lending ear or mind to such fables can strip one of faith.
This is a serious spiritual danger.
4
Internalize the imperative
Sanusi commands to 'tighten your hand upon the truth' and 'cast away everything else.' Reflect on how this applies to your own engagement with reports about prophets.
The truth is clear; hold fast to it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وبالنظر إلى وجودِهِ مِنْ عامَّةِ المؤمنينَ .. فهو في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ـ لكمال معرفتهم بالله تعالى ، وسلامتهم مِنْ دواعي النفس والهوى ، وأمنهم مِنْ طوارقِ الفَتَراتِ والمَلَلِ يقظة ونوماً ، وتأييدهم بعصمة الله تعالى في كلِّ حالٍ - لا يقعُ منهم إلا طاعةً يثابونَ عليها ، صلَّى الله على نبينا وعلى جميع إخوانِهِ مِنَ النبيِّينَ والمرسلينَ ولتكن أيُّها المؤمنُ على حذرٍ عظيمٍ ووَجَلٍ شديدٍ على إيمانك أنْ يُسلَبَ منكَ ؛ بأن تصغي بأُذُنِكَ أو عقلِكَ إِلى خرائفَ ينقلُها كَذَبَةٌ (1) والمؤرخين (1) ، وتبعهم في بعضها بعضُ جهلة المفسرين(2) ، فقد سمعت الحقِّ الذي لا غبار عليهِ في حقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، فشُدَّ يدَكَ عليهِ ، وانبذ كلَّ ما سواه ، والله المستعانُ .
And with regard to their condition from the generality of the believers... So in their right, peace be upon them, due to the perfection of their knowledge of God Almighty, and their safety from the promptings of the self and desire, and their security from the vicissitudes of lapses and weariness awake and asleep, and their support by the infallibility of God Almighty in every state - nothing occurs from them except obedience for which they are rewarded. May God bless our Prophet and all his brothers among the prophets and messengers. And let you, O believer, be on great guard and intense fear for your faith lest it be stripped from you; by lending your ear or your mind to superstitious fables which liars and historians transmit, and some ignorant exegetes followed them in some of them. For you have heard the truth that has no dust upon it concerning their right, peace be upon them, so tighten your hand upon it, and cast away everything else. And God is the Helper.
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage defines the state of the prophets: due to their perfect knowledge of God, immunity from selfish desires and passions, and security from lapses and weariness in all states (awake and asleep), supported by divine infallibility, they only perform acts of obedience for which they are rewarded. The author then prays for the Prophet and all prophets and messengers. Following this, he issues a stern warning to the believer to be on great guard and intense fear for his faith lest it be snatched away by lending ear or mind to superstitious fables (khurāfāt) transmitted by liars and historians, and followed by some ignorant exegetes. The believer is reminded that he has heard the unblemished truth concerning the prophets, so he should hold fast to it and reject everything else.

Proof of the Necessity of Prophets Conveying All Revelation
Sanusi proves that prophets must convey all revelation using logic and Quran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the logical and Quranic proof that prophets cannot conceal any part of what they are commanded to convey.

Core Idea
If a prophet could conceal, we would have to imitate him—but concealment is cursed, so it is impossible.

Sanusi presents a concise yet powerful proof that prophets must deliver all revelation without omission. His argument rests on the principle of following the prophet: if they could conceal, we would be obliged to imitate them, which leads to an absurd and cursed consequence. The proof is then reinforced by two Quranic verses that establish both the prohibition of concealment and the gravity of failing to convey even a part.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic original and its literal translation. Notice the logical flow: 'if they did x, we would have to do x, but x is forbidden, so they cannot do x.'
The argument is compact; take time to follow each step.
2
Analyze the logical premise
Identify the conditional statement: if prophets could conceal, then believers would be commanded to imitate them in concealment. But concealment of knowledge is cursed, so the antecedent is impossible.
This is a proof by contradiction (implication of an impossible consequence).
3
Examine the Quranic evidence
Study the two verses: Surah al-Baqarah 2:159 curses concealers, and Surah al-Ma'idah 5:67 equates partial omission with total failure. Understand how each verse supports the proof.
The Ma'idah verse also contains a subtle linguistic point about the wording of the condition and answer.
4
Reflect on the deeper lesson
Consider the mention of the Prophet's fear and the commentary on its proportionality to knowledge. This serves as a reminder of the seriousness of conveying divine messages.
The footnote explains the rhetorical beauty of the verse's phrasing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وهذا بعينِهِ هو برهان وجوبِ الثالث ( مراده بالثالث : تبليغهم عليهم الصلاة والسلامُ ما أمروا بتبليغه ، ولا شك أنَّهم لو وقع منهم عليهم الصلاةُ والسلامُ خلافُ ذلكَ لكُنَّا مأمورينَ بأن نقتدي بهم في ذلك ، فنكتم نحنُ أيضاً بعض ما أوجبَ الله تعالى علينا تبليغَهُ مِنَ العلم النافع لمن اضطر إليه ، كيف وهو محرَّمٌ ملعون فاعلُهُ ؟! قال الله تعالى ﴿إِنَّ الَّذِينَ يَكْتُمُونَ مَا أَنزَلْنَا مِنَ الْبَيِّنَاتِ وَالْهُدَىٰ مِن بَعْدِ مَا بَيَّنَّاهُ لِلنَّاسِ فِي الْكِتَابِ أُوْلَٰئِكَ يَلْعَنُهُمُ اللهُ وَيَلْعَنُهُمُ اللَّاعِنُونَ﴾ [البقرة : ١٥٩] . وكيف يتصوَّرُ وقوع ذلك منهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ومولانا جل وعزّ يقولُ لسيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ﴿ يَاأَيُّهَا الرَّسُولُ بَلِّغْ مَا أُنزِلَ إِلَيْكَ مِن رَّبِّكَ وَإِن لَّمْ تَفْعَلْ فَمَا بَلَّغْتَ رِسَالَتَهُ﴾ [المائدة : ٦٧] أي : إن لم تبلغ بعض ما أُمِرْتَ بتبليغِهِ مِنَ الرسالة(1) .. فحكمُكَ حكمُ مَنْ لم يبلغ شيئاً منها ، والله تعالى أعلم . فانظر هذا التخويف العظيمَ لأشرف خلقِهِ وأكملهم معرفةً بهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، فكانَ خوفُهُ على قدْرِ معرفتِهِ ، ولهذا كانَ يُسْمَعُ لصدرِهِ صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ أزيز - أي : غليان ـ كأزيز المرجَلِ ؛ مِنْ خوفِ الله تعالى(2) (1) إنما تأوَّل تبليغ ما أنزل بالبعض ؛ لكيلا يكون الجواب عين الشرط ؛ إذ لا يقال : إن لم يأتِ زيدٌ لم يأتِ ؛ فكأنه قال : إن لم تبلغ ما أنزل إليك كاملاً ؛ بأن كتمت بعضاً منه . . فما بلغت رسالة الله تعالى أصلاً . وقال ابن المنير في ( الانتصاف ) ( ٢/ ٢٦٩ ) وقد جعل الجواب والشرط متحدين في المعنى متخالفين في اللفظ : ( وهذه المغايرة اللفظية وإن كان المعنى واحداً .. أحسنُ رونقاً وأظهر طلاوة من تكرار اللفظ الواحد في الشرط والجزاء ، وهذه الذروة انحط عنها أبو النجم بذكر المبتدأ بلفظ الخبر ـ في رجزه المشهور : أنا أبو النجم وشعري شعري - وحق له أن تتضاءل فصاحته عند فصاحة المعجز ، فلا يعاب عليه في ذلك ) (2) رواه أبو داود ( 904 ) ، والنسائي ( 13/3 ) من حديث سيدنا عبد الله بن ...
His saying: (And this itself is the proof of the necessity of the third) — he means by 'the third': their conveying, peace be upon them, what they were commanded to convey. And there is no doubt that if from them, peace be upon them, contrary to that had occurred, we would be commanded to imitate them in that, so we too would conceal some of what God Almighty obliged us to convey of beneficial knowledge for whoever needs it. How so, when it is forbidden and its doer is cursed?! God Almighty said: {Indeed, those who conceal what We sent down of clear proofs and guidance after We made it clear for the people in the Scripture — those God curses and the cursers curse them} [Al-Baqarah 2:159]. And how can its occurrence from them be imagined, peace be upon them, when our Master, Mighty and Majestic, says to our Master and our Liege Muhammad, may God bless him and grant him peace: {O Messenger, convey what has been sent down to you from your Lord, and if you do not, then you have not conveyed His message} [Al-Ma'idah 5:67] — meaning: if you do not convey some of what you were commanded to convey of the message... then your judgment is the judgment of one who did not convey any of it. And God knows best. So consider this great intimidation for the most noble of His creation and the most complete of them in knowledge of Him, may God bless him and grant him peace. For his fear was proportional to his knowledge, and for this reason there used to be heard from his chest, peace be upon him, a bubbling — that is, a boiling — like the bubbling of a cauldron, from fear of God Almighty. (1) He interpreted 'convey what was sent down' as referring to some, so that the answer would not be identical to the condition; for it is not said: 'If Zayd did not come, he did not come.' So it is as if He said: If you do not convey what was sent down to you completely, by concealing some of it... then you have not conveyed God's message at all. And Ibn al-Munir said in al-Intisaf (2/269): 'He made the answer and the condition identical in meaning but different in wording, and this verbal difference, even if the meaning is one, is more beautiful in luster and more manifest in sweetness than repeating the same word in the condition and the answer. This peak Abu al-Najm fell short of when he mentioned the subject in the wording of the predicate in his famous rajaz: "I am Abu al-Najm and my poetry is my poetry" — and it is fitting that his eloquence should be diminished before the eloquence of the miraculous, so he is not blamed for that.' (2) Narrated by Abu Dawud (904) and al-Nasa'i (13/3) from the hadith of our master Abdullah ibn ...
Source pages p. 244

Commentary
This passage presents a proof that prophets must convey all of their revelation without omission. The argument is logical: if a prophet could commit an act contrary to what he was commanded (i.e., conceal part of revelation), then believers would be required to imitate that act, leading them to also conceal beneficial knowledge. But concealing such knowledge is forbidden and its doer is cursed, as proven by the Qur'anic verse from Surah al-Baqarah (2:159). Therefore, it is impossible for prophets to conceal any part of revelation. This is further supported by the verse from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:67), where God tells the Prophet that failure to convey any part of the message is equivalent to not conveying it at all. The author then comments on the Prophet's intense fear of God, which was proportional to his knowledge, citing a hadith about a bubbling sound from his chest. The footnotes explain the interpretation of the verse and provide the hadith source.

Key Terms
برهان وجوب الثالث
تبليغ
كتمان
عصمة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think a prophet could fail to convey some parts without consequence.
Correction: The proof shows that if a prophet concealed, we would be commanded to imitate him, but concealment is cursed, so it is impossible.

Checkpoint
According to the proof, what would be required of believers if prophets could conceal some revelation?
A) They would be free to do the same.
B) They would be commanded to imitate that concealment, which is impossible because concealment is cursed.
C) They would be excused from following some parts.
D) They would be required to obey only the majority.

Key Takeaway
Prophets must convey all revelation because failure to do so would oblige believers to imitate an act that is cursed, making it impossible for the infallible prophets.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are there any truths from the Quran or Sunnah that you know but have been silent about because you feared the reaction of others? What would it take for you to speak, knowing that concealing the truth is cursed?
?
The Prophet's chest boiled like a cauldron from fear of Allah, yet he never failed to convey a single letter. Does your knowledge of Allah produce a fear that moves you to action? What is standing between your knowledge and your obedience?
?
If you were judged by the standard of Quran 5:67—that omitting even a part of what you are entrusted to convey renders your entire mission void—would you be found faithful? What are you holding back today that you must deliver?

Prophethood
beginner
4 min
The Prophet's Perfect Delivery and the Distinction Between Completeness and Perfection
Sanusi cites Quranic verses to prove prophetic perfect delivery and explains kamal/tamam distinction.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Quranic verses testify to the Prophet's complete delivery, and how Sanusi distinguishes between kamal (completeness) and tamam (perfection) using the example of 'ten complete'.

Core Idea
The Prophet delivered the message perfectly in both essence and details.

In this passage, Imam al-Sanusi establishes that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) delivered the message with absolute perfection. He cites three Quranic verses as divine testimony. Then he unpacks a subtle distinction between two terms: tamam, meaning perfection of the essence, and ikmal, meaning completeness of the attributes. This distinction helps us understand the fullness of Prophetic delivery.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once and then the literal translation. Let the author's own wording and Quranic references settle in before analysis.
Notice that the passage flows from divine testimony to a technical distinction.
2
Identify the three Quranic verses
The passage cites three verses: 5:3, 2:256, and 51:54. For each, consider how it supports the idea that the Prophet delivered the message perfectly and is not to be blamed.
Verse 5:3 speaks of perfection and completion, verse 2:256 of clarity, verse 51:54 of not being blamed.
3
Understand the kamal/tamam distinction
Sanusi explains that tamam removes deficiency of the essence (asl), while ikmal removes deficiency of the accidents (awarid) while the essence is already perfect. Reflect on how this distinction applies to the Prophet's delivery.
The Quranic phrase 'ten complete' (2:196) illustrates that the number ten is perfect in essence but its attributes (like quality) may need completion.
4
Consider the significance
Ask yourself: Why does this distinction matter? It shows that the Prophet conveyed both the essential message and all its details without any deficiency.
This guards against the misconception that the Prophet only delivered the gist but not the particulars.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد شهد مولانا جل وعزَّ لسيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ بكمال التبليغ ، فقال تعالى : ﴿ الْيَوْمَ أَكْمَلْتُ لَكُمْ دِينَكُمْ وَأَتَمَمْتُ عَلَيْكُمْ نِعْمَتِي وَرَضِيتُ لَكُمُ الْإِسْلَامَ دِينًا ﴾ [المائدة : ٣] ، وقال تعالى : ﴿ لَا إِكْرَاهَ فِي الدِّينِ قَد تَبَيَّنَ الرُّشْدُ مِنَ الْغَيِّ ﴾ [البقرة : ٢٥٦] ، وقال تعالى : ﴿ فَتَوَلَّ عَنْهُمْ فَمَا أَنتَ بِمَلُومٍ ﴾ [الذاريات : ٥٤] ، والآي في ذلك كثيرةٌ ، وبالله تعالى التوفيق . وفي الآية إشارة إلى الفرق بين الكمال والتمام ؛ فإن التمام لإزالة نقص الأصل والإكمال لإزالة نقص العوارض مع تمام الأصل ، ومن ثم قال : ﴿ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَةٌ ﴾ [البقرة : ١٩٦] ؛ لأن التمام في العدد قد علم ، وإنما بقي احتمال نقص بعض صفاته .
And our Lord, Glorified and Exalted, testified for our master and lord Muhammad, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, with the perfection of delivery. So He, the Most High, said: 'This day I have perfected for you your religion and completed My favor upon you and have approved for you Islam as a religion' [Al-Ma'idah 5:3], and He, the Most High, said: 'There is no compulsion in religion; the right course has become clear from the wrong' [Al-Baqarah 2:256], and He, the Most High, said: 'So turn away from them, for you are not to be blamed' [Adh-Dhariyat 51:54]; and the verses in that matter are many. And with Allah the Most High is success. And in the verse there is an indication to the difference between completeness (al-kamal) and perfection (al-tamam); indeed, perfection (al-tamam) is for removing the deficiency of the essence, and completeness (al-ikmal) is for removing the deficiency of the accidents along with the perfection of the essence. And from that He said: 'ten complete (kamilah)' [Al-Baqarah 2:196], because the perfection of the number is known, and only the possibility of deficiency in some of its attributes remained.
Source pages p. 246

Commentary
This passage is a proof from the Quran for the perfection of the Prophet's delivery of the message. It begins by stating that Allah Himself testified to the Prophet's complete delivery. Then three verses are cited: 1) Verse 5:3 which states that Allah perfected the religion and completed His favor, indicating the finality and completeness of the Prophet's mission. 2) Verse 2:256 which states there is no compulsion in religion, implying the Prophet's clear presentation. 3) Verse 51:54 which tells the Prophet to turn away from those who reject, as he is not to blame, showing his duty was only to convey. The author then notes that many verses support this. After this, the passage explains a theological nuance: the difference between كمال (completeness) and تمام (perfection). It argues that التمام (perfection) refers to removing the deficiency of the essence itself (i.e., the original elements). Whereas الإكمال (making complete) refers to removing any deficiency in the accidental attributes while the essence is already perfect. This is illustrated by the Quranic phrase 'عشر كاملة' (ten complete) in verse 2:196, where the number ten is perfect in its category, but there could still be a deficiency in some of its attributes (like quality). So completeness implies perfection of essence plus perfection of attributes. The lesson thus uses Quranic evidence to show the Prophet's message was fully delivered in both essence and details.

Key Terms
كمال التبليغ
تمام
إكمال
الأصل
العوارض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That kamal and tamam are synonymous and interchangeable terms.
Correction: Tamam refers to perfection of the essence (removing its deficiency), while ikmal refers to completing the accidents (removing their deficiency) while the essence is already perfect.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the Quranic verse 'اليوم أكملت لكم دينكم' indicate regarding the prophetic mission?
A) That the Prophet's message was complete in essence but not in details
B) That Allah perfected the religion and the Prophet delivered it perfectly without any deficiency in essence or accidents
C) That the religion was perfect, but the Prophet's delivery was not fully complete
D) That the religion was only complete for the Arabs

Key Takeaway
The Quranic verses and Sanusi's analysis show that the Prophet delivered the message with complete perfection in both essence and details.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on the fact that Allah has perfected the religion in both essence and details, are you content with following the Sunnah completely, or do you pick and choose based on your convenience? Which aspect of the Prophet's teachings have you been neglecting, and what will you do to change that starting today?
?
The Prophet delivered the message so clearly that no compulsion is needed, yet many of us are hesitant to share it. Is your silence about Islam due to a lack of trust that the message is indeed complete and clear? How can you personally testify to the clarity of the Quran in your daily interactions?
?
The distinction between tamam and kamal shows that every detail of the religion has been perfected. Consider one small act of the Prophet you often dismiss as cultural or trivial—such as entering with the right foot or a specific supplication. If the Prophet was sent to perfect all details, can you still see that act as insignificant? What would it take to implement it consistently?

Proof of Human Attributes in Prophets
Sanusi presents the proof of permissibility of human attributes in prophets with wisdoms and a crucial clarification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the rational proof that human attributes like illness are permissible for prophets and that they do not impair their spiritual rank.

Core Idea
Human attributes in prophets serve higher purposes and never diminish their spiritual perfection.

Sanusi presents a proof based on observation to establish that prophets experienced human conditions like illness. He then explains the wisdoms behind these occurrences and clarifies that such attributes only affect the outer body, not the prophetic heart and its knowledges.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own structure come through before you interpret.
Notice that the passage opens with a direct statement of the proof.
2
Identify the proof and the four wisdoms
The passage states the proof is the observed occurrence. Then it lists four possible wisdoms for why human attributes happen to prophets. Find and understand each wisdom.
The wisdoms are introduced by 'إِمَّا لِتَعْظِيم أَجْرِهِمْ ، أَوْ لِلتَّشْرِيعِ ، أَوْ لِلنَّسَلِّي عَنِ الدُّنْيَا ، وَالثَّنَبهِ لِخِسَّة قَدْرِهَا...'
3
Understand the distinction between body and heart
Sanusi clarifies that attributes like illness only affect the apparent body, not the heart which contains divine knowledges and lights. This protects prophetic perfection.
The footnote about 'الفطنة' shows this condition also establishes other attributes for prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بَرْهَانُ جَوَازِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ - صَلَوَاتُ اللهِ وَسَلامُهُ عَلَيْهِمْ - : فَمُشَاهَدَةُ وُقُوعِهَا بِهِمْ ؛ إِمَّا لِتَعْظِيم أَجْرِهِمْ ، أَوْ لِلتَّشْرِيعِ ، أَوْ لِلنَّسَلِّي عَنِ الدُّنْيَا ، وَالثَّنَبهِ لِخِسَّة قَدْرِهَا عِنْدَ اللهِ تَعَالَى ، وَعَدَمِ رِضَاهُ تَعَالَى بِهَا دَارَ جَزَاءِ لِأَوْلِيَائِهِ (١) ؛ بِأَعْتِبَارِ أَحْوَالِهِمْ فِيهَا عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ . يَعْنِي : أَنَّ الْأَعْرَاضَ الْبَشَرِيَّةَ لَا يَقَعُ مِنْهَا بِالْأَنْبِيَاءِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ إِلَّا مَا لَا يُخِلُّ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ مَقَامَاتِهِمْ ، وَلَا يَقْدَحُ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ مَرَاتِبِهِمْ . فَالْمَرَضُ مَثَلًا وَإِنْ كَانَ يَقَعُ بِهِمْ فَحَدُّهُ مِنْهُمُ الْبَدَنُ الظَّاهِرُ ، أَمَّا قُلُوبُهُمْ بِاعْتِبَارِ مَا فِيهَا مِنَ الْمَعَارِفِ وَالْأَنْوَارِ الَّتِي لَا يَعْلَمُ قَدْرَهَا إِلَّا مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي مَنَّ عَلَيْهِمْ بِهَا .. فَلَا يُخِلُّ الْمَرَضُ وَنَحْوُهُ بِقُلَامَةِ . (١) كذا في جميع النسخ ، والمعنى: وعدم رضاه تعالى بها دار جزاء لأوليائه فضلاً عن أنبيائه الذين هم سادات أوليائه ؛ إذ نفي الأعم مقتض لنفي الأخصّ . (٢) وبهذا القيد ثبتت لهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام الفطنة ، وغيرها من الصفات التي رأى العلامة ياسين - كما تقدم النقل عنه ( ص ٢٣٤ ) - أنها من الصفات الثابتة بالشرع أو العادة
The proof of the permissibility of human attributes upon them – the prayers and peace of Allah be upon them – is the observation of their occurrence with them; either for the magnification of their reward, or for legislation, or for detachment from the world, and to draw attention to the lowliness of its worth with Allah the Most High, and that He the Most High is not pleased with it as an abode of recompense for His saints; considering their states in it, upon them be prayers and peace. That is: human attributes do not occur to the prophets, upon them be prayer and peace, except that which does not impair any of their stations (maqamat), nor does it detract from any of their ranks (maratib). For illness, for example, even if it occurs to them, its limit from them is the apparent body. As for their hearts, considering what is in them of knowledges (ma'arif) and lights (anwar) whose extent none knows except our Lord, Glorified and Exalted, who bestowed them upon them... then illness and the like do not impair even a nail-paring of it. (Footnote 1: Thus in all copies, and the meaning: And that He the Most High is not pleased with it as an abode of recompense for His saints, let alone His prophets who are the masters of His saints; for the negation of the general necessitates the negation of the specific. (2) And by this condition, discernment (al-fitnah) and other attributes which the scholar Yasin – as the citation from him preceded (p. 234) – considered to be among the attributes established by law or custom became established for them, upon them be prayer and peace.)
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a proof (برهان) for the permissibility of human attributes (الأعراض البشرية) occurring to prophets. The proof is observational: we see such attributes like illness, hunger, etc., happening to them. The author then lists possible wisdoms behind these occurrences: 1) To increase their reward, 2) To establish legal rulings (التشريع), 3) To promote detachment from worldly life, and 4) To highlight the lowliness of this world in Allah's sight, and that He does not intend it as a reward for His saints. The author then interprets: These attributes only occur to prophets in a way that does not impair their stations (مقامات) or detract from their ranks (مراتب). For example, illness only affects the external body, not the heart which contains divine knowledges and lights. The footnote clarifies that the phrase 'His saints' includes prophets by implication (negation of general includes specific). Additionally, the footnote mentions that this condition (i.e., not impairing stations) establishes attributes like 'الفطنة' (discernment, intelligence) for prophets, as noted by the scholar Yasin, as attributes confirmed by law or custom. Thus, the passage defends the prophetic perfection by showing that human frailties are only outward and do not affect their spiritual rank or mission.

Key Terms
الأعراض البشرية
جواز
مقامات
مراتب
الفطنة
التشريع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Any human attribute like illness would diminish prophetic perfection and rank.
Correction: The passage clarifies that these attributes only affect the outer body, not the spiritual heart and its knowledges, and they actually serve higher wisdoms.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary proof that human attributes are permissible for prophets?
A) The logical necessity that prophets must experience all human conditions
B) The observed occurrence of such attributes in prophets
C) The unanimous consensus of scholars
D) The Quranic verses stating that prophets are human

Key Takeaway
Human attributes in prophets are permissible and do not detract from their spiritual rank; they affect only the body and serve divine wisdoms.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear about prophets suffering illness or hardship, do your thoughts align with the lesson's explanation that this only affects their bodies, not their hearts? Reflect on a time when you assumed a prophet's external condition reflected their spiritual state. How does this lesson challenge that assumption?
?
The lesson says one wisdom behind human attributes in prophets is to detach them from the world. In your own life, what hardship or trial has Allah used to remind you of the lowliness of this world? Will you embrace detachment more sincerely after this lesson?
?
The passage distinguishes between the prophets' outward body and inward heart filled with divine lights. How often do you judge others (or yourself) by external appearances, neglecting the spiritual realities known only to Allah? What concrete step can you take to focus on hearts rather than bodies?

Prophethood

5 min
Human Accidents upon Prophets: Proof and Spiritual Protection
Sanusi proves and explains the permissibility of human accidents upon prophets.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the proof that human accidents befall prophets and why these accidents do not diminish their spiritual perfection.

Core Idea
Prophets face human hardships, yet their hearts remain untouched by imperfection.

Sanusi presents a proof based on observation: prophets do experience illness, hunger, and other human conditions. However, he immediately clarifies that these affect only the outer body, leaving their hearts filled with divine cognitions and lights unaffected. This lesson explores the proof, the purposes behind these accidents, and the crucial distinction between outer and inner states.

Guided Path
1
Observe the proof
The passage begins with the proof: we see accidents happen to prophets. Notice the four purposes given: magnification of reward, legislation, weaning from the world, and showing the world's lowliness.
The proof is direct observation, not theoretical reasoning.
2
Understand the limitation
Sanusi explains that only accidents that do not impair their stations occur. Focus on the example of illness: it only touches the body, not the heart. The heart's cognitions and lights remain intact.
Illness does not cause vexation, deviation, or weakness of inner powers.
3
Reflect on the spiritual state
Hunger and sleep do not dominate their hearts; their eyes sleep but hearts do not. Their hearts constantly glow with lights and ascent in proximity. The benefit of outward afflictions is the magnification of their reward.
The prophets' performance of duties remains perfect in all states.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا دَلِيلُ جَوَازِ الْأَعْرَاضِ الْبَشَرِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِمْ - صَلَوَاتُ اللهِ وَسَلامُهُ عَلَيْهِمْ - : فَمُشَاهَدَةُ وُقُوعِهَا بِهِمْ ؛ إِمَّا لِتَعْظِيم أَجْرِهِمْ ، أَوْ لِلتَّشْرِيعِ ، أَوْ لِلنَّسَلِّي عَنِ الدُّنْيَا ، وَالثَّنَبهِ لِخِسَّة قَدْرِهَا عِنْدَ اللهِ تَعَالَى ، وَعَدَمِ رِضَاهُ تَعَالَى بِهَا دَارَ جَزَاءِ لِأَوْلِيَائِهِ ؛ بِأَعْتِبَارِ أَحْوَالِهِمْ فِيهَا عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ
يعني : أنّ الأعراض البشرية لا يقعُ منها بالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام إلا ما لا يُخِل بشيءٍ مِنْ مقاماتِهم ، ولا يقدح بشيءٍ مِنْ مراتبهم
فالمرض مثلاً وإنْ كانَ يقعُ بهم فحده منهم البدنُ الظاهرُ ، أَمَّا قلوبهم باعتبارِ ما فيها مِنَ المعارفِ والأنوار التي لا يعلمُ قدرَها إلا مولانا جل وعزَّ الذي مَنَّ عليهم بها .. فلا يُخِلُّ المرضُ ونحوُهُ بقُلامةِ ظُفُرِ منها ، ولا يكدِّرُ شيئاً مِنْ صفوها ، ولا يوجب لهم ضجراً ولا انحرافاً ولا ضعفاً لقواهم الباطنة أصلاً كما هو كذلك موجود في حق غيرهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام
وكذا الجوع والنوم لا يستولي على شيءٍ مِنْ قلوبهم ، ولهذا تنام أعينهم ولا تنام قلوبهم
وحال قلوبهم في توهجها بأنوارِ المعارفِ ، والحضور والترقّي في منازلِ القُرْبِ التي لم يَحُمْ أَحدٌ ممَّنْ سواهم حول أدنى شيءٍ منها ، وقيامهم بالوظائف التي كُلّفوا بها في الحضر والسفرِ والصحة والمرض أكمل قيام.. هو على حد السواء في جميع الأحوال
فوائد نزولِ الأعراض البشرية بالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام ] وفائدة إصابةِ ظواهرهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام بتلك الأعراض البشرية : ما أشرنا إليه في أصلِ العقيدةِ ؛ مِنْ تعظيم أجرهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام
As for the proof of the permissibility of human accidents upon them (may Allah's prayers and peace be upon them): it is the observation of their occurrence with them; either to magnify their reward, or for legislation, or to wean from the world, and to point out the lowness of its value with Allah most high, and His most high not being pleased with it as a recompense for His friends; in consideration of their states in it – upon them be prayer and peace. He means: that of the human accidents, only that which does not impair anything of their stations nor detract from anything of their ranks occurs to the prophets (upon them be prayer and peace). So illness, for example, even if it occurs to them, its limit is the outward body; as for their hearts, in consideration of what they contain of cognitions and lights whose extent none knows except our Lord, mighty and majestic, who bestowed them upon them, illness and the like does not impair a fingernail clipping of that, nor does it disturb anything of their clarity, nor does it cause them vexation, deviation, or weakness of their inner powers at all, as is likewise found in the case of others besides them (upon them be prayer and peace). Likewise, hunger and sleep do not dominate anything of their hearts; therefore their eyes sleep but their hearts do not sleep. And the state of their hearts in their glowing with the lights of cognitions, presence, and ascent in the stations of proximity which no one else has even approached the nearest thing to them, and their performance of the duties they were charged with – in residence and travel, health and illness – a most perfect performance, is on the same level in all circumstances. Benefits of the descent of human accidents upon the prophets (upon them be prayer and peace): the benefit of their outward appearances (upon them be prayer and peace) being afflicted with those human accidents is what we indicated in the original creed: the magnification of their reward (upon them be prayer and peace).
Source pages p. 247

Commentary
This passage is a proof and explanation regarding the permissibility of human accidents (al-aʿrāḍ al-bashariyya) befalling the prophets. The author begins by stating the proof: it is the observed occurrence of such accidents upon them. The purposes of these accidents are four: (1) to magnify their reward, (2) for legislation (al-tashrīʿ), i.e., to teach others how to bear hardships, (3) to wean them from attachment to the world and show its lowliness before Allah, and (4) that Allah is not pleased with this world as a recompense for His friends. The author then clarifies the meaning: only those accidents that do not impair the prophets' lofty stations or detract from their ranks occur to them. He illustrates with the example of illness: it only affects the outward body, not their hearts, which are filled with divine cognitions (maʿārif) and lights (anwār). Illness does not disturb their inner clarity, cause vexation, deviation, or weakness of their inner powers. Similarly, hunger and sleep do not dominate their hearts; thus their eyes sleep but their hearts remain awake, as in the famous hadith. The state of their hearts in glowing with lights, spiritual presence, and ascent in the stations of closeness to Allah remains constant regardless of physical states. Finally, the benefit of these outward afflictions is the magnification of their reward, as previously mentioned in the creed.

Key Terms
الأعراض البشرية (human accidents)
الأنبياء (prophets)
المشاهدة (observation)
التعظيم (magnification)
المعارف (cognitions)
الأنوار (lights)
القلوب (hearts)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that prophets experiencing illness or hunger implies imperfection or that their spiritual state is affected.
Correction: This passage clarifies that these accidents only affect the outward body, never diminishing their inner perfection and spiritual state.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is one purpose for prophets experiencing human accidents such as illness?
A) To show that they are weak like ordinary humans
B) To magnify their reward
C) To prove that they are not sinless
D) To distract them from worship

Key Takeaway
Prophets experience human accidents outwardly, but their hearts remain spiritually untouched, and these accidents serve higher purposes like magnifying their reward.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial, do you immediately assume it is a punishment or a sign of God's displeasure? How does the lesson that prophets' hardships magnify their reward challenge your perspective? What would it take for you to embrace hardships as opportunities for spiritual elevation, as the prophets did?
?
The passage says that prophets' hearts are never disturbed by illness or hunger. Reflect on a recent difficulty that disturbed your inner peace. What does that reveal about the strength of your faith? How can you cultivate a heart that, like the prophets', remains firmly attached to Allah even in hardship?
?
If the world is so lowly in Allah's sight that He does not make it a recompense for His friends, how much of your heart is still tied to worldly comforts and successes? What step will you take today to 'wean' yourself from the world, even by a small act of detachment?

The Wisdom Behind Prophets' Human Experiences
Sanusi explains two benefits of prophets' human afflictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Allah chooses to involve prophets in human hardships and how these experiences serve both to magnify their reward and to provide practical legislative examples for the community.

Core Idea
Prophets' trials are not pointless; they magnify reward and teach us how to worship.

This passage from Sanusi's commentary addresses a common question: why do prophets suffer? It explains that these experiences serve divine wisdom—they increase the prophets' reward and provide practical examples for Islamic law. By examining the Prophet's actions, we gain stronger rulings than from words alone.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the literal translation. Notice the two benefits Sanusi identifies and the objection he answers.
The passage ends with a commentary note from Yasin.
2
Understand the first benefit: increased reward
Identify how prophets' hardships magnify their reward, as supported by the hadith. Reflect on why Allah does not simply grant reward without hardships.
Consider Allah's justice and wisdom as described.
3
Understand the second benefit: legislative rulings
See how the Prophet's actions in illness, forgetfulness, and eating become precedents for Islamic rulings. Compare the strength of action versus speech as evidence.
The objection and answer clarify why action is stronger than speech.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فوائد نزول الأعراض البشرية بالأنبياء عليهم الصلاة والسلام. وفائدة إصابة ظواهرهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام بتلك الأعراض البشرية: ما أشرنا إليه في أصل العقيدة؛ من تعظيم أجرهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام؛ وذلك كما في أمراضهم وجوعهم وإذاية الخلق لهم، ولهذا قال صلى الله عليه وسلم: أشدكم بلاء الأنبياء، ثم الأمثل فالأمثل. ومولانا جل وعز قادر أن يوصل لهم ذلك الثواب الأعظم بلا مشقة تلحقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام، لكن بعدله جل وعلا وعظيم حكمته التي لا تحصرها العقول اختار أن يوصل لهم ذلك الثواب الأعظم مع تلك الأعراض، يفعل ما يشاء، لا يسأل جل وعز عما يفعل تبارك وتعالى. ومن فوائد نزول تلك الأعراض بهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام: تشريع الأحكام المتعلقة بها للخلق، كما عرفنا أحكام السهو في الصلاة من سهو سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلى الله عليه وسلم، وكيف تؤدى الصلاة في حال المرض والخوف من فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام لها عند ذلك، وعرفنا هيئة أكل الطعام وشرب الشراب من أكله وشربه. لا يقال: يمكن معرفة أحكام السهو بالإخبار؛ إذ هذا السهو الشريف منه صلى الله عليه وسلم في ترسيخ الحكم أقوى؛ لأن دلالة الفعل أقوى من دلالة القول؛ إذ لا يفعل بنفسه صلى الله عليه وسلم إلا الأفضل، بخلاف القول؛ إذ يعتقد فيه الترخيص، فيخالفه المكلف ارتكاباً للمشقة. مفاد ياسين.
Benefits of the descent of human afflictions upon the prophets, peace be upon them. And the benefit of the prophets' outward selves being afflicted with those human afflictions: what we indicated in the original creed: to magnify their reward, peace be upon them; such as in their illnesses, hunger, and harm from people. And for this he, peace be upon him, said: 'The most severely tried of people are the prophets, then the closest, then the closest.' And our Lord, Exalted and Glorified, is able to deliver to them that greatest reward without hardship afflicting them, peace be upon them, but by His justice, Exalted and Glorified, and His immense wisdom that minds cannot encompass, He chose to deliver that greatest reward with those afflictions. He does what He wills, He is not asked about what He does, Blessed and Exalted. And among the benefits of the descent of those afflictions upon them, peace be upon them: the legislation of rulings related to them for the people, just as we learned the rulings of forgetfulness in prayer from the forgetfulness of our master and lord Muhammad, peace be upon him, and how prayer is performed in illness and fear from his action, peace be upon him, in that situation, and we learned the manner of eating food and drinking drink from his eating and drinking. It cannot be said: 'The rulings of forgetfulness could be known through report'; for this noble forgetfulness from him, peace be upon him, is stronger in establishing the ruling, because the indication of action is stronger than the indication of speech; since he does not do except the best, unlike speech, where concession may be believed, so the responsible person might oppose it to undertake hardship. (From the meaning of Yasin.)
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage discusses the wisdom behind prophets undergoing human experiences like illness, hunger, and harm. The author identifies two main benefits. First, these experiences magnify the prophets' reward, as indicated in the original creed. The Prophet himself stated that prophets face the severest trials. Allah, though able to grant reward without hardship, chooses to give them reward through these experiences due to His justice and wisdom. Second, these experiences serve as a basis for legislation. For example, the rulings on forgetfulness in prayer are derived from the Prophet's own forgetfulness, and the manner of performing prayer in illness and fear is known from his actions. Similarly, rules of eating and drinking come from his practice. The author then answers an objection: could we not derive these rulings from reports alone? He responds that action gives a stronger indication because the Prophet only does what is best, while speech may be interpreted as a concession, leading people to avoid it. This shows the superiority of deriving rulings from actions.

تشريع الأحكام
دلالة الفعل
دلالة القول

Misconception: Prophets' sufferings are pointless or indicate divine displeasure.
Correction: The passage shows these sufferings have divine wisdom: they increase prophets' reward and provide practical examples for the community's legislation.

B) To teach the community through their actions

D) To humble them

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

Are you running from trials that could be your pathway to a higher rank? Will you embrace one small difficulty for His sake today?
