The Divine Wisdom in Prophetic Afflictions
Author explains the divine wisdom behind prophetic afflictions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why God chooses to afflict prophets despite being able to reward them without hardship, and the role of His justice and wisdom.

Core Idea
God's justice and wisdom combine reward with affliction for prophets.

The hadith states that prophets suffer the greatest trials. This raises a question: if God can grant them the ultimate reward without any pain, why do they suffer? This passage reveals the divine rationale: it is an act of justice and wisdom that cannot be fully grasped by the human mind.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and opening statement
Begin by reading the Prophet's statement about the severity of affliction for prophets, and the author's premise that God could grant reward without hardship.
2
Identify the divine attributes invoked
Notice how the author references God's power, justice, and wisdom as the framework for understanding why affliction happens.
Justice ('adl) and wisdom (hikma) are key.
3
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that God does as He wills and is not questioned. This emphasizes divine sovereignty despite human questioning.
This is a reminder of tawheed in action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لهم ، ولهذا قال صلّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ : ( أَشَدُّكُمْ بَلاءَ الأَنْبِيَاءُ ، ثُمَّ الأَمْثَلُ فَالأَمْثَلُ ) ومولانا جل وعزَّ قادرٌ أنْ يُوصِلَ لهم ذلك الثواب الأعظم بلا مشقة تلحقهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام ، لكن بعدلِهِ جلَّ وعلا وعظيم حكمتِهِ التي لا تحصرها العقولُ .. اختارَ أنْ يُوصِلَ لهم ذلكَ الثوابَ الأعظمَ مع تلك الأعراض ، يفعل ما يشاءُ ، لا يُسأل جل وعزَّ عمَّا يفعلُ تبارك وتعالى ومن فوائدِ نزولِ تلكَ الأعراض بهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام : تشريع الأحكام المتعلقة بها للخلْقِ ، كما عرفنا أحكام السهو في الصلاةِ مِنْ سهو سيدنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ (۲) ، وكيف تؤدَّى الصلاة في حال المرض والخوفِ مِنْ فعلِهِ عليهِ الصلاةُ والسلام لها عندَ ذلك ، وعرفنا هيئة أكل الطعام وشرب الشرابِ مِنْ أكله وشربه صلَّى الله عليهِ وسلَّمَ ، وإلا فهو كانَ عليه الصلاة والسلام غنيّاً عن الطعام والشراب ؛ إذْ هو عليه الصلاة والسلامُ يبيتُ عندَ رَبِّهِ يطعمُهُ ويسقيه ) ، إلى غير ذلك
To them, and thus the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'The most severe of you in affliction are the prophets, then the most excellent, then the most excellent.' And our Master, Exalted and Mighty, is able to convey to them that greatest reward without hardship afflicting them, peace be upon them, but by His justice and immense wisdom, which minds cannot encompass, He chose to convey to them that greatest reward with those afflictions. He does what He wills, He is not asked about what He does, Blessed and Exalted. Among the benefits of the descent of those afflictions upon them, peace be upon them, is the legislation of rulings connected to them for creation, just as we have come to know the rulings of forgetfulness in prayer from the forgetfulness of our Master and Lord Muhammad (peace be upon him), and how prayer is performed in illness and fear from his action (peace be upon him) in that situation, and we have come to know the manner of eating food and drinking drink from his eating and drinking (peace be upon him), and otherwise he (peace be upon him) was independent of food and drink, for he (peace be upon him) spends the night with his Lord, feeding and watering him, etc.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is an exposition on the wisdom behind prophets experiencing severe afflictions. The author begins by citing the hadith that prophets suffer the greatest trials, then explains that God is fully capable of granting them the ultimate reward without any hardship. However, due to His justice and incomprehensible wisdom, He chooses to combine reward with affliction. The author then lists one major benefit: that such afflictions become a means of legislating rulings for the community. Examples include the rules of forgetfulness in prayer derived from the Prophet's own forgetfulness, how to pray when ill or fearful, and proper eating and drinking etiquette, all learned from the Prophet's actions—even though he himself did not need food or drink. This shows that the afflictions serve a legislative purpose.

الأنبياء
الثواب الأعظم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets suffer because God cannot protect them or reward them otherwise.
Correction: The passage clarifies that God is fully able to grant reward without hardship, but He chooses otherwise out of justice and wisdom.

Checkpoint

D) Because the prophets asked for trials.

Key Takeaway
Prophets suffer not because God is unable, but because His justice and wisdom choose to combine reward with affliction, demonstrating His sovereignty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
The passage says God is not asked about what He does. Have you ever questioned God's decree in your heart, wanting Him to justify Himself to you? How can you submit to His sovereignty without understanding the wisdom?

Detachment from Worldly Life through Prophetic Afflictions
The author explains that prophetic afflictions teach detachment from the world.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of detachment from the world as taught by prophetic afflictions, including its definition, benefits, and the rational basis for valuing it.

Core Idea
Prophetic hardships teach us to see the world as it truly is: worthless.

This lesson explores a profound benefit of the afflictions suffered by prophets: they teach us detachment from the world. The author explains that by witnessing how the prophets endured hardships and turned away from worldly allurements, we learn to find rest and pleasure in losing worldly things, recognizing their baseness in God's sight.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully, then the literal translation. Notice the key terms and the flow of the argument.
The passage is concise but rich in meaning.
2
Understand the definition of التسلي
The author defines 'al-tasalī 'an al-dunyā' as patience and finding rest/pleasure in losing worldly things. Reflect on how this differs from simple deprivation.
This is the core concept of the lesson.
3
Examine the rational evidence
The author points to the suffering of prophets and their turning away from worldly adornment as evidence of the world's low worth. Compare this to the wise person's attitude toward a putrid carcass.
The hadith 'The world is a putrid carcass' reinforces the point.
4
Apply the lesson
Consider how this teaching can shape your own relationship with worldly possessions and ambitions. Detachment does not mean rejecting necessities but not being deceived by superfluities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن فوائدها أيضاً : التسلي عن الدنيا ؛ أي : التصبر ووجود الراحةِ واللذَّةِ لفقدِها ، والتنبه لخسَّة قدرها عندَ اللهِ تعالى بما يراه العاقلُ مِنْ مقاساة هؤلاء الساداتِ الكرام خيرةِ اللهِ تعالى مِنْ خلقِهِ لشدائدها ، وإعراضهم عنها وعن زُخْرُفِها الذي غرَّ كثيراً مِنَ الحمقى إعراض العقلاء عن الجِيفِ والنجاساتِ ، ولهذا قال عليه الصلاة والسلام : ( الدُّنْيَا جِيفَةٌ قَذِرَةٌ ) ، ولم يأخذوا منها عليهم الصلاةُ
And among its benefits also: detachment from the world, i.e., enduring patiently and experiencing rest and pleasure in losing it, and being alerted to the baseness of its worth with God Almighty, by what the rational person sees of the suffering of these noble masters, the chosen of God Almighty from His creation, from its hardships, and their turning away from it and from its adornment which has deceived many fools, as the turning away of the wise from carcasses and impurities. And for this he (peace be upon him) said: 'The world is a putrid carcass,' and they (peace be upon them) took nothing from it.
Source pages p. 250

Commentary
This passage is a continuation of the author's enumeration of the benefits of afflictions upon prophets. Here he explains that another benefit is 'al-tasalī 'an al-dunyā', which means detachment or comfort in being deprived of worldly goods. The author clarifies that this detachment includes patience and finding rest and pleasure in lacking worldly things. This is achieved by recognizing the low value of the world in God's sight, as seen in how the prophets endured severe hardships and turned away from its glitter that deceives fools. The author likens it to wise people avoiding filth. He supports this by citing the hadith that the world is a foul carcass, and notes that the prophets took nothing from it.

Key Terms
التسلي عن الدنيا
التصبر
الراحة واللذّة
خسة قدر الدنيا
جيفة قذرة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That detachment from the world means rejecting all worldly necessities and living in complete asceticism.
Correction: Detachment (al-tasalī) means not being attached to worldly superfluities and not being deceived by its adornment, but it does not forbid permissible worldly needs. The prophets themselves engaged in lawful worldly activities while remaining detached in their hearts.

Checkpoint

A) Accumulating wealth for the afterlife.
B) Experiencing comfort and patience in losing worldly things.
C) Indulging in permissible pleasures.
D) Seeking worldly honor to serve religion.

Key Takeaway
Prophetic afflictions teach us that detachment from the world is a virtue that brings rest and pleasure by recognizing the world's low value and following the prophets' example.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you lose something you love, do you find rest or despair? How does the example of the prophets' detachment challenge you to respond differently to loss starting today?
?
What specific worldly adornment—status, wealth, relationships—are you most attached to? If it were stripped away, would you still feel peace? What one step can you take this week to loosen your grip on it?
?
The world is a putrid carcass—do you live like you believe this? Examine your daily worries and ambitions: how much of your energy goes toward something the prophets turned away from? What will you change today?

The Shahada's Implication: Belief in All Prophets and the Unseen
Sanusi explains that the Shahada entails belief in all prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that declaring Muhammad as Allah's Messenger logically requires believing in all that he confirmed, including previous prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day.

Core Idea
The Shahada does not stop at Muhammad—it affirms all messengers.

When a Muslim says 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah,' it is not a statement about Muhammad alone. It is a declaration that carries forward to every truth he endorsed. This passage shows how the second part of the Shahada includes faith in all the prophets, angels, heavenly books, and the Last Day, because Muhammad came confirming all of that.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice how Sanusi connects the Shahada to broader beliefs.
The passage is concise—focus on the logical connection.
2
Identify the included beliefs
List the four categories mentioned: all prophets, angels, heavenly books, and the Last Day.
These are the core articles of faith that the Shahada entails.
3
Understand the reasoning
The passage gives a reason: 'because he came confirming all of that.' This shows that the Shahada is not a bare statement but implies acceptance of everything the Prophet confirmed.
4
Reflect on the scope
Consider how this principle unifies all prophetic messages. Ask yourself: Does your declaration of faith include all these elements?
This connects belief in Muhammad with belief in earlier prophets.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لَا خَفَاءَ فِي صِدْقِ مَا ذُكِرَ، وَتَتَبُّعُ كَلَامِهِ بِالِاسْتِقْرَاءِ يَشْهَدُ لَهُ وَلَيْسَ الْخَبَرُ كَالْعِيَانِ. مَا يَلْزَمُ عَنْ قَوْلِنَا: (مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ) وَأَمَّا قَوْلُنَا: (مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ) فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الْإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الْأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالْمَلَائِكَةِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ، وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ، وَالْيَوْمِ الْآخِرِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ. لَا شَكَّ أَنَّ تَصْدِيقَ سَيِّدِنَا وَمَوْلَانَا مُحَمَّدٍ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ فِي رِسَالَتِهِ بِحَسَبِ مَا دَلَّتْ عَلَيْهِ مُعْجِزَاتُهُ الَّتِي لَا حَصْرَ لَهَا، وَالْإِقْرَارَ بِذَلِكَ يَسْتَلْزِمُ التَّصْدِيقَ بِكُلِّ مَا جَاءَ بِهِ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلَامُ. وَمِنْ جُمْلَةِ مَا أَتَى بِهِ مَا ذُكِرَ هُنَا، وَكَذَا غَيْرُ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا لَا يَنْحَصِرُ؛ كَالْبَعْثِ لِعَيْنِ هَذَا الْبَدَنِ لَا لِمِثْلِهِ، وَفِتْنَةِ الْقَبْرِ وَعَذَابِهِ، وَالصِّرَاطِ، وَالْمِيزَانِ، وَالْحَوْضِ، وَالشَّفَاعَةِ، وَغَيْرِ ذَلِكَ مِمَّا يَطُولُ تَتَبُّعُهُ، وَهُوَ مُفَصَّلٌ فِي الْكِتَابِ وَالسُّنَّةِ وَتَأْلِيفِ عُلَمَاءِ الشَّرِيعَةِ.
There is no concealment in the truth of what was mentioned, and following his words by induction bears witness to it, and news is not like eyewitness. What follows from our statement: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him).' As for our statement: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him),' it includes faith in all the prophets and angels, peace be upon them, and the heavenly books, and the Last Day; because he, peace and blessings be upon him, came confirming all of that. There is no doubt that the truthfulness of our master and lord Muhammad (peace be upon him) in his message, according to what his miracles, which are countless, indicate, and acknowledgment of that necessitates belief in everything he brought, peace and blessings be upon him. Among what he brought is what is mentioned here, and likewise other things that are not limited; such as the resurrection of this very body, not a similar one, and the trial of the grave and its punishment, and the Path, and the Scale, and the Basin, and the Intercession, and other things whose pursuit is lengthy, and it is detailed in the Book and the Sunnah and the works of the scholars of the Sharia.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage explains the logical implications of declaring 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah.' The author first asserts that what has been said is true and that induction supports it, though secondhand report (khabar) is not like direct witness (ʿiyan). Then the main point: saying that Muhammad is Allah's Messenger necessarily includes faith in all previous prophets, angels, the heavenly books, and the Last Day, because Muhammad came confirming all of that. The reason given is that his countless miracles prove his truthfulness, and acknowledging him as a messenger requires believing everything he conveyed. The author then lists specific eschatological beliefs that are part of what he brought: the resurrection of this very body (not a substitute), the trial and punishment of the grave, the Sirat (bridge), the Mizan (scale), the Hawd (basin), and al-Shafaʿa (intercession). The passage concludes that these matters are extensively detailed in the Quran, Sunnah, and works of Sharia scholars.

الملائكة
الكتب السماوية
اليوم الآخر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception: Some think 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' only affirms Muhammad's prophethood, not other prophets or unseen matters.
Correction: The Shahada includes faith in all previous prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day because Muhammad confirmed them.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does saying 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' include?
A) Faith in Muhammad alone
B) Faith in all prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day
C) Faith in resurrection and accountability
D) Faith in the Quran only

Key Takeaway
Declaring Muhammad as Allah's Messenger logically requires affirming all that he confirmed: previous prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the Shahada in your daily prayers, do you consciously affirm belief in all prophets, angels, books, and the Last Day, or have you reduced it to a mere statement about Allah and Muhammad? Will you today deliberately meditate on the full implications of your testimony?
?
If the Shahada commits you to believe in all previous scriptures, how do you currently view the Torah and Gospel? Are you honoring them as Allah's revelation in your heart, or do you dismiss them? What is one concrete step you can take this week to show respect for the earlier books?
?
The Shahada also binds you to belief in the Last Day. Does your daily life reflect a genuine expectation of judgment? Identify one specific behavior you engage in that you would not want to be caught doing when the Hour arrives. What will you change starting today?

The Eschatological Articles of Faith Confirmed by the Prophet
Sanusi enumerates specific eschatological beliefs that are part of what the Prophet brought.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will know the specific eschatological events that the Prophet brought, which a believer must affirm.

Core Idea
The Prophet's message includes detailed realities of the afterlife.

The Shahada does not only point to general beliefs—it extends to specific events that will occur after death. In this passage, Sanusi lists several of these: the resurrection of this very body, the trial of the grave, the Path, the Scale, the Basin, and Intercession. These are all part of what the Prophet conveyed, and a believer must accept them.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that this passage lists specific eschatological items.
These are all 'samiyyat'—matters known from revelation.
2
Identify the listed items
Find and note each item: resurrection of the very body, trial of the grave, Path, Scale, Basin, Intercession.
The text also mentions there are more, not limited to these.
3
Understand the significance
These are not optional beliefs; they are necessary consequences of accepting Muhammad's message. The passage says they are detailed in the Book and Sunnah.
Belief in these is part of faith in the Unseen.
4
Reflect on personal belief
Consider whether you affirm each of these events. The passage reminds us that the Prophet taught them, so we must believe.
This connects to the learning objective.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
Intercession on that Day is only for those whom Allah permits. Are you living in such a way that you can hope for the Prophet’s intercession, or are you relying on empty claims without deeds?

What the Shahada Implies: Belief in All Prophets, Angels, and the Hereafter
The author enumerates what is entailed by the testimony of Muhammad's messengerhood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the testimony 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' necessarily entails belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, the Last Day, and specific eschatological events.

Core Idea
The shahada to Muhammad's messengerhood includes everything he confirmed.

The author begins by unpacking the implications of the second part of the shahada. Saying 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' is not a standalone statement; it ties together the entire fabric of Islamic belief because the Prophet confirmed all previous revelations and eschatological truths. This passage shows how one testimony carries the weight of many doctrines.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening statement
Read the Arabic text and translation of the first part. Focus on the phrase 'there enters into it faith in all the prophets...'
2
Identify the specific items listed
List the items that the author says are included in the shahada: faith in all prophets, angels, scriptures, Last Day, resurrection of the body, grave trial, Sirat, Balance, Basin, intercession, etc.
3
Reflect on the reasoning
Understand why these are entailed: because Muhammad came confirming all of them, and his miracles prove his truthfulness, so we must believe everything he brought.
The author also notes that the list is not exhaustive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا قَوْلُنَا : ( مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ ( صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ : فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالْمَلَائِكَةِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلامُ ، وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ ، وَالْيَوْمِ الآخِرِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ . لا شك أنَّ تصديق سيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في رسالتِهِ بحَسَبِ ما دلّتْ عليهِ معجزاتُهُ التي لا حصر لها ، والإقرار بذلك .. يستلزم التصديق بكل ما جاءَ بهِ عليه الصلاة والسلام . ومن جملة ما أتى بهِ ماذكر هنا، وكذا غير ذلكَ ممَّا لا ينحصر ؛ كالبعث لعين هذا البدنِ لا لمثلِهِ ، وفتنة القبر وعذابه ، والصراطِ ، والميزان ، والحوض ، والشفاعة ، وغير ذلك مما يطولُ تتبعه ، وهو مفصل في الكتاب والسنة وتأليف علماء الشريعة . وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ : وُجُوبُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ ، وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الْكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِمْ ، وَإِلا لَمْ يَكُونُوا رُسُلاً أمَنَاءَ لِمَوْلانَا الْعَالِم بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ ، وَاسْتِحَالَةُ فِعْل الْمَنْهَيَّاتِ كُلِّهَا ؛ لِأَنَّهُمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ أُرْسِلُوا لِيُعَلِّمُوا الْخَلْقَ بِأَفْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَسُكُوتِهِمْ ، فَيَلْزَمُ أَلَا يَكُونَ فِي جَمِيعِهَا مُخَالَفَةٌ لِأَمْرِ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي اخْتَارَهُمْ عَلَى جَمِيعِ الْخَلْقِ ، وَأَمِنَهُمْ عَلَى سِرِّ وَحْيِهِ . لا شكّ أنَّ إضافة ( الرسولِ ) إلى ( الله ) تعالى تقتضي أنَّهُ جَلَّ وعزَّ اختارَهُ للرسالة كما اختار إخوانَهُ المرسلين لذلكَ ، وقد علمتَ أنَّ علمه تعالى محيط بما لا نهاية له ، وأنَّ الجهل وما في معناه مستحيل على الله تعالى ، فلزمَ أنَّ تصديقَهُ تعالى لهم مطابق لما علمهُ تعالى منهم مِنَ الصدق والأمانة ، فيستحيلُ أنْ يكونوا في نفس الأمر على خلافِ ما علمَهُ تعالى منهم ، وقد أمر تعالى بالاقتداء بهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام في أقوالهم وأفعالهم ، فيلزم أن يكون جميعها على ما يُرضيه تعالى .
And as for our saying: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace)', there enters into it faith in all the prophets and the angels (upon them prayer and peace), and the heavenly scriptures, and the Last Day; because he (upon him prayer and peace) came confirming all of that. There is no doubt that affirming our master and lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) in his message, according to what his innumerable miracles have indicated, and acknowledging that, necessitates affirming everything he brought (upon him prayer and peace). And among what he brought is what is mentioned here, and likewise other matters that are not limited, such as the resurrection of this very body not a similar one, the trial of the grave and its punishment, the Sirat, the Balance, the Basin, intercession, and other things whose tracking is lengthy, and it is detailed in the Book and the Sunna and the works of the scholars of the Sharia. And from it is deduced: the obligation of truthfulness of the messengers (upon them prayer and peace), and the impossibility of lying upon them, otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers to our Lord, the Knower of hidden things, Glorified and Exalted; and the impossibility of doing all forbidden acts; because they (upon them prayer and peace) were sent to teach creation by their words, their deeds, and their silences, so it necessarily follows that in all of them there should be no opposition to the command of our Lord, Glorified and Exalted, Who chose them over all creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. There is no doubt that the attribution of 'the Messenger' to 'Allah' Most High implies that He, Glorified and Exalted, chose him for the message just as He chose his brother messengers for that. And you have known that His knowledge encompasses what is without end, and that ignorance and what is in its meaning are impossible for Allah Most High. So it necessarily follows that His affirmation of them corresponds to what He knew of them of truthfulness and trustworthiness, so it is impossible that they should be in reality contrary to what He knew of them. And He Most High has commanded following them (upon them prayer and peace) in their words and deeds, so it necessarily follows that all of them should be in accordance with what pleases Him.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a theological deduction from the testimony that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. The author first explains that this testimony implicitly includes belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day, because Prophet Muhammad confirmed all that. Then he argues that affirming his message based on his miracles necessitates affirming everything he brought, including specific eschatological events like resurrection of the very body, grave trial, Sirat, Balance, Basin, intercession, etc. From this, the author deduces two essential properties of messengers: (1) the necessity of truthfulness and impossibility of lying, for otherwise they would not be trustworthy; (2) the impossibility of committing any forbidden act, because they are role models in all their states. The reasoning is that since prophets are sent to teach people, their every action must conform to Allah's command. Furthermore, because Allah's knowledge is infinite and free of ignorance, His choice of a messenger implies that the messenger matches His perfect knowledge of truthfulness and trustworthiness. Therefore, prophets must be truthful and impeccable in all they do. The passage ends by noting that Allah commanded following them, so all their actions must be pleasing to Him.

Key Terms
رسول الله
تصديق
معجزات
البعث
فتنة القبر
الصراط
الميزان
الحوض
الشفاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the shahada only affirms Muhammad's prophethood without entailing other doctrines.
Correction: The passage shows it implies belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, the Last Day, and specific afterlife events.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does the statement 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah' necessarily entail?
A) Only that Muhammad received revelation.
B) Faith in all prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day.
C) That Muhammad's miracles are limited.
D) That prophets may sin in minor matters.

Key Takeaway
The testimony to Muhammad's messengerhood implicitly affirms the entire spectrum of Islamic beliefs, from earlier prophets to the afterlife.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Does your shahada truly commit you to everything the Prophet brought, including the unseen realities of the grave and the hereafter? Or do you mentally separate your declaration from the difficult details of eschatology?
?
If you genuinely believed that your very own body will be resurrected and you will have to cross the Sirat, how would that change the way you live today?
?
The author says affirming Muhammad's message 'necessitates' belief. Is your belief in the resurrection of this exact body, the balance, and intercession a necessary conviction, or just a passive acceptance? What would it cost you to truly internalize it?

Prophethood
intermediate
6 min
Why Prophets Must Be Truthful and Sinless
The author deduces the necessity of prophetic truthfulness and sinlessness.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theological deduction that prophets are necessarily truthful and protected from sin, based on their role and Allah's knowledge.

Core Idea
Prophets cannot lie or sin because they are Allah's trusted messengers.

After establishing what the shahada implies about the content of faith, the author now draws logical conclusions about the prophets themselves. If they are messengers entrusted with revelation, they must be truthful and impeccable in all they do. This passage provides the rational basis for the doctrines of prophetic truthfulness and sinlessness.

Guided Path
1
Read the deduction passage
Read the Arabic text and translation starting from 'And from it is deduced...' Focus on the two properties mentioned.
2
Identify the two deduced properties
The author deduces: (1) obligation of truthfulness and impossibility of lying, (2) impossibility of committing any forbidden act.
These are called 'wujub sidq al-rusul' and 'istihalah fi'l al-munhiyat'.
3
Understand the reasoning
Prophets are teachers by word, deed, and silence, so they cannot contradict Allah's command. Also Allah's perfect knowledge means He would not choose someone contrary to His knowledge; thus they must be truthful and sinless.
The reasoning also includes that Allah commanded following them, so their actions must please Him.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا قَوْلُنَا : ( مُحَمَّدٌ رَسُولُ اللهِ ( صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ : فَيَدْخُلُ فِيهِ الإِيمَانُ بِسَائِرِ الأَنْبِيَاءِ وَالْمَلَائِكَةِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلَاةُ وَالسَّلامُ ، وَالْكُتُبِ السَّمَاوِيَّةِ ، وَالْيَوْمِ الآخِرِ ؛ لِأَنَّهُ عَلَيْهِ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ جَاءَ بِتَصْدِيقِ جَمِيعِ ذَلِكَ . لا شك أنَّ تصديق سيّدِنا ومولانا محمد صلَّى اللهُ عليهِ وسلَّمَ في رسالتِهِ بحَسَبِ ما دلّتْ عليهِ معجزاتُهُ التي لا حصر لها ، والإقرار بذلك .. يستلزم التصديق بكل ما جاءَ بهِ عليه الصلاة والسلام . ومن جملة ما أتى بهِ ماذكر هنا، وكذا غير ذلكَ ممَّا لا ينحصر ؛ كالبعث لعين هذا البدنِ لا لمثلِهِ ، وفتنة القبر وعذابه ، والصراطِ ، والميزان ، والحوض ، والشفاعة ، وغير ذلك مما يطولُ تتبعه ، وهو مفصل في الكتاب والسنة وتأليف علماء الشريعة . وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ : وُجُوبُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ ، وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الْكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِمْ ، وَإِلا لَمْ يَكُونُوا رُسُلاً أمَنَاءَ لِمَوْلانَا الْعَالِم بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ ، وَاسْتِحَالَةُ فِعْل الْمَنْهَيَّاتِ كُلِّهَا ؛ لِأَنَّهُمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ أُرْسِلُوا لِيُعَلِّمُوا الْخَلْقَ بِأَفْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَسُكُوتِهِمْ ، فَيَلْزَمُ أَلَا يَكُونَ فِي جَمِيعِهَا مُخَالَفَةٌ لِأَمْرِ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي اخْتَارَهُمْ عَلَى جَمِيعِ الْخَلْقِ ، وَأَمِنَهُمْ عَلَى سِرِّ وَحْيِهِ . لا شكّ أنَّ إضافة ( الرسولِ ) إلى ( الله ) تعالى تقتضي أنَّهُ جَلَّ وعزَّ اختارَهُ للرسالة كما اختار إخوانَهُ المرسلين لذلكَ ، وقد علمتَ أنَّ علمه تعالى محيط بما لا نهاية له ، وأنَّ الجهل وما في معناه مستحيل على الله تعالى ، فلزمَ أنَّ تصديقَهُ تعالى لهم مطابق لما علمهُ تعالى منهم مِنَ الصدق والأمانة ، فيستحيلُ أنْ يكونوا في نفس الأمر على خلافِ ما علمَهُ تعالى منهم ، وقد أمر تعالى بالاقتداء بهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام في أقوالهم وأفعالهم ، فيلزم أن يكون جميعها على ما يُرضيه تعالى .
And as for our saying: 'Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah (may Allah bless him and grant him peace)', there enters into it faith in all the prophets and the angels (upon them prayer and peace), and the heavenly scriptures, and the Last Day; because he (upon him prayer and peace) came confirming all of that. There is no doubt that affirming our master and lord Muhammad (may Allah bless him and grant him peace) in his message, according to what his innumerable miracles have indicated, and acknowledging that, necessitates affirming everything he brought (upon him prayer and peace). And among what he brought is what is mentioned here, and likewise other matters that are not limited, such as the resurrection of this very body not a similar one, the trial of the grave and its punishment, the Sirat, the Balance, the Basin, intercession, and other things whose tracking is lengthy, and it is detailed in the Book and the Sunna and the works of the scholars of the Sharia. And from it is deduced: the obligation of truthfulness of the messengers (upon them prayer and peace), and the impossibility of lying upon them, otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers to our Lord, the Knower of hidden things, Glorified and Exalted; and the impossibility of doing all forbidden acts; because they (upon them prayer and peace) were sent to teach creation by their words, their deeds, and their silences, so it necessarily follows that in all of them there should be no opposition to the command of our Lord, Glorified and Exalted, Who chose them over all creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation. There is no doubt that the attribution of 'the Messenger' to 'Allah' Most High implies that He, Glorified and Exalted, chose him for the message just as He chose his brother messengers for that. And you have known that His knowledge encompasses what is without end, and that ignorance and what is in its meaning are impossible for Allah Most High. So it necessarily follows that His affirmation of them corresponds to what He knew of them of truthfulness and trustworthiness, so it is impossible that they should be in reality contrary to what He knew of them. And He Most High has commanded following them (upon them prayer and peace) in their words and deeds, so it necessarily follows that all of them should be in accordance with what pleases Him.
Source pages p. 293

Commentary
This passage is a theological deduction from the testimony that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. The author first explains that this testimony implicitly includes belief in all prophets, angels, scriptures, and the Last Day, because Prophet Muhammad confirmed all that. Then he argues that affirming his message based on his miracles necessitates affirming everything he brought, including specific eschatological events like resurrection of the very body, grave trial, Sirat, Balance, Basin, intercession, etc. From this, the author deduces two essential properties of messengers: (1) the necessity of truthfulness and impossibility of lying, for otherwise they would not be trustworthy; (2) the impossibility of committing any forbidden act, because they are role models in all their states. The reasoning is that since prophets are sent to teach people, their every action must conform to Allah's command. Furthermore, because Allah's knowledge is infinite and free of ignorance, His choice of a messenger implies that the messenger matches His perfect knowledge of truthfulness and trustworthiness. Therefore, prophets must be truthful and impeccable in all they do. The passage ends by noting that Allah commanded following them, so all their actions must be pleasing to Him.

Key Terms
وجوب صدق الرسل
استحالة الكذب
استحالة فعل المنهيات
الأمانة
العلم المحيط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think prophets could sin in minor matters.
Correction: The passage states the impossibility of doing all forbidden acts (istihalah fi'l al-munhiyat kulliha), meaning they are protected from all sins.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which two properties are necessarily true of messengers?
A) They are wealthy and powerful.
B) They are truthful and sinless.
C) They are human and mortal.
D) They are infallible only in major matters.

Key Takeaway
Prophets are necessarily truthful and sinless because they are Allah's chosen messengers and teachers, and His perfect knowledge guarantees their integrity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you hear stories about prophets that seem to imply imperfection, do you automatically assume the interpretation must be wrong because of what this lesson proves? How can you train yourself to immediately refer to the principle of ‘ismah (sinlessness) rather than doubt?
?
The prophets taught by every action and silence. If your life were examined today, what would your words, deeds, and silences teach others about Islam? Which specific habit or silence needs to change to become a better teacher by example?
?
Allah chose the prophets based on His perfect knowledge of their inner truthfulness. Do you trust that Allah's choices of scholars, imams, or those in authority over you are also based on His knowledge, even when you see flaws? What does that trust require from you in terms of obedience and respect?

Prophethood

The Obligation of Truthfulness for Prophets
Sanusi derives prophetic truthfulness and sinlessness from the testimony of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why prophets must be truthful and sinless as derived from the testimony of faith.

Core Idea
Prophets must be truthful and sinless to be trustworthy messengers.

In this lesson, Sanusi begins with a direct derivation from the shahada, establishing that prophets cannot lie or commit sins. He argues that if they could, they would not be trusted by God, who knows all hidden things. This sets the foundation for the doctrine of prophetic infallibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the derivation passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp Sanusi's initial point.
Notice the concise style.
2
Identify the two attributes
Notice that Sanusi first states the obligation of truthfulness, then the impossibility of lying and sin.
3
Understand the reasoning
Reflect on why these attributes are necessary: without them, prophets would not be trustworthy messengers.
Consider the role of prophets as teachers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَيُؤْخَذُ مِنْهُ : وُجُوبُ صِدْقِ الرُّسُلِ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ ، وَاسْتِحَالَةُ الْكَذِبِ عَلَيْهِمْ ، وَإِلا لَمْ يَكُونُوا رُسُلاً أمَنَاءَ لِمَوْلانَا الْعَالِم بِالْخَفِيَّاتِ جَلَّ وَعَزَّ ، وَاسْتِحَالَةُ فِعْل الْمَنْهَيَّاتِ كُلِّهَا ؛ لِأَنَّهُمْ عَلَيْهِمُ الصَّلاةُ وَالسَّلامُ أُرْسِلُوا لِيُعَلِّمُوا الْخَلْقَ بِأَفْوَالِهِمْ وَأَفْعَالِهِمْ وَسُكُوتِهِمْ ، فَيَلْزَمُ أَلَا يَكُونَ فِي جَمِيعِهَا مُخَالَفَةٌ لِأَمْرِ مَوْلَانَا جَلَّ وَعَزَّ الَّذِي اخْتَارَهُمْ عَلَى جَمِيعِ الْخَلْقِ ، وَأَمِنَهُمْ عَلَى سِرِّ وَحْيِهِ(۱) لا شكّ أنَّ إضافة ( الرسولِ ) إلى ( الله ) تعالى تقتضي أنَّهُ جَلَّ وعزَّ اختارَهُ للرسالة كما اختار إخوانَهُ المرسلين لذلكَ ، وقد علمتَ أنَّ علمه تعالى محيط بما لا نهاية له ، وأنَّ الجهل وما في معناه مستحيل على الله تعالى ، فلزمَ أنَّ تصديقَهُ تعالى لهم مطابق لما علمهُ تعالى منهم مِنَ الصدق والأمانة ، فيستحيلُ أنْ يكونوا في نفس الأمر على خلافِ ما علمَهُ تعالى منهم ، وقد أمر تعالى بالاقتداء بهم عليهم الصلاة والسلام في أقوالهم وأفعالهم (۲) ، فيلزم أن يكون جميعها على وفق ما يرضاه مولانا جلَّ وعزَّ ، وهو المطلوب
And from it is taken: the obligation of truthfulness of the messengers, peace be upon them, and the impossibility of lying upon them, and otherwise they would not be trustworthy messengers to our Lord, the Knower of hidden things, the Mighty and Sublime. And the impossibility of performing all forbidden actions; because they, peace be upon them, were sent to teach the creation by their words, actions, and silences, so it is necessary that in all of them there be no violation of the command of our Lord, the Mighty and Sublime, who chose them over all of creation and entrusted them with the secret of His revelation(1). There is no doubt that the attribution of 'the messenger' to 'God' Almighty necessitates that He, Mighty and Sublime, chose him for the message just as He chose his brother messengers for that. And you have known that His knowledge, praise be to Him, encompasses what has no end, and that ignorance and what is in its meaning is impossible for God. So it follows that His confirmation of them corresponds to what He knew of them of truthfulness and trustworthiness, so it is impossible that they be in reality contrary to what He knew of them. And He commanded following them, peace be upon them, in their words and actions(2), so it is necessary that all of them be in accordance with what pleases our Lord, Mighty and Sublime. And that is what is sought.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage is a derivation (istinbat) from the testimony of faith. It begins by deducing the necessary attributes of prophets: they must be truthful, lying is impossible for them, and they cannot commit any forbidden act. The reason given is that if they could lie or sin, they would not be trustworthy messengers from God, Who knows all hidden things. Moreover, they were sent to teach humanity by their words, actions, and even their silences; therefore, none of these can contradict God's commands. The author then provides a deeper rational proof: since God chose them for the message and His knowledge encompasses all, and ignorance is impossible for God, His confirmation of them (i.e., calling them messengers) must correspond to their actual state of truthfulness and trustworthiness. Thus, it is impossible for them to be other than what God knows them to be. Additionally, God commands us to follow them, so their actions must be in full accord with His pleasure.

Key Terms
وجوب
صدق
استحالة
كذب
أمانة
رسالة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets are infallible because they are inherently perfect humans.
Correction: Their infallibility is a necessary consequence of their role as messengers and God's trust, not an inherent human trait.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what would be the consequence if prophets could lie?
A) They would still be respected.
B) They would not be trustworthy messengers.
C) They would be forgiven.
D) It would not matter.

Key Takeaway
Prophets must be truthful and sinless because they are God's trusted messengers and examples for humanity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If the prophets had to be truthful in every word, how do you justify your own 'small' lies or exaggerations? Will you commit to truthfulness even when it costs you something today?
?
The prophets taught by their actions as well as their words. In what area of your life do your actions not match your faith? What is one concrete change you will make this week to align your behavior with your beliefs?
?
God chose the prophets over all creation and entrusted them with His secret revelation. Do you treat the revelation you have (the Quran) with that same reverence, or do you take it lightly? What will you do to honour the Word of God in your daily life?
